Recommended Practices in the Eid Khutbah
Lists sunan for the Eid khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended practices (sunan) for the Eid khutbah and distinguish them from obligatory elements.

Core Idea
The Eid khutbah's takbir is sunnah, not fixed; the congregation listens silently.

The khutbah for Eid is a distinct act of worship with specific sunan. This passage from Maraqi al-Falah outlines what the khateeb should mention, how he should sit, and how the takbir should be performed. Understanding these sunan helps one appreciate the beauty of worship while avoiding innovation.

Guided Path
1
Extract the prescribed actions
List all actions and statements the text instructs for the khateeb: reminding about sadaqat al-fitr, sitting between khutbahs, saying takbir, beginning with takbir, etc.
Look for imperative verbs or phrases like 'يذكر', 'ويجلس', 'يكبر', 'يبدأ'.
2
Identify the legal category of each action
Determine if each action is described as wajib (obligatory), sunnah (recommended), or mustahabb. Key indicators: 'يستحب' (recommended), 'لا ينبغي' (should not), and explicit statements like 'هو السنة'.
The text uses 'يستحب' for the nine and seven takbirs, indicating sunnah.
3
Recognize the scope of authority
Note that the takbir count is not fixed in Zahir al-Riwayah, but a recommendation from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud is cited. Understand that later scholars like Qadikhan distinguish between Eids.
This shows that practice may vary; the mufta bihi is the described recommendation.
4
Apply the rulings to the congregation
What should the congregation do? They say takbir and send blessings on the Prophet silently, while listening attentively (sunnat al-inṣāt).
The text says 'يكبر القوم ويصلون على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في أنفسهم'.
5
Distinguish from Jumu'ah
The khateeb begins Jumu'ah with tahmid (praise of Allah), but begins the Eid khutbah with takbir. This is a key difference.
The text states: 'ويبدأ الخطيب بالتحميد في الجمعة وغيرها، ويبدأ بالتكبير في خطبة العيدين'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيذكر من تجب عليه ولمن تجب ومم تجب ومقدار الواجب ووقت الوجوب، ويجلس بين الخطبتين جلسة خفيفة، ويكبر في خطبة العيدين وليس لذلك عدد في ظاهر الرواية لكن لا ينبغي أن يجعل أكثر الخطبة التكبير ويكبر في خطبة عيد الأضحى أكثر مما يكبر في خطبة الفطر كذا في قاضيخان ويبدأ الخطيب بالتحميد في الجمعة وغيرها، ويبدأ بالتكبير في خطبة العيدين ويستحب أن يستفتح الأولى بتسع تترى والثانية بسبع قال عبد الله هو السنة ويكبر القوم ويصلون على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في أنفسهم امتثالاً للأمر وسنة الإنصات
He mentions for whom it is obligatory and to whom it is due and from what it is due and the amount of the obligation and the time of obligation, and he sits between the two khutbahs a light sitting, and he says takbir in the khutbah of the two Eids and there is no specific number for that in Zahir al-Riwayah but it is not appropriate to make most of the khutbah takbir, and he says more takbir in the khutbah of Eid al-Adha than in the khutbah of Eid al-Fitr, as in Qadikhan. The khateeb begins with tahmid on Friday and other than it, and begins with takbir in the khutbah of the two Eids. It is recommended to open the first with nine consecutive and the second with seven. Abdullah said: That is the Sunnah. The people say takbir and send blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) silently, obeying the command and the Sunnah of listening attentively.
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage, likely from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah, lists the recommended content and actions of the Eid khutbah. The khateeb is instructed to remind the congregation about the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr: who must pay it, to whom it is given, from what wealth, the amount (half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates/barley/raisins), and the time (dawn of Eid day). He should sit briefly between the two khutbahs. The takbir during the khutbah has no fixed number in the authoritative sources, but the majority of the khutbah should not be takbir; more takbir is said on Eid al-Adha than on Eid al-Fitr. The khateeb begins the Jumu'ah khutbah with tahmid (praise of Allah), but on Eids he begins with takbir. It is recommended to start the first khutbah with nine takbirs and the second with seven, as narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). The congregation is to say takbir and send blessings on the Prophet silently, as this complies with the command to attend attentively.

Key Terms
تترى (tatrā): Consecutive numbers of takbir (nine in the first khutbah, seven in the second).
سنة الإنصات (sunnat al-inṣāt): The Sunnah of listening attentively to the khutbah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
With what does the khateeb begin the Eid khutbah according to this passage?
A) Tahmid
B) Takbir
C) Recitation of a surah
D) Supplication

Key Takeaway
The Eid khutbah has recommended practices (sunan) including mentioning sadaqat al-fitr, sitting lightly between khutbahs, and performing takbir without a fixed number, though nine and seven are recommended.

Ruling on Missing the Eid Prayer
States that one who misses the Eid prayer does not make it up but may pray four rak'ahs optionally

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for someone who misses the Eid prayer with the imam and explain the recommended substitute.

Core Idea
The missed Eid prayer is not made up; instead, four rak'ahs of Duha are recommended.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses a common scenario: missing the Eid prayer with the congregation. The Hanafi school distinguishes between obligatory and supererogatory acts, and here it provides a clear substitute that aligns with the voluntary Duha prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of missing the Eid prayer with the imam. What is the ruling? No qada' (makeup) is required.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? A narration from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) prescribing four rak'ahs with specific surahs.
The hadith is ahad (single narration), providing zanni (speculative) evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this narration prove the ruling? The explicit statement of a Sahabi indicates the practice is recommended, not obligatory. The promise of reward confirms desirability.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Do other schools agree? Shafi'is and Hanbalis consider Eid prayer sunnah, so also no qada', but do not prescribe a specific substitute.
The practical difference is the recommendation of four rak'ahs in the Hanafi school.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is mufta bihi? The relied-upon Hanafi position is that no qada' is required; the optional four rak'ahs are preferred but not obligatory.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is well established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ومن فاتته الصلاة فلم يدركها (مع الإمام لا يقضيها ) لأنها لم تعرف قربة إلا بشرائط لا تتم بدون الإمام أي السلطان أو مأموره فإن شاء انصرف وإن شاء صلى نفلاً والأفضل أربع فيكون له صلاة الضحى لما روي عن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه أنه قال: من فاتته صلاة العيد صلى أربع ركعات يقرأ في الأولى بسبح اسم ربك الأعلى وفي الثانية والشمس وضحاها وفي الثالثة والليل إذا يغشى وفي الرابعة والضحى وروي في ذلك النبي وعداً جميلاً وتواباً جزيلاً
(And whoever misses the prayer and does not catch it (with the imam), he does not make it up) because it is not known as an act of worship except with conditions that are not completed without the imam, meaning the ruler or his deputy. If he wishes, he may leave, and if he wishes, he may pray supererogatory prayer, and the best is four, so it becomes for him the Duha prayer. Based on what was narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: Whoever misses the Eid prayer should pray four rak'ahs, reciting in the first Surah al-A'la, in the second Surah al-Shams, in the third Surah al-Layl, and in the fourth Surah al-Duha. And it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) promised a beautiful reward and abundant recompense.)
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi ruling for someone who misses the Eid prayer with the congregation. Since the Eid prayer is not individually obligatory (fard 'ayn) but rather a wajib that requires the imam, if one misses it, he does not make it up as a qada' prayer. Instead, he may either leave or pray a voluntary prayer of four rak'ahs, which will count as the Duha prayer. The preferred time for this is the Duha time. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) who prescribed this practice with specific surahs: in each rak'ah, after al-Fatiha, recite al-A'la, al-Shams, al-Layl, and al-Duha respectively. The hadith promises a great reward. Note that this is a recommended substitute, not an obligatory makeup.

Key Terms
صلاة الضحى (ṣalāt al-ḍuḥā): The voluntary forenoon prayer; in this context, four rak'ahs prayed in place of the missed Eid prayer.
لا يقضيها (lā yaqḍīhā): He does not make it up as a qada' (compensatory) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the Hanafi school recommend for someone who misses the Eid prayer with the imam?
A) Make it up as qada' after the imam finishes
B) Pray four rak'ahs as Duha prayer
C) Pray two rak'ahs as a makeup
D) Nothing; it is lost

Key Takeaway
The missed Eid prayer is not made up; the recommended substitute is four rak'ahs of Duha.

Delaying Eid Prayer and Eating Before Adha
Two sub-rulings with dalil from Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for delaying Eid prayer to the next day and explain the preferred ruling on eating before the Adha prayer.

Core Idea
Eid prayer delayed only one day with excuse; eating before Adha prayer is not disliked.

Eid prayers have specific rulings that differ from daily prayers. One such rule is that if a valid excuse prevents knowing the correct day, the prayer may be offered the next day—but not later. For Eid al-Adha, a unique sunnah is to delay eating until after the prayer, yet eating beforehand is not considered disliked in the preferred view. This lesson unpacks these two rulings, their proofs, and the underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage covers (a) delaying Eid prayer due to an excuse and (b) eating before Eid al-Adha prayer. Recognize that each has a default rule and an exception.
2
Analyze the delay of Eid prayer
Note the default: Eid prayer is not made up if missed (like Jumu'ah). The exception: it may be prayed on the next day only, provided a valid excuse existed. The excuse is a condition for validity, not mere dislike.
The proof is the Prophet's action of delaying once when the moon was hidden.
3
Analyze the ruling on eating before Adha prayer
The sunnah is to delay eating until after prayer. However, if one eats beforehand, it is not makruh according to the preferred view (mukhtar). Some earlier views considered it disliked, but the later tarjih settled on non-dislike.
The Prophet's practice is the proof: he would not eat until after returning from prayer.
4
Understand the Duha prayer discussion
The text addresses an objection: if Eid prayer substitutes for Duha, then after Eid, one should not pray Duha. But the response clarifies that substitution does not prevent offering Duha separately.
This is a peripheral point; the core is the ruling on eating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتؤخر ) صلاة عيد الفرط (بعذر) كان غم الهلال وشهدوا بعد الزوال أو صلوها في غيم فظهر أنها كانت بعد الزوال فتؤخر (إلى الغد فقط) لأن الأصل فيها أن لا تقضي كالجمعة إلا أنا تركناه بما روينا من أنه عليه السلام أخرها إلى الغد بعذر ولم يرو أنه أخرها إلى ما بعده فبقي على الأصل وقيد العذر للجواز لا لنفي الكراهة، فإذا لم يكن عذر لا تصح في الغد (وأحكام ) عيد الأضحى كالفطر) وقد علمتها لكنه في الأضحى يؤخر الأكل عن الصلاة استحباباً فإن قدمه لا يكره في المختار لأنه عليه السلام : كان لا يطعم في يوم الأضحى حتى يرجع فيأكل من أضحيته، فلذا قيل: لا يستحب إلى الظهر أجيب بأنا إن سلمنا ذلك لا يضرنا لكن صلاة الضحى غير واجبة فيتخير بخلاف الظهر في الجمعة فإنه فرض فيلزم أداؤه اهـ، ويلزم على ما ذكره أنه لا يأتي بالضحى إذا صلى العيد لعدم الجمع بين العوض والمعوض وليس كذلك
And the Eid prayer is delayed (due to an excuse) such as the moon being hidden and they testify after noon, or they prayed in cloudiness and then it became apparent that it was after noon, so it is delayed (only to the next day) because the original principle is that it is not made up like Jumu'ah, except that we abandoned that due to what we narrated that he (peace be upon him) delayed it to the next day due to an excuse, and it is not narrated that he delayed it beyond that, so the original remains. And the excuse is conditioned for permissibility, not for negation of dislike; if there is no excuse, it is not valid on the next day. (And the rulings of Eid al-Adha are like al-Fitr) and you have known them, but on Adha he delays eating until after the prayer as a recommendation; if he eats beforehand, it is not disliked in the preferred view, because he (peace be upon him) would not eat on the day of Adha until he returned and ate from his sacrifice. Therefore it is said: it is not recommended until noon. It was answered: If we accept that, it does not harm us, but Duha prayer is not obligatory so one has a choice, unlike Zuhr on Friday which is obligatory so its performance is necessary. End. And based on what he mentioned, he would not perform Duha if he prayed Eid, due to the lack of combining the substitute and the original, but that is not the case.
Source pages p. 536

Commentary
This passage covers two sub-topics: (1) Delaying the Eid prayer due to an excuse, and (2) Specifics of Eid al-Adha regarding eating. On delay: The original principle is that Eid prayer, like Jumu'ah, is not made up if missed. However, based on the Prophet's action of delaying the Eid prayer to the next day when the moon was hidden, it is permissible to delay only one day when there is an excuse such as cloudiness or late testimony. The excuse is a condition for validity of the delay, not merely to remove dislike; without an excuse, praying on the next day is invalid. On eating: For Eid al-Adha, it is recommended to delay eating until after the prayer, following the Prophet's practice of eating from his sacrifice after returning. However, if one eats before, it is not disliked (makruh) according to the preferred view, though some disliked it. The text addresses an objection: some argued that delaying eating until noon is not recommended, but the response is that Duha prayer is voluntary, unlike Zuhr on Friday which is obligatory, so the situation differs. Also, the criticism that one would not pray Duha if he prayed Eid (since Duha is substituted by Eid) is rejected; the substitution does not prevent offering Duha separately.

Key Terms
العذر (al-ʿudhr): An excuse such as hidden moon, late testimony, or cloudiness that makes the correct day uncertain.
المختار (al-mukhtār): The preferred (chosen) opinion in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer?
A) It is haram
B) It is not disliked in the preferred view
C) It invalidates the prayer
D) It is wajib to eat before

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer delay requires a valid excuse and is limited to one day; eating before Adha prayer is not disliked, though delay is recommended.

Making Up Missed Eid Prayer with Four Rak'ahs
Ruling on qada of Eid prayer with specific surahs and hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada of missed Eid prayer, identify the specific surahs to recite, and explain the hadith proof from Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
Missed Eid prayer is made up as four rak'ahs with specific surahs, based on a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud.

The Eid prayer is a highly emphasized sunnah, but what if one misses the congregational prayer? The Hanafi school provides a specific make-up prayer consisting of four rak'ahs with prescribed recitations. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its category
The act is qada of Eid prayer. In Hanafi fiqh, this is a sunnah prayer (sunnah ghayr muakkadah).
2
State the ruling from the text
The person prays four rak'ahs with specific surahs in each rak'ah.
First rak'ah: Surah al-A'la; second: al-Shams; third: al-Layl; fourth: al-Duha.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The text refers to a report from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) promising great reward.
The phrase 'ruwiya' indicates a transmitted report.
4
Analyse the thubut and dalala of the dalil
This is a zanni (speculative) proof, hence the ruling is sunnah, not wajib.
Ahad hadith in Hanafi usul are acted upon for fada'il but do not create obligation.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools do not recommend qada of Eid; the Hanafi school recommends it based on this report.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf respecting different methodological principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن فاتته صلاة العيد صلى أربع ركعات يقرأ في الأولى بسبح اسم ربك الأعلى وفي الثانية والشمس وضحاها وفي الثالثة والليل إذا يغشى وفي الرابعة والضحى وروي في ذلك النبي وعداً جميلاً وتواباً جزيلاً) اهـ قوله (وروى في ذلك) بصيغة الفاعل، وضميره لابن مسعود. قوله: (وتواباً جزيلاً) في القهستاني عن المسعودية يعطي ثواباً بعدد كل ما نبت في هذه السنة .اهـ.
From whoever misses the Eid prayer, he prays four rak'ahs, reciting in the first (after Fatiha) 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la', in the second 'Wa al-shamsi wa duhaha', in the third 'Wa al-layli idha yaghsha', in the fourth 'Wa al-duha'. And it was reported in that (hadith) from the Prophet a beautiful promise and abundant reward. End. His statement: 'and it was reported' (by the active participle) and its pronoun refers to Ibn Mas'ud. His statement: 'and abundant reward' – in al-Qahastani from al-Mas'udiyyah: He gives reward equal to the number of everything that grew in this year. End.
Source pages p. 536

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the qada (make-up) of the missed Eid prayer, presented by the author of Maraqi al-Falah with its supporting hadith. The ruling states that a person who misses the Eid prayer (either Eid al-Fitr or Eid al-Adha) should pray four rak'ahs, and the specific surahs to be recited after Surah al-Fatiha in each rak'ah are given: in the first rak'ah Surah al-A'la, in the second Surah al-Shams, in the third Surah al-Layl, and in the fourth Surah al-Duha. This is the Hanafi position. The commentator, Imam al-Tahtawi, then explains that the wording 'ruwiya' (it was reported) in the matn refers to Ibn Mas'ud, meaning the hadith is from him. He further clarifies from al-Qahastani that the reward mentioned is enormous: for every plant that grew in that year, the one who performs this prayer receives a reward. This emphasizes the merit of this qada prayer.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Compensatory prayer performed after the prescribed time has passed.
سبح اسم ربك الأعلى (Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la): Surah al-A'la (87) recited in the first rak'ah of the qada prayer.
والشمس وضحاها (Wa al-shamsi wa duhaha): Surah al-Shams (91) recited in the second rak'ah.
والليل إذا يغشى (Wa al-layli idha yaghsha): Surah al-Layl (92) recited in the third rak'ah.
والضحى (Wa al-duha): Surah al-Duha (93) recited in the fourth rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many rak'ahs does one pray when making up a missed Eid prayer?
A) Two rak'ahs
B) Four rak'ahs
C) Six rak'ahs
D) Eight rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends a four-rak'ah qada for missed Eid prayer with specific surahs, based on a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud.

Delaying Eid Prayer for Remote People Due to Excuse
Ruling on delaying Eid prayer for outlying residents to the next day when an obstacle occurs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying the Eid prayer for farqt (remote people) due to an excuse, explain its proof, and distinguish between the qada and ada views within the school.

Core Idea
Eid prayer for remote people may be delayed one day only if a valid excuse occurs; without excuse, it is invalid.

This passage addresses a specific situation: when people living outside the city (farqt) miss the Eid prayer due to an excuse like cloudiness or late testimony. The Hanafi school permits them to pray the following day, based on a Prophetic precedent. However, this is a limited exception to the general rule that Eid prayer is not made up. We will explore the conditions, the proof, and an internal scholarly debate on whether the delayed prayer is considered qada or ada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is delaying the Eid prayer for farqt. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) to delay to the next day only when a valid excuse exists.
The general rule for city dwellers is that Eid prayer must be performed on time and is not made up.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a reported action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) delaying the Eid prayer to the next day due to an excuse. This is a sunnah ahad hadith.
The dalil is cited as 'بما روينا من أنه عليه السلام أخرها إلى الغد بعذر'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action shows permissibility for delay, but the fact that he did not delay beyond one day indicates that the exception is limited to one day. The original principle (al-asl) is that Eid prayer is not made up, like Jumu'ah.
Thus, the exception does not extend beyond the reported limit.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, there is a difference on whether the delayed prayer is qada (make-up) or ada (performance in its proper time). The text records two opinions.
Al-Qahastani reports the two views; al-Sayyid indicates the preferred view is qada.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the prayer is qada, as supported by al-Hidayah, al-Kirmani, and others. This aligns with the principle that the time for Eid is only the first day.
The tarjih authority is al-Sayyid and al-Qahastani, citing the majority of scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( وتؤخر ) صلاة عيد الفرط (بعذر) كان غم الهلال وشهدوا بعد الزوال أو صلوها في غيم فظهر أنها كانت بعد الزوال فتؤخر (إلى الغد فقط) لأن الأصل فيها أن لا تقضي كالجمعة إلا أنا تركناه بما روينا من أنه عليه السلام أخرها إلى الغد بعذر ولم يرو أنه أخرها إلى ما بعده فبقي على الأصل وقيد العذر للجواز لا لنفي الكراهة، فإذا لم يكن عذر لا تصح في الغد قوله : ( كان غم الهلال الخ) وكالمطر ونحوه كما في السراج، وكما لو صلى بالناس على غير طهارة، ولم يعلم إلا بعد الزوال كما في الخانية. قوله: (وشهدوا بعد الزوال أو قبله بحيث لا يمكن إجتماع الناس برهان قال السيد: وفي كونها قضاء أو أداء قولان حكاهما القهستاني ونصه أي يقضي صلاته كما أشار إليه الكرماني والجلابي والهداية، وغيرها أو يؤدي كما في التحفة .اهـ. قوله : (إلى الغد) ووقتها من الثاني كالأول أفاده السيد .
And the Eid prayer of the farqt (the people of outlying areas) is delayed due to an excuse, such as the new moon being obscured, and they testified after noon, or they prayed under cloudiness and it became apparent that it was after noon, so it is delayed to the following day only, because the original principle is that it is not made up like Jumu'ah, except that we abandoned that due to what we narrated that he (peace be upon him) delayed it to the next day due to an excuse, and it was not reported that he delayed it beyond that, so it remains on the original principle. And the specification of 'excuse' is for permissibility, not for negating dislike. So if there is no excuse, it is not valid on the next day. His statement: 'such as the new moon being obscured etc.' includes rain and the like, as in al-Siraj, and also if he led the people in prayer without purification and it was not known except after noon, as in al-Khaniyya. His statement: 'and they testified after noon or before it in a way that the gathering of people is not possible...' al-Sayyid said: regarding whether it is qada or ada, there are two opinions as narrated by al-Qahastani, and its text: 'he makes up his prayer as indicated by al-Kirmani, al-Jullabi, al-Hidayah, and others, or he performs it (as ada) as in al-Tuhfa.' His statement: 'to the next day' – its time from the second is like the first, as stated by al-Sayyid.
Source pages p. 536

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of the farqt (people living in remote areas) who may miss the Eid prayer on its proper day due to a legitimate excuse. The ruling distinguishes between the people of the city (who should not delay) and the farqt. The excuse is like the new moon being obscured so that the exact day of Eid is unknown until witnesses testify after noon, or if they prayed under cloud cover and later discovered the actual time was after noon. In such cases, the Eid prayer is delayed to the following day only, not beyond. The reason is that the original principle (al-asl) for Eid prayer is that it is not made up if missed, similar to Jumu'ah. However, due to the prophetic practice of delaying once, we depart from that principle, but only to the extent of one day. Therefore, it is not permissible to delay beyond one day without an excuse. The excuse is a condition for the validity of the delay; without excuse, praying on the next day is invalid. The commentator then clarifies what constitutes an excuse: obscured moon, rain, etc., and also if the imam prayed without wudu and it was discovered after noon. He notes a difference of opinion regarding whether this delayed prayer is considered qada (make-up) or ada (performance in its proper time), quoting al-Qahastani that the reliable view is that it is qada, as supported by many authorities, though some consider it ada.

Key Terms
الفرط (al-farqt): The people of outlying areas or suburbs who are not counted as city dwellers for the purpose of Eid prayer.
غم الهلال (ghumm al-hilal): The new moon being obscured by clouds, making sighting difficult.
قضاء (qada'): A compensatory performance of a prayer after its prescribed time has elapsed.
أداء (ada'): Performing a prayer within its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For whom is it permissible to delay the Eid prayer to the following day due to an excuse, according to this passage?
A) All Muslims
B) Only the imam
C) The farqt (remote people)
D) Only those who missed the prayer without excuse

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer for remote people (farqt) may be delayed one day only due to an excuse; the delayed prayer is qada (make-up) according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Eid al-Adha Rulings: Eating, Takbir, Udhiyah, and Takbir al-Tashriq
Summary of Hanafi Eid al-Adha rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying eating on Eid al-Adha, identify the conditions of udhiyah, and define Takbir al-Tashriq.

Core Idea
Eid al-Adha rulings mirror Eid al-Fitr except for recommended delay in eating and wajib status of sacrifice.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah brings together the key fiqh of Eid al-Adha. You'll learn the etiquette of eating on this day, the takbir on the way to prayer, the rules of sacrifice (udhiyah), and the meaning of Takbir al-Tashriq. Each element builds on the Prophet's practice and Hanafi juristic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the unique ruling on eating for Eid al-Adha
Note that on Eid al-Adha, delaying eating until after the prayer is recommended (mustahabb), unlike Eid al-Fitr where eating before prayer is recommended. Understand the hadith basis and the Hanafi distinction between city and village dwellers.
The phrase 'yaukkhiru al-akl 'an al-salat istihbaban' is key.
2
Understand the takbir on the way to the prayer
The takbir is recited aloud from home to the prayer place. It stops when reaching the prayer ground or when the imam starts. It is also recited when meeting groups or ascending heights. This takbir is specific to Eid al-Adha and not prescribed on other days except in fear situations.
The practice differs from Eid al-Fitr.
3
Learn who must perform udhiyah and from which animals
Udhiyah is wajib on every free, sane, Muslim who owns the nisab (minimum wealth). It must be from camels, cattle, or sheep. The animal must be thani (specific age) for each type; jadha' (six-month-old sheep) is acceptable.
Hanafi school: wajib for those who can afford; not merely sunnah.
4
Apply the conditions of time, slaughterer, and distribution
The slaughter time is the day of Eid and two days after. The owner should slaughter if able, or appoint another and witness it. The meat is divided into three parts: eat, gift, store; if dependents exist, they take priority.
This distribution follows the Prophet's guidance.
5
Define Takbir al-Tashriq and its linguistic basis
Takbir al-Tashriq is the takbir recited after fard prayers during the days of tashriq (11th-13th Dhul Hijjah). The term 'tashriq' originally refers to drying meat, but here it refers to raising the voice in takbir. The grammatical construction can be interpreted as 'takbir of the days of tashriq' or 'the takbir that is tashriq'.
The Hanafi ruling on when to recite it is from Fajr of 9th to Asr of 13th.

قوله : (وأحكام عيد الأضحى كالفطر) وقد علمتها لكنه في الأضحى يؤخر الأكل عن الصلاة استحباباً فإن قدمه لا يكره في المختار لأنه عليه السلام : كان لا يطعم في يوم الأضحى حتى يرجع فيأكل من أضحيته، فلذا قيل: كما في تقسيم المأمور به من الكشف قهستاني. قوله: (فإن قدمه لا يكره في المختار) قال الحموي : المنفي كراهة التحريم إذ لا بد من الكراهة بترك السنة، وأدنى مراتبها التنزيه اهـ. قوله : (كان لا يطعم) بفتح الياء أي لا يأكل قوله: (فيأكل أضحيته) وفي لفظ البيهقي فيأكل من كبد أضحيته. قال في غاية البيان: لأن الناس أضياف الله تعالى في هذا اليوم فيستحب أن يكون تناولهم من لحوم الأضاحي التي هي ضيافة الله تعالى. قوله: (فلذا قبل الخ) أي لهذا الحديث قيل الخ. قال السيد: وهو ظاهر في ترجيح الإطلاق لحكايته التفصيل بقيل اهـ وقيده في غاية البيان بالمصري أما القروي فإنه يذوق من تأخير الأكل إلا لمن يضحي ليأكل منها أولاً ويكبر في الطريق ذاهباً إلى المصلى (جهراً) استحباباً كما فعل النبي ( ويعلم الأضحية فيبين من تجب عليه ومم تجب وسن الواجب ووقت ذبحه والذابح، وحكم الأكل، والتصدق والهدية والادخار (و) يعلم (تكبير التشريق) سنة حين يصبح ولا يمسك كما في عيد الفطر لأن الأضاحي تذبح في القرى من الصباح بخلاف المصر حيث لا تذبح فيه قبل الصلاة ،اهـ وقوله فإنه يذوق من حين يصبح أي من أضاحيهم بدليل التعليل بقوله : لأن الأضاحي، وإلا لعلل بعدم الصلاة عليهم قوله : (ويكبر في الطريق جهراً) أشار بذكر الطريق إلى ما في المبسوط، وشرح الطحاوي أنه يقطعه إذا انتهى إلى الجبانة وفي رواية حتى يشرع الإمام فيها وعمل الناس على هذه الرواية، ويكبر كلما لقي جمعاً أو علا شرفاً، أو هبط وادياً كالتلبية ولا يسن التكبير جهراً في غير هذه الأيام إلا بإزاء عدو أو لصوص قيل : وكذا الحريق والمخاوف كلها كما في الزاهدي قوله : (من تجب عليه) هو المسلم العاقل الحر المالك للنصاب، ولو غير تام قوله : (ومم تجب) فتجب من الأنواع الثلاثة الأبل والبقر والغنم. قوله : (وسن الواجب) هو الثني من هذه الأنواع، وهو ما تم له من الغنم، وطعن في الثانية ومن البقر ما تم له سنتان وطعن في الثالثة، ومن الإبل، ما تم له أربعة وطعن في الخامسة ويجزىء الجذع من الضأن وهو ما تم له نصف حول، أو أكثر كما بين في محله قوله : ( ووقت ذبحه) هو يوم العيد، ويومان بعده. قوله: (والذابح) هو صاحب الأضحية أن كان يبحسن الذبح، وإلا فيأمر غيره، ويشهد الذبح فإنه يغفر له بأول قطرة من دمها كما قاله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم السيدة نساء العالمين بنته فاطمة رضي الله عنها قوله : (وحكم الأكل والتصدق) هما بالثلث ويهدي ،ثلثاً، ويدخر ثلثاً إن لم يكن صاحب عيال، وإلا فصرفه إلى عياله أولى من صرفه إلى الصدقة والهدية. قوله : (ويعلم تكبير التشريق) هو في اللغة تقديم اللحم بإلقائه في المشرقة أي الشمس، وقد جرت عادتهم بتشريق لحوم الأضاحي في اليوم الحادي عشر والثاني عشر والثالث عشر فسميت هذه الثلاثة أيام التشريق، وأيام النحر ثلاثة أيضاً ، وهو العاشر من ذي الحجة، ويومان بعده فالمجموع أربعة الأول منها نحر النحر، فقط، والرابع تشريق فقط، والمتوسطان نحر وتشريق، وعلى هذا المعنى اعترضت الإضافة بأن المعنى حينئذ تكبير أيام التشريق ولا يصح لأنه يؤتى به في غيرها، وأجيب بأنه لما كان أكثر أيامه أيام التشريق نزل الأكثر منزلة الكل، وبأن لفظ التشريق كما يطلق على ما تقدم يطلق أيضاً على رفع الصوت بالتكبير في هذه الأيام المخصوصة، كما قاله أئمة اللغة: وحيننذ فالإضافة من قبيل إضافة البيان أي التكبير الذي هو التشريق، وهذا الثاني هو الذي أشار إليه المؤلف بقوله : من إضافة الخاص أي الذي هو التشريق بالمعنى الثاني إلى العام، وهو مطلق تكبير وهذا إنما يتمشى على أن أول المتضايفين مضاف إليه، وهو أحد أقوال ثلاثة، وقيل: بالعكس، وهو المشهور وقيل : كل يطلق على كل .
His statement: 'And the rulings of Eid al-Adha are like those of al-Fitr' – you already know them, but on al-Adha, one delays eating after the prayer as a recommendation; if one does it early, it is not disliked in the chosen view, because he (peace be upon him) would not eat on the day of al-Adha until he returned and ate from his sacrifice. Therefore, it is said: it is not recommended to delay until Dhuhr. It was answered: even if we accept that, it does not harm us, but the Duha prayer is not obligatory, so one has a choice, unlike the Zuhr of Jumu'ah which is obligatory, so its performance is required. End. And it follows from what he mentioned that he does not perform the Duha prayer if he prays the Eid, because of the combination of compensation and the compensated, but it is not so. His statement: 'and it was reported' as an active participle, and its pronoun refers to Ibn Mas'ud. His statement: 'and abundant reward' – in al-Qahastani from al-Mas'udiyyah: He gives reward equal to the number of everything that grew in this year. End. His statement: 'such as the new moon being obscured etc.' includes rain and the like, as in al-Siraj, and also if he led the people in prayer without purification and it was not known except after noon, as in al-Khaniyya. His statement: 'and they testified after noon or before it in a way that the gathering of people is not possible...' al-Sayyid said: regarding whether it is qada or ada, there are two opinions as narrated by al-Qahastani, and its text: 'he makes up his prayer as indicated by al-Kirmani, al-Jullabi, al-Hidayah, and others, or he performs it (as ada) as in al-Tuhfa.' His statement: 'to the next day' – its time from the second is like the first, as stated by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'And the rulings of al-Adha' i.e., the conditions and recommended acts are the rulings of al-Fitr, and there is no need to enumerate the identical, rather only the different needs to be counted, as indicated by al-Sad. His statement: 'delays eating after the prayer' and also everything that contradicts fasting from its dawn until he prays, and reports from the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) have come in succession about preventing boys from eating and infants from breastfeeding on the morning of al-Adha, as in al-Zahidi. In it there is a hint that this abstention is not fasting, so intention is not required for it, and that it is mandub (recommended) only for the city dwellers, as in the division of the commanded from al-Kashf of Qahastani. His statement: 'and if he does it early, it is not disliked in the chosen view' – al-Hamawi said: the negation is of karahah tahrim, but there must be karahah of leaving the sunnah, the lowest degree of which is tanzih. End. His statement: 'he would not eat' with the ya' fat-ha, i.e., he would not eat. His statement: 'he eats from his sacrifice' and in the wording of al-Bayhaqi, 'he eats from the liver of his sacrifice'. He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: because people are the guests of Allah Almighty on this day, so it is recommended that their consumption be from the meats of the sacrifices which are the hospitality of Allah Almighty. His statement: 'therefore it is said etc.' i.e., because of this hadith, it is said etc. Al-Sayyid said: it is apparent in preferring the absolute because he narrated the detail with 'qil'. End. And he restricted it in Ghayat al-Bayan to the city dweller; as for the villager, he tastes from the delay of eating except for one who sacrifices to eat from it first. And he recites takbir on the way going to the prayer place aloud, as recommended as the Prophet did. He teaches the sacrifice and explains whom it is obligatory upon, from what it is obligatory, the age of the obligatory, the time of its slaughter, the slaughterer, the ruling on eating, giving charity, presenting gifts, and storing. He teaches the takbir al-tashriq as a sunnah from dawn on the day of Arafah? Actually 'when morning comes' and he does not abstain as in Eid al-Fitr because sacrifices are slaughtered in villages from the morning, unlike the city where they are not slaughtered before the prayer. End. His statement: 'he tastes from when morning comes' i.e., from their sacrifices, by evidence of the cause by his statement 'because the sacrifices', otherwise he would have reasoned with the absence of prayer over them. His statement: 'and recites takbir on the way aloud' – by mentioning the way he referred to what is in al-Mabsut and Sharh al-Tahawi, that he stops when he reaches the cemetery, and in a narration 'until the imam begins in it', and the people act upon this narration. He recites takbir whenever he meets a group or ascends a high place or descends a valley, like the talbiyah. Reciting takbir aloud is not sunnah on other days except in front of an enemy or thieves; it is said: similarly fire and all fears, as in al-Zahidi. His statement: 'who is obligatory upon him' – the Muslim, sane, free, owner of the nisab, even if incomplete. His statement: 'from what it is obligatory' – it is obligatory from three types: camels, cows, and sheep. His statement: 'the age of the obligatory' – it is the thani from these types: for sheep, what has completed one year and entered the second; for cows, what has completed two years and entered the third; for camels, what has completed four years and entered the fifth. And the jadha' from sheep is sufficient, which is what has completed half a year or more, as explained in its place. His statement: 'the time of its slaughter' – it is the day of Eid and two days after. His statement: 'the slaughterer' – he is the owner of the sacrifice if he knows how to slaughter, otherwise he orders another, and he witnesses the slaughter, for he is forgiven at the first drop of its blood, as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to the chief of the women of the worlds, his daughter Fatimah (may Allah be pleased with her). His statement: 'the ruling on eating and giving charity' – both are one-third, and he gives a third as gift, and stores a third if he does not have dependents; otherwise spending on his dependents is better than giving charity or gift. His statement: 'and he teaches takbir al-tashriq' – linguistically it is the sending forth of meat by throwing it into the sun (i.e., drying it). And their custom was to dry the meat of sacrifices on the 11th, 12th, and 13th days, so these three days are called the days of tashriq. The days of nahr (slaughter) are also three: the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and two days after, so total four: the first is nahr only, the fourth is tashriq only, and the middle two are both nahr and tashriq. On this meaning, the construction (idaafa) was objected: the meaning would be 'takbir of the days of tashriq', but that is incorrect because it is performed outside them. The answer is that since most of its days are the days of tashriq, the majority takes the place of the whole. Also, the word 'tashriq' is applied to the raising of the voice in takbir on these particular days, as the linguists said. Then the construction is that of bayan (explication), i.e., the takbir that is al-tashriq. This second interpretation is what the author referred to by his statement 'the addition of the specific which is tashriq in the second sense to the general, which is absolute takbir'. And this is only valid if the first of the two words in the idaafa is the mudaf ilayh, which is one of three opinions. It is said: the opposite is the famous view. And it is said: each can be applied to the other.
Source pages p. 536

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya covers the important rulings of Eid al-Adha as summarised in Maraqi al-Falah. The commentary begins by explaining that the rulings of Eid al-Adha are the same as those of Eid al-Fitr with one exception: on Eid al-Adha it is recommended (mustahabb) to delay eating until after the prayer, whereas on Eid al-Fitr it is recommended to eat before prayer. The commentator discusses the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would not eat on Eid al-Adha until he returned from the prayer and ate from his sacrifice. There is a discussion about whether it is disliked to eat before the prayer; the chosen view is that it is not prohibitively disliked, but it remains the recommended sunnah to delay. The ruling applies primarily to city dwellers (ahl al-misr); for villagers (qarawi), the custom differs because they slaughter early, so they may eat earlier. Then the text covers the takbir on the way to the prayer: one recites the takbir (Allahu Akbar) aloud, and stops when reaching the place of prayer, or when the imam begins the prayer, according to the more common practice. The takbir is also recited when meeting another crowd, ascending a high place, etc. It is not prescribed to recite takbir aloud on other days except in certain situations like battle or fear. The passage then details the rulings of the sacrifice (udhiyah): who must sacrifice (a free sane Muslim who owns the nisab), from which animals (three types: camel, cattle, sheep), the required age (thani for each, and jadha' for sheep), the time (Eid day and two days after), the slaughterer (the owner if able, otherwise another, and the owner should witness the slaughter for forgiveness), and the distribution of the meat: it is recommended to eat one-third, give one-third as gift, and store one-third; if one has dependents, spending on them takes priority. Finally, the passage explains Takbir al-Tashriq: the linguistic meaning of 'tashriq' is the drying of meat in the sun, and the days of tashriq are the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah. However, the takbir is also recited on these days, so the phrase 'takbir al-tashriq' can be interpreted in two ways: either as the takbir of the days of tashriq, or the takbir that is itself called tashriq. The commentator clarifies the grammatical construction and the difference between the two interpretations, concluding that the intended meaning is the takbir that is performed specifically during these days, and it is a specific type of takbir.

Key Terms
أضحية (udhiyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on Eid al-Adha.
ثني (thani): An animal that has reached the required age: for sheep, one year; for cows, two years; for camels, four years.
جذع (jadha'): A young sheep that is at least six months old, acceptable for sacrifice.
تشريق (tashriq): Linguistically: drying meat in the sun; technically: the three days following Eid al-Adha (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah).
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The special takbir recited after every fard prayer during the days of tashriq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi classification of udhiyah (sacrifice) for those who own the nisab?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah muakkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats udhiyah as wajib for those who can afford it, and the other Eid rulings (delaying eating, takbir) are sunnah based on Prophetic practice.

Delaying 'Eid al-Adha Prayer: Conditions and Timing
Commentary on delaying the 'Eid al-Adha prayer: timing and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying the 'Eid al-Adha prayer and identify the conditions (excuse vs. no excuse) and time restrictions (three days, between sunrise and midday).

Core Idea
Delaying 'Eid al-Adha prayer without excuse is disliked; with excuse, it removes dislike, but must be between sunrise and midday.

This commentary from al-Tahtawi clarifies a key subtlety in the 'Eid al-Adha prayer timing. While the matn allows delay up to three days, al-Tahtawi explains that with an excuse it is not disliked, without it is disliked, and the prayer is only valid between sunrise and zenith each day. He also links the prayer time to the sacrifice timing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the 'Eid al-Adha prayer. The ruling is that it may be delayed up to three days, but with conditions on dislike and timing.
2
Identify the condition of excuse
If there is an excuse (e.g., rain, obstacles), delaying removes the karahah. Without an excuse, delaying is makruh (disliked) because it contradicts the established practice.
3
Identify the time restrictions
The prayer is timed to the sacrifice days (three days). However, each day it must be performed between sunrise (irtifa') and midday (zawal). After zawal, the prayer is invalid on that day.
4
Understand the link to sacrifice
The sacrifice (qurbani) is also timed to the days of al-Adha. On the first day, the prayer precedes the sacrifice. If prayer is delayed, sacrifice is delayed accordingly. On the second day, same applies, unless there is no hope of the imam leading the prayer.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario with or without an excuse, determine whether delaying is allowed and whether it is disliked. Also verify the prayer time within the window.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتؤخر صلاة عيد الأضحى بعذر لنفي الكراهة وبلا عذر مع الكراهة لمخالفة المأثور إلى ثلاثة أيام لأنها مؤقتة بوقت الأضحية فيما بين الارتفاع إلى الزوال ولا تصح بعدها قوله : (لأنها مؤقتة بوقت الأضحية) وذلك لأن التضحية قربة تتوقت بأيام النحر، وهي ثلاثة فكذا الصلاة لأنها صلاة الأضحى، ولو أخرت صلاة العيد في اليوم الأول أخر، والتضحية إلى الزوال ولا تجزيهم إلا بعده، وكذا في اليوم الثاني، لا تجزيهم قبل الزوال، إلا إذا كانوا لا يرجون أن يصلي الإمام، فحينئذ تجزيهم قوله : (فيما بين الخ) كالاستدراك على ما قبله يعني الصلاة، وان وقتت بوقت الأضحية نظراً إلى الأيام الثلاثة لكنها تتقيد بما بين الارتفاع إلى الزوال، ولا تصح بعدها
And the 'Eid al-Adha prayer is delayed due to an excuse to remove dislike, and without an excuse it is with dislike due to contradicting the transmitted practice up to three days because it is timed to the time of sacrifice in between sunrise to zenith and it is not valid after that. He said: (because it is timed to the time of sacrifice) and that is because sacrifice is an act of worship timed to the days of slaughter, which are three, and likewise the prayer is the prayer of al-Adha. If the 'Eid prayer is delayed on the first day, it is delayed, and the sacrifice is up to zenith and it does not suffice except after it, and likewise on the second day, it does not suffice before zenith, unless they do not hope that the imam will pray, then it suffices them. He said: (in between etc.) It is like an exception to what preceded, meaning the prayer, and although it is timed to the time of sacrifice considering the three days, it is restricted to between sunrise and zenith, and it is not valid after that.
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya explains the ruling on delaying the 'Eid al-Adha prayer. The underlying matn states that the prayer may be delayed up to three days, but with a condition: if there is an excuse (such as rain or other obstacles), then delaying removes the dislike (karahah); if there is no excuse, delaying is disliked because it goes against the established practice (al-ma'thur). The reason for the permissibility of delay is that the 'Eid al-Adha prayer is linked to the sacrifice, which has a time window of three days. However, the commentary clarifies that within each day, the prayer must be performed between sunrise (irtifa') and midday (zawal); it is not valid after zawal. On the first day, if the prayer is delayed, the sacrifice must also be delayed until after the prayer. On the second day, the same applies, but if there is no hope of an imam leading the prayer, the sacrifice can be made before the prayer. This reflects the Hanafi ruling that the 'Eid prayer's time is linked to the sacrifice but is restricted to the first half of each day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can the 'Eid al-Adha prayer be delayed?
A) Not at all, it must be on the first day before midday.
B) Up to three days, but with an excuse to avoid dislike, and without an excuse it is disliked.
C) Up to seven days, as long as sacrifices are still being performed.
D) It can be delayed indefinitely.

Key Takeaway
The 'Eid al-Adha prayer may be delayed up to three days, but only between sunrise and noon each day; with an excuse it is not disliked, without it is disliked.

Timing and Delay of Eid al-Adha Prayer
Ruling on permissible delay and time window for Eid al-Adha prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying the Eid al-Adha prayer and identify the permissible time window up to three days.

Core Idea
Eid al-Adha prayer can be delayed up to three days but never valid after noon each day.

This passage from Maraqi al-Falah with al-Tahtawi's commentary explains the timing for the Eid al-Adha prayer. Unlike Eid al-Fitr, which is only on the first day, the Hanafi school permits the Eid al-Adha prayer to be offered on the 10th, 11th, or 12th of Dhul Hijjah. However, the prayer's time window each day is restricted to between sunrise and noon. The reason given is that the prayer is tied to the sacrifice (udhiyah), which itself is tied to the three days of Nahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and rule
The act is the Eid al-Adha prayer. The rule: it may be delayed up to three days (with excuse to negate dislike, without excuse disliked).
2
Understand the reason
The prayer is tied to the sacrifice, which is valid on three days. Thus, the prayer may be performed on any of those days.
3
Restrict the daily time window
Each day, the prayer is only valid between sunrise (irtifa') and noon (zawal). It cannot be performed after noon.
4
Note the exception
For those who do not hope the imam will pray, the sacrifice is valid before the prayer, but the prayer itself still follows the time window.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتؤخر) صلاة عيد الأضحى (بعذر) لنفي الكراهة وبلا عذر مع الكراهة لمخالفة المأثور إلى ثلاثة أيام لأنها مؤقتة بوقت الأضحية فيما بين الارتفاع إلى الزوال ولا تصح بعدها قوله : (شرعت له أي لأجل التعليم المأخوذ من يعلم قوله : (وينبغي) البحث لصاحب البحر. قوله : (لأنها مؤقتة بوقت الأضحية) وذلك لأن التضحية قربة تتوقت بأيام النحر، وهي ثلاثة فكذا الصلاة لأنها صلاة الأضحى، ولو أخرت صلاة العيد في اليوم الأول أخر، والتضحية إلى الزوال ولا تجزيهم إلا بعده، وكذا في اليوم الثاني، لا تجزيهم قبل الزوال، إلا إذا كانوا لا يرجون أن يصلي الإمام، فحينئذ تجزيهم قوله : (فيما بين الخ) كالاستدراك على ما قبله يعني الصلاة، وان وقتت بوقت الأضحية نظراً إلى الأيام الثلاثة لكنها تتقيد بما بين الارتفاع إلى الزوال، ولا تصح بعدها
The Eid al-Adha prayer may be delayed (with an excuse) to negate dislike, and without an excuse it is disliked for opposing the transmitted practice, up to three days, because it is tied to the time of sacrifice, between sunrise and noon, and it is not valid after that. He said: (It is legislated for it) meaning for the sake of teaching derived from 'he teaches'. He said: (It is appropriate) the discussion is for the author of al-Bahr. He said: (Because it is tied to the time of sacrifice) That is because sacrifice is an act of worship tied to the days of Nahr, which are three, so likewise the prayer because it is the prayer of al-Adha. If the Eid prayer is delayed on the first day, the sacrifice is delayed to noon and is not valid for them except after it, likewise on the second day, it is not valid for them before noon, unless they do not hope that the imam will pray, then it is valid for them. He said: (within the interval etc.) It is like an exception to what came before, meaning the prayer, and although it is tied to the time of sacrifice in view of the three days, it is restricted to between sunrise and noon, and it is not valid after that.
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah, with expansion commentary from al-Tahtawi. The ruling states that the Eid al-Adha prayer can be delayed up to three days if there is an excuse, and doing so without an excuse is makruh because it contradicts the established practice. The reason given is that the prayer is linked to the sacrifice (udhiyah), which itself is tied to the three days of Nahr (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah). However, the prayer's specific time within each day is between sunrise (irtifa') and noon (zawal). The commentary explains that the sacrifice is valid only after the imam's prayer, so if the prayer is delayed, the sacrifice follows suit. For those in remote areas who do not expect the imam to pray, they may sacrifice earlier. The prayer is not valid after noon, even within the three days.

Key Terms
الأضحية (al-udhiyah): The sacrificial animal offered on Eid al-Adha and the following days.
الارتفاع (al-irtifa'): The time when the sun has risen and is clearly above the horizon, about 15-20 minutes after sunrise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the time window for Eid al-Adha prayer each day according to this passage?
A) From sunrise to noon
B) From sunrise to sunset
C) From noon to sunset
D) From sunrise to mid-morning

Key Takeaway
The Eid al-Adha prayer is valid between sunrise and noon on the 10th, 11th, or 12th of Dhul Hijjah; delaying it beyond the first day without excuse is makruh.

Ruling on al-Ta'rif: Imitating Pilgrims at Arafat is a Disliked Innovation
Ruling with proof that imitating pilgrims at Arafat is a disliked innovation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on al-Ta'rif, explain why it is makruh tahrimi, and apply the maxim 'dar' al-mafsadah muqaddam' to similar cases.

Core Idea
Imitating the Arafat vigil outside Mecca is a prohibited innovation.

On the day of Arafah, many Muslims who are not performing Hajj may feel inclined to gather and supplicate as if they were at Arafat. This practice, known as al-Ta'rif, is examined in this passage from the Hanafi tradition. The text clarifies that it is not a recommended act but rather a disliked innovation, and it employs the important legal principle that repelling harm takes precedence over bringing benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the definition of al-Ta'rif in the text and the explicit ruling from the matn and hashiah. The matn says 'it is not a recognized practice' and 'not recommended but disliked'.
The hashiah specifies 'makruh tahrimi' (prohibitively disliked) because it resembles a specific worship (standing at Arafat) done in the wrong place.
2
Understand the proof: why it is an innovation
The text argues that al-Ta'rif is an innovation (bid'ah) not established from the Prophet or his Companions. It draws an analogy with tawaf around a non-Ka'bah building, which is forbidden.
The comparison shows that mimicking a place-specific worship elsewhere is prohibited.
3
Refute the counter-proof: Ibn Abbas report
The passage addresses a potential objection: a report that Ibn Abbas did something similar in Basra. It interprets this as a prayer for rain (istisqa'), not imitation of the Arafat vigil.
This interpretation preserves the ruling and shows how reports are reconciled with principles.
4
Apply the principle of repelling harm
The hashiah ends with the legal maxim 'repelling corruption takes precedence over bringing benefit'. It highlights the real-world harms: rabble, gender mixing, and fitna.
The commentator concludes that preventing al-Ta'rif is obligatory (wajib) due to prevalent corruption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتعريف) وهو التشبه بالواقفين بعرفات (ليس بشيء) معتبر فلا يستحب بل يكره في الصحيح لأنه اختراع في الدين ولا يخفى ما يحصل من رعاع العامة باجتماعهم، واختلاطهم بالنساء والأحداث في هذا الزمان ودرء المفسدة قوله : ( وهو التشبه بالواقفين) هذا المراد هنا، هو ويطلق على التطيب بذي عرف أي ريح طيبة، وإنشاد الضالة والوقوف بعرفات أي تشبيه الناس أنفسهم بالواقفين بعرفات والأولى التشبيه قوله بل يكره في الصحيح) وظاهر أنها تحريمية لأن الوقوف عهد قربة بمكان مخصوص فلم يجز فعله في غيره كالطواف، ونحوه ألا ترى أنه لا يجوز الطواف حول مسجد أو بيت سوى الكعبة تشبهاً كما في غاية البيان، وفي الكافي من طاف بمسجد سوى الكعبة يخشى عليه الكفر اهـ. قوله : (لأنه اختراع في الدين) إذ لم يثبت عنه ، ولا عن أصحابه رضوان الله تعالى عليهم، وما نقل عن ابن عباس أنه فعل ذلك بالبصرة يحمل على أنه خرج للاستسقاء ونحوه لا للتشبيه بأهل عرفات قال عطاء الخراساني : إن استطعت أن تخلو بنفسك عشية عرفة فافعل .اهـ. قوله: (رعاع) قال في القاموس : الرعاع كسحاب الأحداث والطغام وكسحابة النعامة، ومن لا فؤاد له، ولا عقل اهـ، وقال في مادة حدث، والأحداث أمطار أول السنة ورجل حدث السن وحديثها بين الحداثة، والحدوثة فتى والحديث الجديد والخبر اهـ والمناسب هنا هو أرادة من لا فؤاد له ولا عقل وعليه فالمناسب أن يقول رعاعة العامة أي من لا عقل له منهم، والمراد بالأحداث هنا الفتيان أي الشبان قوله : ( ودرء المفسدة مقدم) أي دفع المفسدة مقدم على جلب المصلحة قال في الشرح بعد ذكر هذه العبارة وحسم ذلك الواجب .اهـ.
Al-Ta'rif (imitating the pilgrims at Arafat) is not a recognized practice, so it is not recommended but rather disliked in the correct view because it is an innovation in religion. And it is not hidden what harm arises from the rabble of the common people gathering, mixing with women and youth in this time, and repelling corruption is prioritised. He said: (It is imitating those standing at Arafat) This is what is meant here. It is also used for perfuming with a pleasant scent, and for lost property announcement, and standing at Arafat i.e. people imitating those standing at Arafat. The better term is 'imitation'. He said (rather it is disliked in the correct view) and its apparent meaning is that it is prohibitively disliked because standing is a confirmed act of worship at a specific place, so it is not permitted to do it elsewhere, like tawaf and similar. Do you not see that tawaf around a mosque or house other than the Ka'bah is not permitted in imitation? As in Ghayat al-Bayan, and in al-Kafi: Whoever makes tawaf around a mosque other than the Ka'bah, we fear for him unbelief. He said: (Because it is an innovation in religion) since it is not confirmed from him (the Prophet) nor from his Companions. What is transmitted from Ibn Abbas that he did that in Basra is interpreted as he went out for istisqa' (rain prayer) and the like, not to imitate the people of Arafat. Ata al-Khurasani said: If you can be alone by yourself on the evening of Arafah, do so. He said: (rabble) He said in al-Qamus: Al-Ra'a' is like clouds: the youth, the rabble, and like a cloud: the ostrich, and he who has no heart nor intellect. And he said under the root 'hadath': al-ahdath are first rains of the year, a young man, etc. The appropriate meaning here is he who has no heart nor intellect. Therefore it is appropriate to say 'ra'a'at al-'ammah' meaning those among them with no intellect. By 'ahdath' here is meant the young men. He said: (and repelling corruption is prioritised) i.e. repelling corruption takes precedence over bringing benefit. The sharh said after mentioning this phrase: 'and cutting off that is obligatory.'
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage starts as a ruling statement from the matn and is then refined by the hashiah. It addresses 'al-Ta'rif', which refers to people gathering on the day of Arafah and acting like the pilgrims at Arafat, such as standing in fields and supplicating. The matn declares it 'not a recognized practice'—meaning it has no legal basis—so it is not recommended (mustahabb) but rather disliked (makruh). The hashiah clarifies that this is the sahih (correct) position, and indicates it is 'tahrimi' (prohibitively disliked) because it resembles a specific act of worship (standing at Arafat) in a different place, analogous to performing tawaf around a non-Ka'bah building, which is strictly forbidden and even leads to fear of kufr. The justification is that it is an innovation (bid'ah) not established from the Prophet or his Companions. The report of Ibn Abbas doing something similar is interpreted as a prayer for rain, not imitation. Additionally, the passage highlights the practical harm of such gatherings: rabble, mixing of genders, and fitna. Therefore, the principle 'repelling corruption takes precedence over bringing benefit' is invoked, and the commentator concludes that preventing this practice is obligatory (wajib).

Key Terms
التعريف (al-ta'rif): The practice of imitating the pilgrims at Arafat on the day of Arafah, by standing and supplicating in congregation outside of Mecca.
درء المفسدة مقدم (dar' al-mafsadah muqaddam): A legal maxim meaning 'repelling harm takes precedence over bringing benefit'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on al-Ta'rif (imitating the pilgrims at Arafat) according to this passage?
A) It is recommended (mustahabb)
B) It is permissible (mubah)
C) It is disliked (makruh) and an innovation
D) It is obligatory (wajib)

Key Takeaway
Al-Ta'rif is a makruh tahrimi innovation because it imitates a place-specific worship and causes harm, and the principle of repelling corruption overrides any perceived benefit.

Obligation and Conditions of Takbir al-Tashriq
Ruling with proof and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Takbir al-Tashriq as wajib, identify its timing, conditions, and the Hanafi proof from the Quran and ijma.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib after every fard prayer from Fajr of Arafah to Asr of Eid, said immediately and in congregation.

This lesson examines the obligation of Takbir al-Tashriq, a specific dhikr recited during the days of Tashriq. We will explore its timing, conditions, and the evidence from the Quran and consensus, as detailed in the classical Hanafi text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what Takbir al-Tashriq is and what legal category (hukm) it falls under according to the Hanafi school.
The text explicitly says 'wajib' in the choice of the majority.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited for the obligation. The text quotes the Quranic verse from Al-Baqarah 2:203.
The verse is general; its interpretation relies on consensus.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the verse proves the obligation. The command 'remember Allah' is general; takbir is a specific form of remembrance. The Hanafi school deduces wujub, not fard, due to the zanni nature of the dalalah.
This distinction is key to Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the disagreement with other schools regarding the starting time. The Hanafi position is from Fajr of Arafah; Shafi'is and Malikis begin after Zuhr of Eid.
The text supports the Hanafi view with consensus on the minimum.
5
Identify the conditions
List the conditions for the obligation: after fard prayer, with immediacy (fawr), in congregation (with a resident imam), and for prayers performed in congregation.
Conditions like 'fawr' and 'jamacah' are critical for practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

التكبير أيام التشريق على الواحد والإثنين التكبير على من صلى بجماعة (مستحبة) خرج به جماعة النساء فيجب على إمام مقيم بمصر) لا مسافر ومقيم بقرية (و) يجب التكبير على قوله : (والتعريف) وهو التشبه بالواقفين ويطلق على التطيب بذي عرف أي ريح طيبة، وإنشاد الضالة والوقوف بعرفات أي تشبيه الناس أنفسهم بالواقفين بعرفات والأولى التشبيه قوله بل يكره في الصحيح) وظاهر أنها تحريمية لأن الوقوف عهد قربة بمكان مخصوص فلم يجز فعله في غيره كالطواف، ونحوه ألا ترى أنه لا يجوز الطواف حول مسجد أو بيت سوى الكعبة تشبهاً كما في غاية البيان، وفي الكافي من طاف بمسجد سوى الكعبة يخشى عليه الكفر اهـ. قوله : (لأنه اختراع في الدين) إذ لم يثبت عنه ، ولا عن أصحابه رضوان الله تعالى عليهم، وما نقل عن ابن عباس أنه فعل ذلك بالبصرة يحمل على أنه خرج للاستسقاء ونحوه لا للتشبيه بأهل عرفات قال عطاء الخراساني : إن استطعت أن تخلو بنفسك عشية عرفة فافعل .اهـ. قوله: (رعاع) قال في القاموس : الرعاع كسحاب الأحداث والطغام وكسحابة النعامة، ومن لا فؤاد له، ولا عقل اهـ، وقال في مادة حدث، والأحداث أمطار أول السنة ورجل حدث السن وحديثها بين الحداثة، والحدوثة فتى والحديث الجديد والخبر اهـ والمناسب هنا هو أرادة من لا فؤاد له ولا عقل وعليه فالمناسب أن يقول رعاعة العامة أي من لا عقل له منهم، والمراد بالأحداث هنا الفتيان أي الشبان قوله : ( ودرء المفسدة مقدم) أي دفع المفسدة مقدم على جلب المصلحة قال في الشرح بعد ذكر هذه العبارة وحسم ذلك الواجب .اهـ.
And the takbir of tashriq is obligatory in the choice of the majority, due to His statement: 'And remember Allah during the appointed days.' [Al-Baqarah 2:203] (From after the Fajr prayer (of Arafah to the end of the Asr of the Eid), because of the consensus on the minimum. And he says it (once) provided it is (immediately after) every (obligatory) prayer (fard), which includes Friday prayer, and excludes supererogatory, witr, funeral, and Eid prayer if the fard is (performed) i.e., even if it is a make-up of the obligatory prayers of this period, which are eight. (In congregation) excludes the individual, based on Ibn Mas'ud's report: 'There is no takbir during the days of tashriq for the one or two; takbir is for the one who prays in congregation.' (Recommended) excludes the congregation of women. So it is obligatory upon a resident imam (in a city), not a traveler or a resident in a village. (And) the takbir is obligatory upon...
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof, expanded by the hashiah. It establishes that Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib (obligatory) according to the majority of Hanafi scholars, citing the Quranic verse 'remember Allah during the appointed days' (2:203). The obligation is for every fard prayer performed in congregation, from Fajr of the day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) until Asr of the day of Eid (10th Dhul Hijjah). The takbir is said once, immediately after each fard prayer, without a long interruption. It applies only to prayers performed in congregation, not for individuals, based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. The imam of the congregation must be a resident (muqim) of a city (misr); if the imam is a traveler or a resident of a village, the takbir is not obligatory on them. The congregation must be recommended (mustahabb) congregation, meaning women's congregation is excluded. The term 'fard' includes all obligatory prayers, including those made up within the tashriq days (eight prayers total from Fajr of Arafah to Asr of Eid).

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The specific takbir (Allahu Akbar) recited after obligatory prayers during the days of tashriq (11th-13th Dhul Hijjah, including Eid day).
فور (fawr): Immediacy; the takbir must be said right after the prayer without a deliberate break that would break the sanctity of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the obligation of Takbir al-Tashriq begin according to the Hanafi school?
A) After the Eid prayer on 10th Dhul Hijjah
B) After Fajr of the day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah)
C) After Zuhr of Eid day
D) After Maghrib of Eid day

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib after every fard prayer from Fajr of Arafah to Asr of Eid, said immediately and in congregation, based on the Quran and ijma.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Takbir al-Tashriq: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Obligation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on takbir al-tashriq obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the obligation of takbir al-tashriq, identify the thamarah al-khilaf, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a concrete scenario.

Core Idea
Takbir al-tashriq is wajib on everyone who prays a fard prayer—fatwa follows the Sahibayn, not Abu Hanifa.

The takbir al-tashriq is a wajib act recited after fard prayers during the days of tashriq. But who is obligated to perform it? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, held different views. The later Hanafi school adopted the more cautious position of the Sahibayn, making the takbir obligatory on every individual. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its basis
Identify that takbir al-tashriq is wajib (not fard) based on a zanni dalil (Quran 2:203) and continuous practice. Note the timing: from Fajr of Arafa to Asr of the last day of tashriq.
The Quranic verse is not qati' al-dalala, so the obligation is wujub, not fard.
2
Identify the dispute
Abu Hanifa restricts obligation to the imam of a city congregation and his followers. The Sahibayn extend it to every person who prays any fard prayer, even alone or traveling.
This is the key point of ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the proofs
Abu Hanifa relies on the athar of Ibn Mas'ud indicating a congregational context. The Sahibayn argue the takbir is a follower (tabi') of the fard prayer itself, thus binding on all who pray it.
Both sides rest on transmitted practice and analogy.
4
Analyze the tarjih
Later scholars gave fatwa on the Sahibayn's view due to caution (ihtiyat): performing it unnecessarily is better than omitting what may be required.
The text states: 'wa bihi ya'malu wa 'alayhi al-fatwa'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a traveler alone or a villager would not say the takbir according to Abu Hanifa, but must say it according to the Sahibayn and the mufta bihi view.
This directly affects the practice of many Muslims today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لقوله تعالى : ( واذكروا الله في أيام معدودات )) إنما لم يكن فرضاً بهذه الآية لما قيل أن المراد به ذكر الله تعالى عند رمي الجمار بدليل : فمن تعجل في يومين الآية فلم يكن الكتاب قطعي الدلالة، فيفيد
