للتنصيص على البعدية، ولو حذف لتوهم أن الغاية غير داخلة قوله : ( ويأتي به مرة وما زاد فهو مستحب . قال البدر العيني في شرح التحفة وأقره في الدر وفي الحموي عن القرا حصاري الإتيان به مرتين خلاف السنة، وفي مجمع الأنهر، أن زاد فقد خالف السنة اهـ ولعل محله ما إذا أتى به على أنه سنة، وأما إذا أتى به على أنه ذكر مطلق فلا ويحرر قوله : (فور كل صلاة (فرض) لأنه من خصائص الصلاة فيؤدي في حرمتها من غير فاصل يمنع البناء كقهقهة، وحدث عمد، وكلام مطلقاً وخروج من المسجد، ومجاوزة الصفوف في الصحراء، وإن لم يخرج منه، أو لم يجاوزها يكبر لأن حرمة الصلاة باقية كما في حاشية المؤلف فإن فصل بشيء من هذه الأشياء سقط عنه لأنها تقطع حرمة الصلاة لكنه إن فعل المنافي عمداً أثم ولو سبق حدث بعد السلام إن شار كبر في الحال لبقاء حرمة الصلاة ولا يشترط له الطهارة كما سيأتي لأنه لا يؤدي في تحريمة الصلاة واختاره السرخسي، وإن شاء توضأ وأتى به وصححه الزيلعي . قوله : (ولو كان قضاء من فروض هذه المدة فيها الخ) خرج به ثلاث صور الأولى فائتة غيرها فيها الثانية فاتتها في غير هذه الأيام الثالثة فائتها قضاها في أيامها من العام القابل، وفي هذ الأخيرة خلاف أبي يوسف، والصحيح أنه لا تكبير لها قوله (وهي الثمانية) الضمير إلى الفرائض . قوله : (والاثنين) لعله محمول على المنفردين، وإلا فالجماعة تتحقق بهما في غير الجمعة إلا أنه على هذا المعنى يرجع إلى المنفرد لأن كلا منهما منفرداً وإنه يعد الأثنين غير جماعة اعتباراً للمتبادر من لفظها قوله : خرج به جماعة النساء) أي والعراة قوله : (على إمام مقيم) هو إمام توطن المصر، أو نوى فيها أقامة خمسة عشر يوماً، أما من نوى أقامة ما دون ذلك لا يجب

من اقتدى به أي بالإمام المقيم ولو كان المقتدي (مسافراً أو رقيقاً، أو أنثى) تبعاً للإمام، والمرأة تخفض صوتها دون الرجال لأنه عورة، وعلى المسبوق التكبير لأنه مقتد تحريمة فيكبر بعد فراغه، ولو تابع الإمام ناسياً لم تفسد صلاته وفي التلبية تفسد، ويبدأ المحرم بالتكبير، ثم بالتلبية ولا يفتقر التكبير للطهارة، وتكبير الإمام (عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله) لما رويناه (وقالا) أي أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله (يجب) التكبير (فور كل فرض على من صلاه ولو كان منفرًا أو مسافراً أو (قروياً لأنه تبع للمكتوبة من فجر عرفة (إلى) عقب (عصر) اليوم الخامس من يوم عرفة) فيكون إلا آخر أيام التشريق (وبه) أي بقولهما: (يعمل وعليه الفتوى) إذ هو الإحتياط لأن الإتيان بما ليس عليه أولى من ترك ما قيل أنه
عليه على ما يفهم من كلامه قوله: (أي بالإمام المقيم هو الأصح، . وقيل: تجب على المقيم المقتدي بالمسافر، وجرى عليه صاحب الدر أفاده السيد قوله : (أو رقيقاً) الأولى حذفه كما فعل في التنوير لأنه يوهم الخلاف، وليس فيه خلاف قوله : (والمرأة تخفض صوتها) بحيث تسمع نفسها والتعليل يفيد الوجوب . قوله : (لأنه عورة هذا غير معتمد، والصحيح أنه يؤدي إلى الفتنة أفاده السيد، وقد سبق والمراد بالعورة معناها اللغوى، وهو العيب. قوله : (وفي التلبية تفسد لأنها كلام أجنبي، وفي البحر والكافي يبدأ بسجود السهو لوجوبه في تحريمتها، ثم بالتكبير لوجوبه في حرمتها، ثم بالتلبية لو محرماً لعدمهما، ولو بدأ بها سقط السجود والتكبير لأنها كلام فيقطع الوصل، ولو بدأ بالتكبير سجد لأنه لا ينافي الصلاة بخلاف التلبية؟ . قوله : ( وتكبير (الإمام بالجر عطفاً على طهارة. قوله لما رويناه) أي من أثر ابن مسعود السابق، وهو إنما يدل على اشتراط الجماعة فقط فهو أخص من المدعي، وللإمام دلائل أخر على ما رآه قوله : (إلى آخر أيام التشريق الأولى حذفه والاستغناء بما قبله لما فيه من إيهام أنه يكبر بعد المغرب لأنها آخر أيامه فتأمل قوله : ( وبه يعمل وعليه الفتوى) هذا بناء على أنه إذا اختلف الإمام وصاحباه، فالعبرة لقوة الدليل على ما في آخر الحاوي القدسي، أو هو مبني على أن قولهما في كل مسألة مروي عنه كما ذكره في الحاوي أيضاً، وإلا فكيف يفتى بقول غير صاحب المذهب كذا في البحر ، قال : وبهذا يندفع ما في الفتح من ترجيح قوله ورد فتوى المشايخ بقولهما : ولو نسي الإمام التكبير أتى به المؤتم وجوباً كسامع السجدة مع تاليها . قال محمد: قال يعقوب صليت بهم المغرب يوم عرفة فسهوت أن أكبر فكبر أبو حنيفة، ويعقوب هو اسم أبي يوسف القاضي صاحب الإمام الأعظم، وهو يعقوب بن ابراهيم بن حبيب بن سعد بن حبتة البجلي استصغر سعد يوم أحد، ونزل الكوفة ومات بها، وصلى عليه زيد بن أرقم وكبر خمساً، وتوفي أبو يوسف سنة اثنتين وثمانين ومائة في خلافة هرون الرشيد، وقد تضمنت هذه الحكاية من الفوائد الحكمية هذه المسألة ومن العرقية جلالة قدر أبي يوسف عند الإمام حيث قدمه وعظم منزلة الإمام في قلبه حيث نسي ما لا ينسى عادة لعلمه بأنه
The Book of Prayer. For His saying (And remember Allah during the appointed days) — it is not made fard by this verse because it is said that what is meant is the remembrance of Allah at the time of stoning the Jamarat, as evidenced by the verse 'whoever hastens in two days', so the Book is not qati' al-dalala, therefore it indicates wujub, not iftiraad. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) continuously observed it without ever leaving it, as did the Rightly Guided Caliphs and all the Companions. His statement: (from after the Fajr prayer of Arafa etc.) is the view of Ibn Mas'ud, both beginning and end, and thus the Imam (Abu Hanifa) adopted it due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Choose for my ummah what Ibn Umm Abd (Ibn Mas'ud) chose for it.' It was also said: its beginning is from after the Zuhr prayer of the first day of Nahr (the 10th of Dhul Hijjah), and this is what Malik and al-Shafi'i adopted, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf. His statement: (to the end) — he added 'end' to specify postposition, and if he had omitted it, it might be understood that the limit is not included. His statement: (he performs it once, and what is more is mustahabb). Al-Badr al-Ayni said in Sharh al-Tuhfa, and it is confirmed in al-Durr and in al-Hamawi from al-Qarahisari: performing it twice is contrary to the Sunnah. In Majma' al-Anhur: if he adds, he has opposed the Sunnah. Perhaps its place is when he performs it as Sunnah; but if he performs it as absolute dhikr, then not. And it is refined. His statement: (immediately after every obligatory prayer) because it is from the special characteristics of the prayer, so it is performed in its sanctity without a break that prevents continuity, such as laughter, intentional hadath, absolutely any speech, leaving the mosque, and passing rows in the desert. If he does not leave it or does not pass rows, he says the takbir because the sanctity of the prayer remains, as in the hashia of the author. If he separates by any of these things, it falls from him because they cut the sanctity of the prayer, but if he does the nullifier intentionally, he sins. If hadath preceded after the salam at the time he participates, he says takbir immediately due to the remaining sanctity of the prayer, and taharah is not required for it, as will come, because it is not performed in the tahrimah of the prayer, and al-Sarakhsi chose this view. If he wishes, he performs wudu and does it, and al-Zayla'i declared it sahih. His statement: (even if it is a qada of the obligatory prayers of this period within these days) — three scenarios are excluded: first, a missed prayer outside these days; second, a missed prayer in other than these days; third, a missed prayer that he makes up on these days in the following year. In this last scenario, there is a difference of opinion from Abu Yusuf, and the sahih is that there is no takbir for it. His statement: (and they are eight) — the pronoun refers to the obligatory prayers. His statement: (and two) — perhaps it is understood as referring to individuals, otherwise congregation is established by two in other than Friday. But in this sense, it returns to the individual because each is an individual, and two is not considered a congregation, considering the apparent meaning of the word. His statement: (excluded by it are women's congregation) — and also naked persons. His statement: (upon a resident Imam) — he is an Imam who has made the town his homeland, or has intended to stay fifteen days in it. As for one who intends to stay less than that, it is not obligatory. From whoever follows him, i.e., the resident Imam, even if the follower is a traveler, a slave, or a woman, following the Imam. The woman lowers her voice unlike men because it is 'awrah. The latecomer should say takbir because he is a follower in the tahrimah, so he says takbir after finishing. If he follows the Imam forgetfully, his prayer is not invalidated, but in talbiyah it is invalidated. The one in ihram begins with takbir, then with talbiyah. Takbir does not require taharah. The takbir of the Imam according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) due to what we have narrated. And the two (i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: (it is obligatory) to say the takbir immediately after every fard prayer upon whoever prays it, even if he is alone or a traveler or a villager, because it is a follower of the obligatory prayer from the Fajr of Arafa until the late Asr of the fifth day from the day of Arafa, so it is to the end of the days of Tashriq. And it is by their (i.e., the two's) view that practice is done and the fatwa is upon, because it is caution: doing that which is not required is better than leaving that which is said to be required, as understood from his words. His statement: (i.e., the resident Imam is the most correct. And it was said: it is obligatory upon the resident who follows the traveler, and the author of al-Durr acted upon it, as reported by al-Sayyid. His statement: (or a slave) — it would have been better to omit it as was done in al-Tanwir, because it suggests a difference, and there is no difference in it. His statement: (the woman lowers her voice) such that she hears herself, and the reasoning indicates obligation. His statement: (because it is 'awrah) — this is not relied upon; the correct view is that it leads to fitnah, as reported by al-Sayyid. It has preceded. The meaning of 'awrah is its linguistic meaning, which is defect. His statement: (and in talbiyah, it invalidates because it is extraneous speech. In al-Bahr and al-Kafi: he begins with sajdat al-sahw due to its obligation in the tahrimah, then with takbir due to its obligation in its sanctity, then with talbiyah if he is in ihram due to the lack of both. If he begins with it, the sujood and takbir are lost because it is speech that cuts the connection. If he begins with takbir, he makes sujood because it does not conflict with the prayer, unlike talbiyah. His statement: (and takbir al-Imam) is in the genitive, coordinated with 'taharah'. His statement: 'due to what we have narrated' — i.e., from the athar of Ibn Mas'ud mentioned earlier, but it only indicates the condition of congregation, so it is more specific than the claim. The Imam has other evidences for what he saw. His statement: 'to the end of the days of Tashriq' — he should have omitted it and sufficed with what came before, because it suggests that he says takbir after Maghrib since it is the last of these days, so consider. His statement: 'and by it practice is done and the fatwa is upon' — this is based on the principle that when the Imam and his two companions differ, the weight is given to the stronger evidence, as in the end of al-Hawi al-Qudsi; or it is based on their statement in every issue is narrated from him, as mentioned in al-Hawi as well; otherwise, how can fatwa be given by the view of other than the school's founder? So in al-Bahr. He said: by this, what is in al-Fath regarding preponderance of his (Abu Hanifa's) view is refuted, and the fatwa of the mashayikh on the view of the two was rejected. And if the Imam forgets the takbir, the ma'mum performs it obligatorily, like one who hears the ayah of sajdah with its reciter. Muhammad said: Ya'qub said: I led them in Maghrib on the day of Arafa and I forgot to say the takbir, so Abu Hanifa said it. Ya'qub is the name of Abu Yusuf al-Qadi, the companion of the Imam al-A'zam. He is Ya'qub bin Ibrahim bin Habib bin Sa'd bin Habta al-Bajali. Sa'd was considered too young on the day of Uhud. He settled in Kufa and died there. Zaid bin Arqam led his funeral prayer and said takbir five times. Abu Yusuf died in the year 182 AH during the caliphate of Harun al-Rashid. This story includes among its legal benefits this issue; and among its ethical benefits, the great status of Abu Yusuf in the Imam's view where he gave him precedence, and the greatness of the Imam's stature in his heart where he forgot what typically is not forgotten, because he knew that he (Abu Hanifa) would correct him.
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah is a critical refinement explaining the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the takbir al-tashriq (the takbir said after obligatory prayers during the days of tashriq: 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah). The author opens by clarifying the legal basis: the Qur'anic verse 'Remember Allah during the appointed days' (2:203) is not qati' al-dalala, so it indicates wujub (obligation) but not fard (necessity), and the continuous practice of the Prophet and the Companions confirms this. The timing of the takbir follows Ibn Mas'ud's view: from Fajr of the day of Arafa (9th) to Asr of the last day of tashriq. Others (Malik, al-Shafi'i, and a narration from Abu Yusuf) start after Zuhr of the first day of Nahr (10th). The takbir is said immediately after each fard prayer, including its qada within those days, but not if made up in other months; it requires consecutiveness and no interruption that breaks the prayer's sanctity. The core dispute is about who must perform it: Abu Hanifa restricts it to the imam of a congregational prayer in a metropolitan city (misr) who is a resident, and those following him even if they are travelers, slaves, or women, but individual (munfarid) and village dwellers are not required. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is obligatory on everyone who prays any fard prayer, even alone or traveling, from Fajr of Arafa to Asr of the fourth day (i.e., end of tashriq). The fatwa is on their view due to caution (ihtiyat). The text then discusses details: women lower their voice, the latecomer says takbir after finishing, following the imam forgetfully does not invalidate the prayer, and the order between sajdat al-sahw, takbir, and talbiyah. The story of Abu Yusuf forgetting the takbir and Abu Hanifa reminding him illustrates the practice.

Key Terms
التكبير أيام التشريق (al-takbir ayyam al-tashriq): The takbir recited after every obligatory prayer from Fajr of the day of Arafa until Asr of the last day of Tashriq.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, following the day of Nahr (10th).
فور (fawran): Immediately after the prayer, without a gap that breaks the sanctity of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, who must perform the takbir al-tashriq?
A) Only the imam leading a congregational prayer in a city
B) Every person who prays a fard prayer during the days of Tashriq, even if alone
C) Only those who are on Hajj
D) Only men, not women

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-tashriq is wajib on every person who prays a fard prayer during the days of tashriq; the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view, making it a widespread obligation.

Takbir al-Tashriq: Wajib or Sunnah? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the ruling on takbir al-tashriq and the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on takbir al-tashriq and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, including the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Takbir al-tashriq is wajib after every fard prayer from Fajr of Arafa to Asr of 13th Dhul Hijjah according to the Sahibayn; fatwa is on their view.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the ruling on takbir al-tashriq, a set of takbirs recited after fard prayers during Hajj days. There is a disagreement within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Hanifa considered it sunnah, but his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, held it is wajib. The hashya explains why the fatwa is given on the Sahibayn's view, citing caution and evidence from the Quran. Understanding this dispute teaches you how later Hanafi scholars resolve ikhtilaf and determine the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is takbir al-tashriq? When is it performed? According to the mufta bihi, what is its legal classification?
The passage states it is recited after every fard prayer from Fajr of Arafa to Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
What did Abu Hanifa say? What did the Sahibayn say? Note that the dispute is within the same madhhab.
Abu Hanifa: sunnah. Sahibayn: wajib.
3
Examine the proof of the Sahibayn
How do the Sahibayn use the Quranic verses (ayyam ma'lumat and ma'dudat) to argue for obligation?
They interpret the command to remember Allah as specifically referring to takbir, and the imperative indicates wujub in Hanafi usul.
4
Explore the tarjih mechanism
Why is the fatwa on the Sahibayn's view? What reasoning does the hashya provide?
Due to caution (ihtiyat) and because doing what is not required is better than leaving what may be required.
5
Determine the practical difference
What is the thamarah al-khilaf? If one misses the takbir, what is the consequence according to each view?
According to Abu Hanifa: no sin; according to Sahibayn: leaving a wajib, so one should make it up.

Whoever follows him (the imam) meaning the resident imam, even if the follower is a traveler, a slave, or a woman, follows the imam. The woman lowers her voice unlike men because it is 'awrah. The latecomer (masbuq) must say takbir because he follows the imam, so he says takbir after finishing. If he follows the imam forgetfully, his prayer is not invalidated, but in talbiyah it invalidates. The muhrim begins with takbir, then talbiyah, and takbir does not require purity. The takbir of the imam (according to Abu Hanifa) based on what we narrated, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The takbir is obligatory immediately after every fard prayer on whoever prays it, even if he is alone, a traveler, or a villager, because it follows the prescribed prayer, from the Fajr of Arafa until after Asr on the fifth day after Arafa, i.e., except the last days of Tashriq. And acting on their saying is the fatwa, because it is caution: doing what is not required is better than leaving what is said to be required, as understood from his words...
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi discusses the ruling of takbir al-tashriq, which is recited after every fard prayer from Fajr of Arafa (9th Dhul Hijjah) until Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah. The central issue is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that this takbir is sunnah (not wajib), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it is wajib. The hashya clarifies that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view, due to caution and the strength of their evidence. The passage also addresses related rulings: the woman lowering her voice in prayer (not because her voice is 'awrah, as that is unreliable, but due to fitnah), the masbuq's takbir, and the case where the imam forgets the takbir—then the follower must do it. The story of Abu Yusuf forgetting the takbir on the day of Arafa, and Abu Hanifa reminding him by saying it, illustrates the importance of the imam's role and the principle that obedience to the imam takes precedence over perceived etiquette. The hashya then delves into the Quranic verses about 'information days' (ayyam ma'lumat) and 'counted days' (ayyam ma'dudat), identifying them with the days of Hajj and Tashriq, and explains that the prescribed remembrance is specifically the takbir.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The takbirs recited after every fard prayer from Fajr of Arafa (9th Dhul Hijjah) until Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah
الأيام المعلومات (al-ayyam al-ma'lumat): The first ten days of Dhul Hijjah, up to and including the Day of Sacrifice (10th)
الأيام المعدودات (al-ayyam al-ma'dudat): The three days of Tashriq: 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on takbir al-tashriq after every fard prayer?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is mustahab.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-tashriq is wajib after every fard prayer from Fajr of Arafa to Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah, based on the Sahibayn's view which is the operative position for fatwa.

The Formula and Timing of Takbir on Eid and Tashriq: Hanafi View
Explaining the Hanafi formula of takbir and its evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi formula of takbir for Eid and Tashriq, identify the evidence, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The Hanafi takbir of Tashriq consists of two 'Allahu Akbar's based on prophetic hadith and companion practice, not three.

This lesson examines the ruling and formula of the takbir performed after Eid prayers and during the days of Tashriq, as presented in al-Tahtawi's hashya. You will learn the precise wording, the evidence from hadith and companion practice, and how the Hanafi school defends its position against the Shafi'i view of three takbirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The takbir after Eid and during Tashriq is a sunnah muakkadah (strongly recommended), not wajib. It is performed after every fard prayer from Fajr of Arafah to Asr of the day of sacrifice, as well as in markets and public places.
The ruling is based on the command to remember Allah in the 'known' and 'counted' days.
2
Learn the formula
The prescribed formula is: 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillah al-hamd.' This includes two 'Allahu Akbar' phrases, not three.
Additional phrases may be added, but the core is two takbirs.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) on the Day of Arafah, where he said: 'The best of what we said and what the prophets before us said on this day is: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillah al-hamd.' This is supported by the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and other Companions.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for a sunnah ruling.
4
Understand the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the takbir should be said three times. The Hanafi school responds that the textual and practical evidence clearly shows two takbirs; making them three is not established in the authentic narrations.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate (mukhtalaf fih), but the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Note the tarjih
The Hanafi position is preferred because the hadith specifies two takbirs, and the practice of the Companions (e.g., Ibn Mas'ud) confirms this. The commentator al-Tahtawi endorses this view.
The tarjih authority is from the later Hanafi tradition (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

بقوله : لأن المعلومات الخ لا يناسبه لأن الأوسطين العاشر والحادي عشر، وأما الثاني عشر فليس من المعلومات، بل هو من المعدودات، وأما الحادي عشر والثاني عشر فكلاهما ليس من المعلومات، فالنسخ التي حذف منها المعدودات أما الأول فلأنه لا ينحر فيه وأما الثاني فلأنه ليس من أيام التشريق، اللهم إلا إذا أريد بها ما يقع فيها تكبير التشريق، فيكون من المعدودات. قوله : واليومان الأوسطان الخ) بل ثلاثة معلومة، ومعدودة وهي أيام النحر، أما الرابع فمعدود فقط، وأما إذا أريد بأيام التشريق الأيام الثلاثة التي بعد أيام النحر فالمراد بالأول معلوم، والأوسطان الحادي عشر والثاني عشر معلومان ومعدودان والأخير معدود لا غير وهو المتبادر. قوله : ولا بأس بالتكبير عقب صلاة العيدين الخ في الظهيرية عن الفقيه أبي جعفر قال : سمعت أن مشايخنا كانوا يرون التكبير في الأسواق في أيام العشر كما في البحر يوم النحر، وهو لتوارث المسلمين ذلك وكذا في الأسواق، وغيرها (والتكبير ) هو (أن يقول الله أكبر الله أكبر) فهما مرتان (لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر الله أكبر ولله (الحمد لما روي أنه صلى صلاة رفة ثم أقبل على أصحابه بوجهه فقال : خير ما قلنا وقالت الأنبياء قبلنا في يومنا هذا يوم عرفة : الله أكبر الله أكبر لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر الله أكبر ولله الحمد ومن جعل التكبيرات في الأول لاثبت له ويزيد على هذا إن شاء فيقول : (الله أكبر كبيرا والحمد لله كثيراً وسبحان الله بكرة وأصيلاً لا إله إلا الله وحده صدق وعده ونصر عبده وأعز جنده وهزم الأحزاب وحده لا إله إلا الله ولا نعبد إلا إياه مخلصين له الدين ولو كره الكافرون اللهم ثلاثاً ست.، وفي الدراية عن جمع التفاريق قيل لأبي حنيفة : ينبغي لأهل الكوفة، وغيرها أن يكبروا أيام التشريق في المساجد والأسواق قال: نعم، وذكر أبو الليث كان إبراهيم بن يوسف يفتي بالتكبير في الأسواق أيام العشر .اهـ. قوله : (فهما) (مرتان وكذا التكبير الآتي مثله فالجمل فيه قوله: (لما روى (الخ الدليل أخص من المدعي لتقييده بقوله في يومنا هذا، والأولى الاستدلال بما رواه ابن أبي شيبة بسند جيد عن الأسود. قال: كان عبدالله يعني ابن مسعود يكبر من صلاة الفجر يوم عرفة إلى صلاة العصر من يوم النحر يقول الله أكبر الخ، وكذا روى عن علي، بل عن الصحابة كلهم لما رواه ابن أبي شيبة حدثنا جرير عن منصور عن ابراهيم قال : كانوا يكبرون يوم عرفة، وأحدهم مستقبل القبلة في دبر الصلاة الله أكبر الخ. قوله: (ومن جعل التكبيرات ثلاثاً (الخ أشار به إلى من قال بذلك كالشافعي رضي الله عنه. قوله : (ويزيد على هذا الخ) ربما يفيد التعبير بعلى أنه لا يزيد في الصيغة المتقدمة كان يجعل التكبير ثلاثاً وإنما يزيد عليها ويدل عليه قوله : فيقول الخ. قوله : (كبيراً) حال مؤكدة. قوله : (كثيراً) صفة لمصدر محذوف أي حمداً كثيراً أي أثنى على الله تعالى، وأذكره بخير ذكراً كثيراً . قوله : (بكرة وأصيلاً) البكرة أول النهار والأصيل آخره والمقصود الاعتراف بالتنزيه الله تعالى في جميع الأوقات وهما منصوبان على الظرفية. قوله: (وحده) حال لازمة قوله : ( ونصر عبده محمدا عطف تفسير على قوله صدق وعده، ويدل عليه ما روى من قوله في غزوة بدر : اللهم انجز لي ما وعدتني، أو خاص أن أريد بالأول الاعتراف بأن كل ما وعد به الحق تعالى صدق قوله : ( وأعز جنده) المسلمين إلا أن الغالبون، أو المراد الصحابة في مغازيهم . حزب الله هم . قوله : ( وهزم الأحزاب وحده في وقعة الخندق فإنهم هزموا من غير محاربة فتمحض الهزم الله تعالى من غير مشاهدة سبب أو المراد الهزم مطلقاً، فإن الفعل الله وحده والمشاهد من الأسباب أمور عادية قوله مخلصين له الدين) أي الطاعة. قوله: (ولو كره الكافرون) الواو للحال .
Due to the command to remember Allah in the known days and the counted days, and not finding any remembrance except the takbirs in the days of Tashriq and the two middle days from them being from the known and counted, because the known are the ten of Dhul Hijjah and the counted are the days of Tashriq. It was said: the known are the days of sacrifice and the counted are so named due to their fewness. Thus it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he said: The first day is from the known, and the two middle days are from the known and the counted. And there is no harm in saying takbir after the Eid prayers. (As in Mabsut of Abu al-Layth) after him, and that is because the habit is only forgetfulness of the first takbir, which occurs after Fajr on the day of Arafah. As for three consecutive times in which one says takbir, that is not so. His statement: (Because doing what is not upon it, etc.) And because it involves taking the majority in acts of worship, especially in remembrance which is commanded to be abundant. This is in response to what Imam mentioned that consensus was reached on the minimum. His statement: (For the command to remember Allah, etc.) is a cause for his statement that it is upon him. And in the commentary, 'and for the command to it', so it is a conjunction on his statement 'because doing, etc.'. His statement: (In the known days) which is His statement: 'And they mention the name of Allah on known days' [Al-Baqarah: 2]. His statement: (And the counted days) which is His statement: 'And remember Allah on counted days'. His statement: (And the lack of) is in the genitive, conjunction on what is governed by the lam, and it is an answer to a question as if it was said to him: Why did you not carry it to other than this takbir? The gist of the answer is that the commanded remembrance is something occurring in these days, and nothing occurs in them except it. His statement: (And the two middle days, etc.) This is found in some copies, but the reasoning by saying 'because the known, etc.' does not befit it, because the two middle are the tenth and eleventh, and as for the twelfth, it is not from the known, but from the counted. And as for the eleventh and twelfth, both are not from the known. So the copies that deleted this expression are correct. His statement: (That he said) is a substitute for the pronoun 'he narrated', but it does not meet it in meaning, and it is better to make it a causative without the lam. His statement: (The first day from the known) if he meant the day of Arafah, then it is not from the known, nor from the counted. As for the first, because no sacrifice is performed on it. As for the second, because it is not from the days of Tashriq, unless what is intended is that in which takbir of Tashriq occurs, then it is from the counted. His statement: (And the two middle days, etc.) Rather, three are known and counted, and they are the days of sacrifice. As for the fourth, it is only counted. And if the days of Tashriq are meant to be the three days after the days of sacrifice, then the first is known, the two middle (eleventh and twelfth) are known and counted, and the last is only counted, which is the apparent meaning. His statement: (And there is no harm in saying takbir after the Eid prayers) in al-Zahiriyyah from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far, he said: I heard that our mashayikh used to see takbir in the markets during the ten days, as in al-Bahr on the day of sacrifice, and it is due to the continuous practice of Muslims. Similarly in markets and elsewhere. And the takbir is that one says: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, so they are two times. La ilaha illa Allah wa Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar wa lillah al-hamd. Because it is narrated that he prayed a prayer, then turned to his companions with his face and said: The best of what we said and what the prophets before us said on this day, the Day of Arafah: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illa Allah wa Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar wa lillah al-hamd. And whoever makes the takbirs at the beginning three, it is not established for him. And he may add to this if he wishes, and say: Allahu Akbaru kabeeran, wa alhamdu lillahi katheeran, wa subhanallahi bukratan wa aseelan, la ilaha illa Allahu wahdahu, sadaqa wa'dahu, wa nasara 'abdahu, wa a'azza jundahu, wa hazama al-ahzaba wahdahu, la ilaha illa Allahu wa la na'budu illa iyyahu, mukhliseena lahu al-deena wa law kariha al-kafiroon. Allahumma... three, six. And in al-Dirayah from Jami' al-Tafariq, it was said to Abu Hanifah: Should the people of Kufa and others say takbir during the days of Tashriq in the mosques and markets? He said: Yes. And Abu al-Layth mentioned: Ibrahim ibn Yusuf used to give fatwa for takbir in the markets during the ten days. End. His statement: (Thus they are) (two times) and likewise the takbir that follows is like it. So the total in it is... His statement: (Because it is narrated) the evidence is more specific than the claim due to its restriction by his saying 'on this day of ours'. It is better to use the evidence narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah with a good chain from al-Aswad, who said: 'Abdullah, meaning Ibn Mas'ud, used to say takbir from Fajr on the day of Arafah to Asr on the day of sacrifice, saying Allahu Akbar, etc. Similarly narrated from 'Ali, rather from all the Companions. As narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah: Jarir narrated to us from Mansur from Ibrahim, who said: They used to say takbir on the day of Arafah, one of them facing the Qibla after the prayer: Allahu Akbar, etc. His statement: (And whoever makes the takbirs three) he indicated by this to one who said that, like al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him. His statement: (And he may add to this) perhaps the expression 'to' indicates that he does not add to the previous formula, making the takbir three, but rather he adds to it, and his statement 'he says, etc.' indicates that. His statement: (Kabeeran) is an emphatic circumstantial accusative. His statement: (Katheeran) is an adjective for an omitted source noun, i.e., much praise, meaning he praised Allah and remembered Him with much good. His statement: (Bukratan wa aseelan) bukra is the beginning of the day and aseel is the end of it, and the purpose is acknowledgment of Allah's transcendence at all times, and both are accusative as adverbs of time. His statement: (Wahdahu) is a permanent circumstantial accusative. His statement: (And He helped His servant Muhammad) is an explanatory conjunction to 'He fulfilled His promise', and it is supported by what is narrated of his saying in the battle of Badr: O Allah, fulfill for me what You promised me. Or it is specific that by the first I mean acknowledgment that everything promised by Allah is true. His statement: (And He strengthened His army) the Muslims, except that the victorious ones... or it means the companions in their battles. The party of Allah are they. His statement: (And He defeated the parties alone) in the battle of the Trench, for they were defeated without fighting, so the defeat was purely from Allah without visible cause. Or it means defeat in general, for the action is Allah's alone, and the seen causes are customary matters. His statement: (Mukhliseena lahu al-deen) means obedience. His statement: (Wa law kariha al-kafiroon) the waw is for the circumstantial clause.
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on Maraqi al-Falah discussing the ruling and formula of takbir during the days of Tashriq and after Eid prayers. The author, Allamah al-Tahtawi, explains that the takbir is performed in pairs: 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar' followed by 'La ilaha illa Allah wa Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar wa lillah al-hamd'. This is based on a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) on the Day of Arafah, and the practice of the Companions as narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah. The Hanafi position is that the takbir is said twice, not three times as held by Imam al-Shafi'i. The author defends this by noting that the hadith specifies two takbirs and that the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and others confirms this. Additionally, the takbir is recommended after every fard prayer from Fajr of Arafah until Asr of the day of sacrifice, and it is also performed in markets and public places. The commentary also clarifies the distinction between the 'known days' (ayyam ma'lumat) and the 'counted days' (ayyam ma'dudat), identifying the known as the ten of Dhul Hijjah (or specifically the day of sacrifice) and the counted as the days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th). The author resolves textual discrepancies regarding the classification of the middle days.

Key Terms
التكبير (al-takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' as a form of glorifying Allah, especially on specified occasions like Eid and the days of Tashriq.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following the day of sacrifice: 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, during which takbir is recommended.
المعلومات (al-ma'lumat): The 'known days'—according to the author, they refer to the ten days of Dhul Hijjah or specifically the day of sacrifice (10th).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many times is the phrase 'Allahu Akbar' repeated in the prescribed takbir of Tashriq?
A) Once
B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Four times

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes two takbirs in the Tashriq takbir, based on explicit prophetic hadith and companion practice, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i three.

The Wording and Number of 'Eid Takbir: Hanafi Proof for Two
Ruling on the wording and place of takbir with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number and wording of 'Eid takbir, identify the hadith proof, and respond to the Shafi'i objection that it should be three.

Core Idea
The 'Eid takbir is two 'Allahu Akbars' followed by tahlil, not three — the prophetic wording is decisive.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the exact wording and number of takbirs for 'Eid and the days of Tashriq. The Hanafi school holds that the takbir is said twice, based on a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) taught this specific wording. The passage also refutes the view that it should be three times, providing a clear critical refinement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that 'Eid takbir is a wajib act, and its wording is defined by the text.
The ruling is not fard but wajib, based on the strength of proof.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited as evidence: the Prophet (ﷺ) after prayer taught the specific wording.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is qati' (clear).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit wording 'الله أكبر الله أكبر' indicates two takbirs, not three.
The phrase 'فهما مرتان' confirms they are two.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that takbir is three times; the text states that has no proof.
This is an inter-madhhab dispute with practical consequences.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi because of stronger evidence: prophetic wording and Companion practice.
Al-Tahtawi supports this with reference to Majma' al-Riwayat.

لتوارث المسلمين ذلك وكذا في الأسواق، وغيرها (والتكبير ) هو (أن يقول الله أكبر الله أكبر) فهما مرتان (لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر الله أكبر ولله (الحمد لما روي أنه صلى صلاة رفة ثم أقبل على أصحابه بوجهه فقال : خير ما قلنا وقالت الأنبياء قبلنا في يومنا عر يوم هذا : الله أكبر الله أكبر لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر الله أكبر ولله الحمد ومن جعل التكبيرات في الأول لاثبت له ويزيد على هذا إن شاء فيقول : (الله أكبر كبيرا والحمد لله كثيراً وسبحان الله بكرة وأصيلاً لا إله إلا الله وحده صدق وعده ونصر عبده وأعز جنده وهزم الأحزاب وحده لا إله إلا الله ولا نعبد إلا إياه مخلصين له الدين ولو كره الكافرون اللهم صل على محمد وعلى آل محمد وعلى أصحاب محمد وعلى أزواج محمد وسلم تسليماً كذا في مجمع الروايات شرح القدوري.
Due to Muslims inheriting that, and likewise in the markets and other places. And the takbir is that he says 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar' - these are two times - 'La ilaha illa Allah, wa Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillahi al-hamd.' Because it was narrated that he (ﷺ) prayed a prayer and then turned to his companions and said: 'The best of what we have said and the prophets before us said on this day of ours is: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, wa Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillahi al-hamd.' Whoever makes the takbir three times in the first has no proof for it. He may add to this if he wishes and say: 'Allahu Akbar kabiran, wa alhamdu lillahi kathiran, wa subhana Allahi bukratan wa asilan, la ilaha illa Allahu wahdahu, sadaqa wa'dahu, wa nasara 'abdahu, wa a'azza jundahu, wa hazama al-ahzaba wahdahu, la ilaha illa Allahu wa la na'budu illa iyyahu, mukhlisina lahu al-dina wa law kariha al-kafirun. Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammadin wa 'ala ali Muhammadin wa 'ala ashabi Muhammadin wa 'ala azwaji Muhammadin wa sallim tasliman.' As in Majma' al-Riwayat Sharh al-Quduri.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the takbir of 'Eid and the days of Tashriq. It states that the takbir is to be said twice (الله أكبر الله أكبر) followed by the tahlil, not three times. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) after prayer taught this wording. The commentary refines that the hadith specifically mentions 'on this day of ours', but there is also stronger evidence from the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and other Companions who said takbir from Fajr of 'Arafah to 'Asr of the Day of Nahr. The commentator also notes that the Shafi'i school makes it three takbirs, but this has no proof in the Hanafi view. Additional wording may be added, as given in the text.

Key Terms
التكبير (al-takbir): Uttering 'Allahu Akbar' on specified occasions such as 'Eid and days of Tashriq.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following the Day of Nahr (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhu al-Hijjah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The 'Eid takbir is wajib with two 'Allahu Akbar's followed by tahlil, as established by the Prophet's (ﷺ) wording.

Ruling on Eclipse Prayer (Salat al-Kusuf) in the Hanafi School
Ruling on eclipse prayer being sunnah with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salat al-kusuf, identify its proof from the hadith, and distinguish it from other schools' positions regarding extra bowings.

Core Idea
The eclipse prayer is a two-rak'ah sunnah performed like regular nafl, without extra bowings.

The eclipse prayer is a confirmed sunnah in the Hanafi school. Unlike some other schools, it is performed exactly like a supererogatory prayer—two rak'ahs with a single bowing in each—and the Prophet's command to 'pray like the most recent obligatory prayer' is interpreted as the Fajr prayer. In this lesson, we examine the ruling, its proof, and the key differences from other madhahib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that the eclipse prayer is sunnah, two rak'ahs, like nafl, with no extra bowings. Determine the hukm level (sunnah muakkadah) from the source.
The matn says 'سن ركعتان كهيئة النفل'.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the hadith narrated by al-Kamal, where the Prophet (ﷺ) commands prayer upon seeing an eclipse. Quote the hadith and classify its transmission (zanni al-thubut).
Hadith: 'فإذا رأيتم ذلك فصلوا...'
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fasallu' indicates prescription. However, Hanafi usul applies the principle that a command does not automatically denote obligation (wujub) when context shows the act is sunnah. Here, the phrase 'كأحدث صلاة صليتموها' points to the Fajr prayer (two rak'ahs, one bowing each), confirming the nafl-like form.
The word 'أحدث' means 'most recent', referring to Fajr.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Hanbali) consider it wajib; others (e.g., Shafi'i) perform two bowings per rak'ah. The Hanafi response is that the hadith explicitly says 'like the most recent obligatory prayer', which is Fajr (two rak'ahs, one bowing each), thus rejecting extra bowings.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi: sunnah muakkadah.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis perform one ruku' per rak'ah; Shafi'is perform two. Also, Hanafis do not consider it wajib, so if missed, no compensation is required.

باب صلاة الكسوف والخسوف والإفزاع (سن ركعتان كهيئة النفل للكسوف من غير زيادة فلا يركع ركوعين كل قوله: (اللهم صل على محمد المندوب السيادة كما قالوا في الصلاة. قوله: (وعلى آل محمد) المراد بهم مطلق الاتباع وعطف الأصحاب من عطف الخاص للاهتمام بسبب الشرف. تتمة : ذكر في الكشاف أن الخليل لما أراد الذبح ونزل جبريل بالفداء خاف عليه العجلة، فنادى من الهواء الله أكبر الله أكبر الله أكبر فسمعه الذبيح فقال : لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر، فقال الخليل الله أكبر ولله الحمد اهـ لكن لم يثبت ذلك عند أهل الحديث، والمختار أن الذبيح اسمعيل عليه السلام وفي القاموس أنه الأصح . قال : ومعناه مطيع الله در والمسألة خلافية سلفاً، وخلفاً فمنهم من قال به، ومنهم قال : بأنه اسحق عليه السلام قال في البحر والحنفية ماثلون إلى الأول، والحاصل كما قال السيوطي أن الخلاف فيه مشهور بين الصحابة فمن بعدهم ورجح كل من القولين كما في الزرقاني على المواهب والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم. مخصوصة من غير باب صلاة الكسوف ذكر هذا الباب بعد صلاة العيد وقبل الاستسقاء لأن كلاً منهما صلاة نهارية بجماعة أذان ولا إقامة إلا أنّ صلاة العيد واجبة وقيل فرض كفاية، وصلاة الكسوف سنة عند الجمهور وقيل واجبة وصلاة الاستسقاء مختلف في سنيتها، فناسب ترتيب الأبواب كذا في الفتح يقال : كسف الله الشمس كسفاً من باب ضرب، فهو معتد، وكسفت الشمس كسوفاً من باب جلس فهو لازم، وما قيل في الكسوف يقال في الخسوف، وهما بمعنى واحد وهو ذهاب الضوء من كل منهما قاله ابن فارس والأزهري، والجوهري وزاد في القاموس الخسوف ذهاب بعضهما والكسوف ذهاب كلهما، والإضافة في صلاة الكسوف للتعريف وهي من إضافة الشيء إلى سببه لأن سببها الكسوف روى الكمال أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: إنّ أناساً يزعمون أن الشمس والقمر لا ينكسفان إلا لموت عظيم من العظماء، وليس كذلك إن الشمس والقمر لا ينكسفان لموت أحد ولا لحياته، ولكنهما آيتان من آيات الله إنّ الله إذا بدا لشيء من خلقه خشع له فإذا رأيتم ذلك فصلوا كأحدث صلاة صليتموها من المكتوبة) اهـ والمراد بالأحدث الأقرب، وكانت الصبح فإن الكسوف كان عند
Chapter of prayer of solar and lunar eclipse and [prayer of] fright. Two rak'ahs are sunnah, like supererogatory prayer, for the eclipse, without increase, so one does not bow two bowings each...
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on eclipse prayer. The matn states that the eclipse prayer is two rak'ahs, performed like supererogatory prayer (nafl), without any increase such as two bowings per rak'ah (which is the practice of some other schools). The commentary explains that the chapter is placed after 'Eid prayer because both are daytime congregational prayers without adhan or iqamah, though 'Eid prayer is wajib, eclipse prayer is sunnah according to the majority, and istisqa' is disputed. The passage also defines the linguistic difference between kusuf and khusuf: according to some, khusuf is partial loss and kusuf is total, though they are often used synonymously. A hadith is cited where the Prophet (ﷺ) refutes the pre-Islamic belief that eclipses occur due to the death of a great person, and instead instructs to pray like the most recent obligatory prayer, which is interpreted as the Fajr prayer because the eclipse occurred at that time.

Key Terms
الكسوف (al-kusuf): The obscuration of the sun's light, either partially or totally.
صلاة الكسوف (salat al-kusuf): A two-rak'ah prayer performed during a solar or lunar eclipse, like nafl without extra bowing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is the eclipse prayer performed?
A) With two bowings in each rak'ah
B) Like a regular supererogatory prayer with one bowing per rak'ah
C) With four prostrations
D) In congregation with audible recitation

Key Takeaway
The eclipse prayer is a sunnah muakkadah performed like nafl with one bowing per rak'ah, based on the hadith commanding prayer like the most recent obligatory prayer (Fajr).

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Rulings of Salat al-Kusuf (Eclipse Prayer) in the Hanafi School
Commentary on the rulings and proofs for eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Kusuf, explain the evidence for one ruku per rak'ah, and distinguish the Hanafi position on recitation and congregation from other schools.

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer is a sunnah muakkadah with one ruku per rak'ah, based on multiple hadiths and analogy with obligatory prayers.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi school's rulings on the eclipse prayer (Salat al-Kusuf) as explained by al-Tahtawi. We will see why the school holds it is sunnah muakkadah, how the evidence supports one ruku per rak'ah, and the specific procedures: silent recitation, no call to prayer, no sermon, and congregation restricted to the Friday imam or sultan's deputy. We will also address the internal disagreement on audible recitation and the external disagreement with other schools on the number of rukus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hukm Level
Determine why eclipse prayer is classified as sunnah muakkadah (not wajib or fard). Note the textual clue 'سن' indicating sunnah, and the emphasis from practice.
The Hanafi school considers it a strongly recommended sunnah, not obligatory.
2
Locate the Dalil
Examine the hadith evidence for the prayer: two rak'ahs with one ruku each, as narrated by Abu Dawud and others. Also note the analogy to the nearest obligatory prayer (Subh).
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but supported by multiple chains.
3
Analyze the Ikhtilaf
Compare the Hanafi position (one ruku per rak'ah) with the Shafi'i/Maliki/Hanbali position (two rukus per rak'ah). Understand each school's evidence.
The opposing schools rely on hadith from Ibn Abbas and Aisha.
4
Derive the Thamarah al-Khilaf
See how the difference in the number of rukus affects the actual performance of the prayer. The Hanafi prayer has two rak'ahs with one ruku each; others have two rukus in each rak'ah.
Practical consequence: differing number of bowings.
5
Apply the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Note the internal disagreement on audible recitation (jahr): Abu Hanifa holds silent, the Sahibayn hold audible. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view due to stronger evidence.
Also note conditions on congregation and place.

وصحة أحاديثه، وموافقته الأصول المعهودة لانا لم نجد في شيء من الصلوات إلا ركوعاً واحداً فيجب أن تكون صلاة الكسوف كذلك. قال الإمام محمد وتأويل ما روى من الركوعين أنه لما أطال الركوع رفع بعض أنه رفع رأسه من الركوع فرفع من خلفهم، فلما رأوا رسول الصفوف رؤسهم .

انصرف، وانجلت الشمس فقال : إنما هذه الآيات يخوف الله تعالى بها عباده فإذا رأيتموها فصلوا كأحدث صلاة صليتموها من المكتوبة قال الكمال وهي الصبح فإن كسوف الشمس كان عند ارتفاعها قيد ،رمحين وفي السنة أنها بركوع واحد في كل ركعة للكسوف، ولا جماعة فيها إلا بإمام الجمعة أو مأمور السلطان دفعاً للفتنة فيصليهما (بلا أذان ولا إقامة ولا جهر) في القراءة فيهما عنده خلافاً لهما (ولا) (خطبة) بإجماع أصحابنا لعدم أمره بالخطبة بل ينادي الصلاة جامعة) ليجتمعوا (وسن تطويلهما) بنحو سورة البقرة قال الكمال : وهذا مستثنى من كراهة تطويل الإمام الصلاة ولو خففها جاز ولا يكون مخالفاً للسنة لأن

كذلك
الله صلى الله عليه وسلم راكعاً ركعوا فركع من خلفهم، فمن كان خلفاً ظن أنه صلى بأكثر من ركوع، فروى على حسب ما عنده من الاشتباه قوله : (بل) ركوع واحد) الأولى ركوعاً واحداً بالنصب. قوله : كأحدث صلاة) أي أقرب صلاة قوله : (وهي) أي أحدث صلاة. قوله : (إلا بإمام الجمعة) أي إمام تصح به إقامة الجمعة، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لا بد لها من شرائط الجمعة، سوى الخطبة كما في السراج، والمعنى في ذلك تحصيل كمال السنة على الظاهر كما في النهر، وفي السيد عن البحر قال العلامة الاسبيجابي يتسحب في كسوف الشمس ثلاثة أشياء الإمام والوقت والموضع أما الإمام ،فالسلطان أو القاضي، ومن له ولاية الجمعة، والعيدين، وأما الوقت فهو الذي يباح فيه التطوع، وأما الموضع فهو الذي يصلي فيه صلاة العيد، أو المسجد الجامع، ولو صلوا في موضع آخر أجزأهم والأول أفضل، ولو صلوا وحدانا في منازلهم جاز ويكره أن يجمع في كل ناحية اهـ يعني لكراهة النفل بجماعة على التداعي إلا ما خص بدليل إلا إذا أذن الإمام لإمام كل مسجد أن يقيمها كما في ابن أمير حاج وفي الظهيرية إذا أمر إمام الجمعة القوم بالصلاة جاز أن يصلوا بالجماعة في مساجدهم يؤمهم فيها إمام حيهم حموي عن البرجندي وفيه أيضاً، وكذا النساء يصلين صلاة الكسوف فرادى . قوله: (عنده خلافاً لهما الصحيح قول الإمام كما في المضمرات لما رواه أصحاب السنن، وصحه الترمذي وابن حبان والحاكم عن سمرة صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في كسوف الشمس لا نسمع له صوتاً وما رواه أحمد عن ابن عباس : صليت مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الكسوف فلم أسمع منه فيها حرفاً، وتأويل ما روياه من الجهر أنه جهر بالآية والآيتين قوله: (ولا خطبة) وخطتبه يوم مات سيدنا إبراهيم ابنه ليست إلا للرد على من توهم أنها كسفت لموته لا أنها مشروعة له، ولذا خطب بعد الانجلاء، ولو كانت سنة له لخطب قبله كالصلاة والدعاء قوله : بل ينادي بالبناء للمفعول قوله : (الصلاة جامعة) بالنصب على الإغراء أي احضر، والصلاة ويصح الرفع فيهما على الابتداء والخبر. قوله : ( بنحو سورة البقرة) المعنى أنه يقرأ في الأولى الفاتحة وسورة البقرة إن كان يحفظها، أو ما يعدلها من غيرها إن لم يحفظها جوهرة. قوله : (ولو خففها الخ) ليس من كلام الكمال، بل ذكر في الفتح ما حاصله إن الحق أن السنة تطويل حاشية الطحطاوي/ م٣٥
Book of Prayer. Rather one rak'ah [with] one bowing because of what Abu Dawud narrated that he (peace be upon him) prayed two rak'ahs and prolonged the standing... [continues]
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah discusses the rulings of Salat al-Kusuf (eclipse prayer). It begins by explaining the wisdom behind the prayer: to refute the Jahili belief that eclipses are caused by celestial bodies. The author then states that the sunnah is two rak'ahs with one ruku each, based on hadith evidence. He addresses the disagreement with Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad, who hold that each rak'ah has two rukus. The Hanafi proof includes multiple hadiths and the principle that all prayers have one ruku per rak'ah. The opposing narration of two rukus is interpreted as a misunderstanding due to prolonged bowing. The passage then details the procedure: no adhan, no iqamah, no jahr (audible recitation) according to Imam Abu Hanifa (contrary to the two disciples), no khutbah, but the call 'al-salatu jamiah' is made. Congregation is only with the imam of Jumu'ah or someone appointed by the sultan to avoid fitna. It is recommended to prolong the prayer like Surah al-Baqarah. The text also discusses the conditions of the imam, time, and place.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse; the sun's light being blocked by the moon.
ركعة (rak'ah): A unit of prayer consisting of standing, bowing, and prostrations.
ركوع (ruku'): Bowing in prayer; an integral (rukn) of prayer.
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation in prayer.
خطبة (khutbah): Sermon delivered after the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The recitation must be audible because the two disciples said so.
B) The recitation is silent, following Abu Hanifa, but if someone recites audibly, it is still valid.
C) The recitation is silent and must not be audible under any circumstances.
D) The recitation is optional; the imam may choose.

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Kusuf is a sunnah muakkadah prayer performed in congregation during a solar eclipse, with two rak'ahs each containing one ruku, silent recitation, no adhan/iqamah, no sermon, and a call 'al-salatu jamiah'.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
15 min
Rulings on Salat al-Kusuf and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Recitation
Explaining the rulings of eclipse prayer, conditions, and the dispute over jahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling and form of the solar eclipse prayer, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation, and identify the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer is sunnah with two rak'ahs, one ruku each; recitation is silent per Abu Hanifa, though the Sahibayn disagreed.

This lesson covers the key rulings of ṣalāt al-kusūf (solar eclipse prayer) as outlined in the Hanafi school, drawing from the commentary of al-Ṭaḥṭāwī. We will examine the legal classification, the conditions for congregation, the recommended acts, and the notable intra-madhhab dispute between Imām Abū Ḥanīfah and his two disciples regarding whether the recitation should be silent (sirr) or aloud (jahr). Understanding this dispute and its resolution is a model of how later Ḥanafī jurists weighed evidence and set the operative position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal ruling
Recognise that the eclipse prayer is not obligatory but a strongly recommended sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah). Note the prophetic instruction to pray 'like the most recent obligatory prayer'.
The ruling is based on the Prophet's practice, not a command of obligation.
2
List the conditions for congregational performance
The prayer is performed in congregation only if led by the Friday imam or a deputy authorised by the ruler. Without such an imam, individuals pray alone at home.
The condition of an imam is to avoid discord (fitna).
3
Describe the form of the prayer
The prayer consists of two rak'ahs with one ruku' each. There is no adhan or iqamah; instead the call is 'al-ṣalātu jāmi'ah'. Recitation should be lengthy (e.g., Sūrat al-Baqarah). Ruku' and sujūd are also prolonged.
No sermon is delivered after the prayer.
4
State the sunnan of the prayer
The recommended acts include lengthening recitation, ruku', and sujūd, supplicating after the prayer, and the congregation saying Āmīn.
The supplication may be done sitting facing qiblah or standing facing the people.
5
Analyse the intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation
Imām Abū Ḥanīfah held that recitation is silent (sirr); Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad held it is aloud (jahr). The relied-upon view is that of Abū Ḥanīfah, supported by hadiths from Samurah and Ibn 'Abbās.
The opposing reports of jahr are interpreted as isolated verses, not the entire prayer.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة
انصرف، وانجلت الشمس فقال : إنما هذه الآيات يخوف الله تعالى بها عباده فإذا رأيتموها فصلوا كأحدث صلاة صليتموها من المكتوبة قال الكمال وهي الصبح فإن كسوف الشمس كان عند ارتفاعها قيد رمحين وفي السنة أنها بركوع واحد في كل ركعة للكسوف، ولا جماعة فيها إلا بإمام الجمعة أو مأمور السلطان دفعاً للفتنة فيصليهما (بلا أذان ولا إقامة ولا جهر) في القراءة فيهما عنده خلافاً لهما (ولا) (خطبة) بإجماع أصحابنا لعدم أمره بالخطبة بل ينادي الصلاة جامعة) ليجتمعوا (وسن تطويلهما) بنحو سورة البقرة قال الكمال : وهذا مستثنى من كراهة تطويل الإمام الصلاة ولو خففها جاز ولا يكون مخالفاً للسنة لأن وهكذا الله صلى الله عليه وسلم راكعاً ركعوا فركع من خلفهم، فمن كان خلفاً ظن أنه صلى بأكثر من ركوع، فروى على حسب ما عنده من الاشتباه قوله : (بل) ركوع واحد) الأولى ركوعاً واحداً بالنصب. قوله : كأحدث صلاة) أي أقرب صلاة قوله : (وهي) أي أحدث صلاة. قوله : (إلا بإمام الجمعة) أي إمام تصح به إقامة الجمعة، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لا بد لها من شرائط الجمعة، سوى الخطبة كما في السراج، والمعنى في ذلك تحصيل كمال السنة على الظاهر كما في النهر، وفي السيد عن البحر قال العلامة الاسبيجابي يتسحب في كسوف الشمس ثلاثة أشياء الإمام والوقت والموضع أما الإمام ،فالسلطان أو القاضي، ومن له ولاية الجمعة، والعيدين، وأما الوقت فهو الذي يباح فيه التطوع، وأما الموضع فهو الذي يصلي فيه صلاة العيد، أو المسجد الجامع، ولو صلوا في موضع آخر أجزأهم والأول أفضل، ولو صلوا وحدانا في منازلهم جاز ويكره أن يجمع في كل ناحية اهـ يعني لكراهة النفل بجماعة على التداعي إلا ما خص بدليل إلا إذا أذن الإمام لإمام كل مسجد أن يقيمها كما في ابن أمير حاج وفي الظهيرية إذا أمر إمام الجمعة القوم بالصلاة جاز أن يصلوا بالجماعة في مساجدهم يؤمهم فيها إمام حيهم حموي عن البرجندي وفيه أيضاً، وكذا النساء يصلين صلاة الكسوف فرادى . قوله: (عنده خلافاً لهما الصحيح قول الإمام كما في المضمرات لما رواه أصحاب السنن، وصحه الترمذي وابن حبان والحاكم عن سمرة صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في كسوف الشمس لا نسمع له صوتاً وما رواه أحمد عن ابن عباس : صليت مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الكسوف فلم أسمع منه فيها حرفاً، وتأويل ما روياه من الجهر أنه جهر بالآية والآيتين قوله: (ولا خطبة) وخطتبه يوم مات سيدنا إبراهيم ابنه ليست إلا للرد على من توهم أنها كسفت لموته لا أنها مشروعة له، ولذا خطب بعد الانجلاء، ولو كانت سنة له لخطب قبله كالصلاة والدعاء قوله : بل ينادي بالبناء للمفعول قوله : (الصلاة جامعة) بالنصب على الإغراء أي احضر، والصلاة ويصح الرفع فيهما على الابتداء والخبر. قوله : ( بنحو سورة البقرة) المعنى أنه يقرأ في الأولى الفاتحة وسورة البقرة إن كان يحفظها، أو ما يعدلها من غيرها إن لم يحفظها جوهرة. قوله : (ولو خففها الخ) ليس من كلام الكمال، بل ذكر في الفتح ما حاصله إن الحق أن السنة تطويل المسنون استيعاب الوقت بالصلاة والدعاء فإذا خفف إحداهما طوّل الأخرى ليبقى على الخشوع، والخوف إلى انجلاء الشمس (و) سن (تطويل ركوعهما وسجودهما) لما روي أن الشمس انكسفت على عهد رسول الله له فقام فلم يكد يركع، ثم ركع فلم يكد يرفع، ثم رفع فلم يكد يسجد ، ثم سجد فلم يكد يرفع وفعل في الركعة الأخرى مثل ذلك أخرجه الحاكم وصححه (ثم يدعو الإمام لأن السنة تأخيره عن الصلاة جالساً مستقبل القبلة إن شاء أو) يدعو (قائماً مستقبل الناس) قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني (وهو أحسن) من استقبال القبلة ولو اعتمد قائماً على عصا أو قوس كان أيضاً حسناً ولا يصعد المنبر للدعاء ولا يخرج (و) إذا دعا (يؤمنون على دعائه ويستمرون كذلك حتى يكمل انجلاء الشمس) كما ورد (وإن لم يحضر الإمام (صلوا أي الناس (فرادى) ركعتين أو أربعاً في منازلهم (كأداء صلاة (الخسوف فرادى لأن القمر خسف مراراً في عهد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولم ينقل إلينا أنه جمع الناس له دفعًا للفتنة وكسوف القمر ذهاب ضوئه والخسوف ذهاب دائرته والحكم أعم (و) كالصلاة فرادى لحصول الظلمة الهائلة نهاراً والريح الشديدة) ليلاً كان أو نهاراً (والفزع) بالزلازل والصواعق وانتشار الكواكب والضوء الهائل ليلاً، والثلج والأمطار
The book of prayer. He turned away and the sun cleared, so he said: 'These signs are only meant by Allah to frighten His servants, so when you see them, pray as the most recent obligatory prayer you prayed.' Al-Kamal said: 'It is the Fajr prayer, for the solar eclipse occurred when the sun was at the height of two spears.' And in the Sunnah, it is with one bowing in each rak'ah for the eclipse. There is no congregation for it except with the imam of Friday or the one appointed by the ruler to avert discord. So they pray them without adhan, without iqama, and without raising the voice in recitation according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Nor a sermon by consensus of our companions due to the lack of command for it. Rather, the caller calls 'al-salatu jami'ah' so they gather. It is sunnah to lengthen them with something like Surah al-Baqarah. Al-Kamal said: 'This is excepted from the disliked lengthening of the imam, and if he shortens it, it is permissible and he would not be opposing the Sunnah.' Because the Prophet, peace be upon him, bowed and those behind him bowed, so one who was behind thought he prayed with more than one bowing, and thus reported according to what he thought due to confusion. His statement: 'rather one bowing' the correct is 'one bowing' in the accusative. His statement: 'like the most recent prayer' meaning the closest prayer. His statement: 'except with the imam of Friday' meaning an imam with whom Friday can be established, indicating that it requires the conditions of Friday except the sermon. And the meaning is to achieve the perfection of the Sunnah apparently. Al-Isbijabi said: 'It is desirable in the solar eclipse three things: the imam, the time, and the place. As for the imam, it is the sultan or judge, or one who has authority over Friday and the two 'Eids. The time is when supererogatory prayer is permissible. The place is where the 'Eid prayer is performed or the congregational mosque. If they pray in another place, it suffices, and the first is better. If they pray individually in their homes, it is permissible, and it is disliked to gather in every locality, because of the dislike of supererogatory prayer with congregation based on mutual call, except what is specified by evidence, unless the imam permits the imam of each mosque to establish it.' In al-Zahiriyyah: 'If the imam of Friday orders the people to pray, it is permissible for them to pray in congregation in their mosques led by the imam of their district.' Also, women pray the eclipse prayer individually. His statement: 'contrary to the two' the correct is the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) as in al-Mudmarat due to the hadith of Samurah: 'The Prophet prayed with us during a solar eclipse and we did not hear his voice.' And the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'I prayed the eclipse with the Prophet and did not hear from him a single letter.' The explanation of the hadith they reported about raising the voice is that he raised his voice in one or two verses. His statement: 'nor a sermon' and his sermon on the day of the death of Ibrahim, his son, was only to refute those who thought it was because of his death, not that it is prescribed for it. Therefore, he gave the sermon after the clearing. If it were sunnah for it, he would have given it before, like the prayer and supplication. His statement: 'rather he calls' is in the passive. His statement: 'al-salatu jami'ah' is in the accusative for urging, meaning 'come to prayer', and raising is also permissible as subject and predicate. His statement: 'with something like Surah al-Baqarah' means he recites al-Fatihah and Surah al-Baqarah in the first if he knows it, or its equivalent if he does not. His statement: 'and if he shortens it' is not from al-Kamal's words. Mentioned in al-Fath that the correct is that the sunnah is to fill the time with prayer and supplication, so if he shortens one, he lengthens the other to maintain humility and fear until the sun clears. It is sunnah to lengthen the bowing and prostration due to the report that the sun eclipsed in the time of the Prophet, and he stood and almost did not bow, then bowed and almost did not raise, then raised and almost did not prostrate, then prostrated and almost did not raise, and did likewise in the other rak'ah. Then the imam supplicates because the sunnah is to delay it after the prayer, sitting facing the qiblah if he wishes, or standing facing the people. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said that standing is better than facing the qiblah. If he leans on a stick or bow while standing, that is also good. He does not ascend the pulpit for supplication, nor does he come out. And when he supplicates, they say 'amin' to his supplication and continue like that until the sun is fully cleared. And if the imam is not present, the people pray individually, two or four rak'ahs in their homes, like performing the lunar eclipse prayer individually, because the moon eclipsed many times in the time of the Prophet and it was not reported that he gathered people for it, to avoid discord. Kusuf of the moon is the loss of its light, and khusuf is the loss of its disc, and the ruling is more general. And like praying individually due to the occurrence of intense darkness during the day and strong wind, night or day, and terror from earthquakes, thunderbolts, falling stars, intense light at night, snow, and rain.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashya discusses the rulings of salat al-kusuf (solar eclipse prayer) and salat al-khusuf (lunar eclipse prayer). It begins by citing the hadith that when the sun eclipsed, the Prophet instructed the people to pray 'the most recent prayer', which al-Kamal identifies as Fajr because the eclipse occurred at the time when the sun was at the height of two spears (after sunrise). The Hanafi position is that the eclipse prayer consists of two rak'ahs, each with one ruku' (bowing), contrary to some reports that suggest two ruku in one rak'ah. The prayer is performed without adhan or iqamah, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the recitation is silent (sirr), while his two disciples (Sahibayn) hold that it is aloud (jahr). The correct position is that of Abu Hanifa, supported by hadiths from Samurah and Ibn Abbas stating that the Prophet's recitation was inaudible. There is no khutbah (sermon) after the prayer, as the sermon on the day of Ibrahim's death was a response to a misunderstanding, not a sunnah. The call to prayer is 'al-salatu jami'ah' (prayer is gathering). It is sunnah to lengthen the prayer with long recitation (e.g., Surah al-Baqarah), and also to lengthen ruku' and sujud. After the prayer, the imam makes supplication, either sitting facing the qiblah or standing facing the people; the latter is considered better. The congregation continues supplicating until the eclipse clears. If the imam is absent, people pray individually at home. The same rulings apply for lunar eclipse, but always individually to avoid fitna (discord) due to nighttime gatherings. The passage also mentions that similar prayers (individual) are offered for other frightening phenomena like darkness, storms, earthquakes, etc.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse (loss of sunlight) – used for the sun's eclipse prayer.
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse (loss of moonlight) – used for the moon's eclipse prayer.
الصلاة جامعة (al-salatu jami'ah): The call to gather for eclipse prayer, instead of adhan or iqamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view regarding recitation in the solar eclipse prayer?
A) Recitation is aloud (jahr) as held by the Sahibayn.
B) Recitation is silent (sirr) as held by Abu Hanifa.
C) Recitation is optional; the imam may choose.
D) Recitation is done only after the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The eclipse prayer is a sunnah performed with specific form, and the Hanafi mufta bihi is silent recitation per Abu Hanifa.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
10 min
Sunnahs of Salat al-Kusuf (Solar Eclipse Prayer)
Lists the recommended acts for solar eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts of the solar eclipse prayer, explain the proof for prolonging ruku' and sujud, and identify the imam's preferred supplication posture according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The eclipse prayer is sunnah muakkadah, and its prescribed acts include prolongation and post-prayer supplication.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi outlines the recommended acts for the solar eclipse prayer. It emphasizes occupying the entire eclipse period with prayer and supplication, prolonging the bowings and prostrations based on a hadith, and specifies the imam's supplication after the prayer. Understanding these sunnah acts ensures the prayer is performed with the prescribed humility and form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
Read the passage and list the actions described as sunnah: occupying time with prayer and supplication, prolonging ruku' and sujud, the imam's supplication, and the congregation's ameen.
2
Locate the proof for prolongation
The text cites a hadith narrated by al-Hakim describing the Prophet's prolonged standing, bowing, and prostrating during an eclipse. This proves the sunnah of prolonging ruku' and sujud.
Hadith is zanni al-thubut (ahad) but sufficient for sunnah.
3
Determine the ruling level
The eclipse prayer and its described acts are classified as sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) in the Hanafi school, not wajib or fard.
Wajib would require a stronger proof; sunnah is inferred from the Prophet's practice.
4
Analyze the imam's supplication
The imam may supplicate sitting facing the qibla or standing facing the congregation. Shams al-A'imma al-Halawani preferred facing the congregation because it allows them to see his humility.
Leaning on a stick or bow while standing is also permissible.
5
Note the exceptions
The imam does not ascend the minbar for supplication, nor does he leave the mosque. The congregation continues supplicating and saying ameen until the sun clears.
These exceptions prevent innovation and maintain focus on prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسنون استيعاب الوقت بالصلاة والدعاء فإذا خفف إحداهما طوّل الأخرى ليبقى على الخشوع، والخوف إلى انجلاء الشمس (و) سن (تطويل ركوعهما وسجودهما) لما روي أن الشمس انكسفت على عهد رسول الله له فقام فلم يكد يركع، ثم ركع فلم يكد يرفع، ثم رفع فلم يكد يسجد ، ثم سجد فلم يكد يرفع وفعل في الركعة الأخرى مثل ذلك أخرجه الحاكم وصححه (ثم يدعو الإمام لأن السنة تأخيره عن الصلاة جالساً مستقبل القبلة إن شاء أو) يدعو (قائماً مستقبل الناس) قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني (وهو أحسن) من استقبال القبلة ولو اعتمد قائماً على عصا أو قوس كان أيضاً حسناً ولا يصعد المنبر للدعاء ولا يخرج (و) إذا دعا (يؤمنون على دعائه ويستمرون كذلك حتى يكمل انجلاء الشمس) كما ورد
The recommended acts are: occupying the time with prayer and supplication, and if one shortens one of them, he lengthens the other to maintain humility and fear until the sun clears. And it is recommended to prolong the bowings and prostrations, based on what is narrated that the sun eclipsed during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he stood and almost did not bow, then he bowed and almost did not raise his head, then he raised and almost did not prostrate, then he prostrated and almost did not raise his head, and he did similarly in the second rak'ah. This was narrated by al-Hakim and he authenticated it. Then the imam supplicates, because the sunnah is to delay it after the prayer, sitting facing the qibla if he wishes, or he supplicates standing facing the people. Shams al-A'imma al-Halawani said: 'And this is better' than facing the qibla. And if while standing he leans on a stick or a bow, that is also good. He does not ascend the minbar for supplication, nor does he go out. And when he supplicates, they say ameen to his supplication, and they continue like that until the sun is completely clear, as reported.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof: it states the sunnah acts of the solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). The commentator explains that the entire time of the eclipse should be spent in prayer and supplication, balancing both. If one shortens the prayer, he lengthens the supplication, and vice versa, to maintain khushu' (humility). The specific sunnah of prolonging ruku' and sujud is supported by a hadith narrated by al-Hakim, describing the Prophet's actions during an eclipse. After the prayer, the imam supplicates. He may sit facing the qibla or stand facing the congregation. According to Shams al-A'imma al-Halawani, standing facing the people is better because it allows the congregation to see his humble state and engage more fully. Leaning on a stick or bow while standing is permissible. The imam does not ascend the minbar, nor does he leave the mosque. The congregation says ameen and continues until the sun is fully uncovered, as the hadith instructs to pray until the eclipse clears.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse; the darkening of the sun.
تطويل (tatwil): Prolongation; specifically in this context, prolonging the ruku' and sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the preferred posture for the imam's supplication after the solar eclipse prayer?
A) Sitting facing the qibla
B) Standing facing the congregation
C) Standing on the minbar
D) Sitting with back to the congregation

Key Takeaway
The solar eclipse prayer is sunnah muakkadah, and its prescribed sunnah acts include prolonging ruku' and sujud, balancing prayer and supplication, and the imam supplicating after the prayer facing the congregation.

Salah — Prayer

Lunar Eclipse and Calamity Prayer: Individual Sunnah
Rulings for lunar eclipse and other calamities: individual prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for lunar eclipse prayer and explain why it is performed individually, citing the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Lunar eclipse prayer is sunnah performed individually—because the Prophet never gathered people for it, to prevent fitna.

When a lunar eclipse or other calamity occurs, many assume that a congregational prayer is prescribed, similar to solar eclipse. However, the Hanafi school teaches a distinct ruling: these prayers are to be performed individually. This lesson examines the textual proof and rationale behind this ruling, based on the Prophet's practice and the concern for social disorder (fitna).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act (lunar eclipse prayer) and its hukm level. According to the text, it is sunnah muakkadah and performed individually.
The sunnah nature is derived from the general command to pray at times of fear, but the congregation is omitted.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the absence of a report that the Prophet gathered people for lunar eclipse. The text says: 'لم ينقل إلينا أنه جمع الناس له' (it has not been transmitted that he gathered people for it).
This is a dalil of omission (dalil al-'adam) which is used as evidence in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this absence prove the ruling? The Prophet's consistent practice (sunnah) is a source of law. If he had intended congregation, he would have done it. Since he did not, the default is individual prayer.
The Hanafi principle: 'The Prophet's action indicates the ruling; his omission indicates it is not required.'
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that lunar eclipse prayer is congregational like solar eclipse. They analogize it to solar eclipse, which is performed in congregation.
Hanafi scholars respond that the analogy is broken because the Prophet's practice differentiated them.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is individual prayer. This is based on the zahir riwayah (explicit transmissions) and is the safer option to avoid fitna.
Some later Hanafis allowed congregation if the calamity is widespread and the imam deems it beneficial, but the classical ruling stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يحضر الإمام (صلوا أي الناس (فرادى) ركعتين أو أربعاً في منازلهم (كأداء صلاة (الخسوف فرادى لأن القمر خسف مراراً في عهد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولم ينقل إلينا أنه جمع الناس له دفعًا للفتنة وكسوف القمر ذهاب ضوئه والخسوف ذهاب دائرته والحكم أعم (و) كالصلاة فرادى لحصول الظلمة الهائلة نهاراً والريح الشديدة) ليلاً كان أو نهاراً (والفزع) بالزلازل والصواعق وانتشار الكواكب والضوء الهائل ليلاً، والثلج والأمطار من الإفزاع والأهوال الدائمة، وعموم الأمراض، والخسوف الغالب من العدو ونحو لأنها آيات مخوّفة للعباد ليتركوا المعاصي، ويرجعوا إلى طاعة الله تعالى التي بها فوزهم وأقرب أحوال العبد في الرجوع إلى ربه الصلاة نسأل الله من فضله العفو والعافية وصلاحهم.
And if the imam is not present, the people pray individually in their homes, two or four rak'ahs, like performing the lunar eclipse prayer individually, because the moon eclipsed many times in the era of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and it has not been transmitted to us that he gathered people for it, to prevent fitna. And kusuf of the moon is the loss of its light, and khusuf is the loss of its disk, and the ruling is more general. And similarly they pray individually due to the occurrence of intense darkness by day, and severe wind by night or day, and fright from earthquakes, thunderbolts, shooting stars, and an immense light by night, and snow and rains from constant terrors and horrors, and widespread diseases, and an overwhelming enemy and the like, because they are terrifying signs for the servants to abandon sins and return to the obedience of Allah Almighty, in which lies their success. And the closest state of the servant in returning to his Lord is prayer. We ask Allah from His bounty for pardon, well-being, and righteousness.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof: it explains that if the imam is not present for the solar eclipse prayer, people should pray individually at home, either two or four rak'ahs. The same applies to lunar eclipse: it should be prayed individually because the Prophet did not gather people for it due to fear of fitna (corruption). The commentator distinguishes between kusuf (loss of light) and khusuf (loss of the disk) for the moon, but the ruling is general for both. Additionally, other terrifying phenomena such as extreme darkness, strong winds, earthquakes, lightning, shooting stars, unusual night light, heavy snow and rain, widespread diseases, and overwhelming enemies require individual prayer. These are signs to make people repent and turn to Allah. The best way to return to Allah is prayer. The text ends with a supplication for pardon, well-being, and righteousness.

Key Terms
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse; the darkening of the moon.
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse; the darkening of the sun. In the text, also used for the moon's loss of light.
فتنة (fitna): Tribulation or corruption, here referring to potential disorder from gathering at night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the lunar eclipse prayer performed individually rather than in congregation?
A) Because the moon is less important than the sun
B) To avoid fitna, as the Prophet did not gather people for it
C) Because it is not a sunnah prayer
D) Because it is only for imams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that lunar eclipse and similar calamity prayers are performed individually to avoid fitna, based on the Prophet's omission of congregation.
