The Definition and Ruling of Salat al-Istisqa
Introduction defining istisqa and its legal status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Salat al-Istisqa and state its legal status (sunnah muakkadah) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The prayer for rain is a sunnah combining fear of drought, supplication, and congregational prayer.

Istisqa is not merely an informal supplication; it is a structured act of worship legislated by the Shari'a. This lesson unpacks the definition from the Hashiya al-Tahtawi and clarifies the Hanafi position that it is a sunnah muakkadah, alongside the connection to the eclipse prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its definition
Locate the term 'istisqa' in the text and note that it is defined as 'seeking rain' (talab al-suqya) from Allah.
The definition includes the means: istighfar, hamd, and thana'.
2
Recognize the legal status (hukm)
The text states it is 'mashru' (legislated). In Hanafi fiqh, this indicates sunnah muakkadah.
The commentator notes it is sunnah muakkadah; confirmed by zahir al-riwayah.
3
Understand the occasion (munasaba)
The author links istisqa to the eclipse prayer (kusuf) because both are performed in a state of fear.
Fear of drought for istisqa, fear of cosmic event for kusuf.
4
Examine the prescribed actions
The definition mentions istighfar (seeking forgiveness), hamd (praise), and thana' (glorification) as integral to the request for rain.
These are part of the supplication; the prayer itself includes a specific two-rak'ah prayer.
5
Apply the ruling
Therefore, when a community faces drought, it is a stressed sunnah to perform the salat al-istisqa in congregation.
The mufta bihi position is to perform it with a sermon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاستسقاء مناسبته للكسوف أنهما يؤديان حال الخوف جوهرة. قوله : (هو طلب السقيا الخ) هذا هو طلب السقيا أي طلب العباد السقي من الله تعالى بالاستغفار والحمد والثناء وشرع
Chapter on seeking rain. Its appropriateness with the eclipse is that both are performed in a state of fear, as a jewel. His saying: (It is seeking rain etc.) This is seeking rain, i.e., the servants asking for water from Allah Almighty through seeking forgiveness, praise, and glorification, and it is legislated.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling: it introduces the chapter on Salat al-Istisqa (prayer for rain). The commentator notes the connection between the eclipse prayer and the rain prayer: both are performed when people are in a state of fear (of eclipse or drought). The matn defines istisqa as the act of seeking rain from Allah by means of istighfar (seeking forgiveness), hamd (praise), and thana' (glorification). The prayer is legislated (mashru') based on the Quran and Sunnah. The hashia expands on the definition, emphasizing that it is a request for water through specific acts of worship.

Key Terms
الاستسقاء (al-istisqa): The act of asking Allah for rain through prayer and supplication.
السقيا (al-suqya): The water or rain being sought.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'istisqa' according to this passage?
A) Asking for forgiveness
B) Asking for rain from Allah using specific acts
C) A type of eclipse prayer
D) Giving charity for rain

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Istisqa is a sunnah muakkadah that combines fear of drought, congregational prayer, and supplication through istighfar, hamd, and thana'.

Rulings on Entering and Exiting a Plague-Stricken Area
Explains ruling on entering/exiting plague area and prayer during epidemics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering and exiting a plague-stricken area and explain the role of belief in divine decree.

Core Idea
Entering or leaving a plague area depends on one's belief in divine decree — not absolute prohibition.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashia addresses a critical fiqh issue: what should a Muslim do when faced with a plague or epidemic? The ruling is not a simple 'permitted' or 'prohibited' — it hinges on the believer's understanding of causality. We will unpack the hadith cited, the scholarly interpretations, and how the Hanafi school balances textual command with theological soundness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled on: entering a plague-stricken land and leaving it. The ruling is not absolute but conditional on the person's belief.
The act is entering/exiting during an epidemic.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith narrated by al-Tahawi: 'Do not advance to it and do not leave fleeing from it.' Identify the text and its chain (ahad, zanni al-thubut).
The hadith is about the plague sent upon Bani Israel.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The commands ('do not advance', 'do not leave') are imperative, but their application depends on the underlying belief. Al-Tahawi explains that if one believes entering causes affliction, he should not enter to protect his belief in predestination.
The dalala (meaning) is conditional on the person's creed.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage mentions other opinions: some say prohibition is to prevent neglect of the sick, others to console the poor. These are additional wisdoms, not mutually exclusive.
There is consensus that prayer is individual (not congregational) during epidemics.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is that the prohibition is protective of belief, not inherent. One who firmly knows all is by decree may enter/exit. This is the mufta bihi view.
This ruling applies to any epidemic (waba'), including plague (ta'un).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك من الإفزاع والأهوال الدائمة، وعموم الأمراض، والخسوف الغالب من العدو ونحو لأنها آيات مخوّفة للعباد ليتركوا المعاصي، ويرجعوا إلى طاعة الله تعالى التي بها فوزهم وأقرب أحوال العبد في الرجوع إلى ربه الصلاة نسأل الله من فضله العفو والعافية وصلاحهم. وعموم الأمراض) كلمتهم متفقة على أنهم يصلون فرادى ويدعون في عموم الوباء، والأمراض. قال في النهر ، وهو شامل للطاعون لأنّ الوباء اسم لكل مرض عام طاعوناً كان، أو غيره، ولا ينعكس، وإن الدعاء يفعله كما يرفعه الناس في الجبل مشروع، وليس هذا دعاء برفع الشهادة لأنها أثره لا عينه يعني فصار كملاقاة العدو وقد ثبت أنه سأل العافية منها اهـ . قال وعلى هذا فما قاله ابن حجر من أن الإجتماع للدعاء برفعه بدعة أي حسنة، فإذا اجتمعوا صلي كل واحد ركعتين ينوي بهما رفعه قال : وهذه المسئلة من حوادث الفتوى اهـ وتمامه في الأشباه، وذكر الطحاوي في مشكل الآثار في تأويل حديث الطاعون أرسل على طائفة من بني إسرائيل، فإذا سمعتم به بأرض فلا تقدموا عليه وإذا وقع بأرض، وأنتم بها فلا تخرجوا فراراً عنه، فقال: إن كان بحال لو دخل وابتلى به وقع عنده أنه ابتلى بدخوله، ولو خرج فنجا، وقع عنده أنه نجا بخروجه لا يدخل، ولا يخرج صيانة لاعتقاده، فأما إذا كان يعلم أن كل شيء بقدر الله تعالى، وأنه لا يصيبه إلا ما كتب الله عليه، فلا بأس بأن يدخل، ويخرج اهـ، وقيل: المنع من الخروج خوفاً من تعطل المرضى الذين في تلك الأرض لأن الناس إذا فروا عنهم تعطلت أحوالهم وأحوال من يموت منهم ، وقيل : جبراً لخاطر الفقير الذي لا يجد ما يعنيه إلا على الخروج ، وقيل : غير ذلك.
That is from the continuous terrors and fears, general diseases, and overwhelming eclipses from the enemy and the like, because they are signs that frighten the servants so that they abandon sins and return to the obedience of Allah, which is their success, and the closest state of the servant in returning to his Lord is prayer. We ask Allah of His bounty for pardon and well-being and their rectification. And general diseases: their word is agreed that they pray individually and supplicate during general epidemics and diseases. He said in al-Nahr: it includes the plague because 'epidemic' is a name for every general disease, whether plague or other, and the reverse is not true. And the supplication is done as raising it (the matter) to the people of the mountain is legislated. This is not a supplication for the removal of martyrdom because it is its effect, not its essence, meaning it becomes like meeting the enemy, and it is established that he asked for well-being from it. He said: based on this, what Ibn Hajar said that gathering for supplication for its removal is a innovation, i.e., good, so if they gather, each one prays two rak'ahs intending its removal. He said: this is a matter of recent fatwas. And its completion is in al-Ashbah. And al-Tahawi mentioned in Mushkil al-Athar in the interpretation of the hadith of the plague: 'It was sent upon a group of the Children of Israel. So if you hear of it in a land, do not advance to it, and if it occurs in a land while you are in it, do not leave fleeing from it.' He said: If he is in a state such that if he enters and is afflicted by it, he believes that he is afflicted by his entry, and if he leaves and is saved, he believes that he is saved by his exit, then he should not enter or leave to protect his belief. But if he knows that everything is by the decree of Allah, and that nothing afflicts him except what Allah has written for him, then there is no harm in him entering and exiting. And it is said: the prohibition against leaving is out of fear for the neglect of the sick in that land, because if people flee from them, their circumstances and the circumstances of those who die among them are neglected. And it is said: to console the poor person who cannot find what helps him except by leaving. And it is said: other than that.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding actions during general epidemics and plagues. The author (al-Tahtawi) begins by explaining that the earlier text mentioned 'continuous terrors and fears, general diseases, and eclipses' as signs that should lead people to repentance and prayer. He then comments on the phrase 'general diseases' stating that scholars agree that during such times, people should pray individually (not in congregation) and make supplication. The author notes that the term 'general disease' includes the plague (ta'un) because it is a type of widespread illness. He then discusses a hadith about the plague: a plague was sent upon a group of Bani Israel, and Muslims are instructed not to enter a land where plague is present, and if they are in such a land, not to leave fleeing from it. Al-Tahawi explains that the ruling depends on the person's belief. If a person believes that entering causes affliction or leaving causes salvation, then he should not enter or leave to avoid corrupting his belief in divine decree. But if he firmly knows that everything is by Allah's decree, then it is permissible to enter or leave. Other opinions are also mentioned: some say the prohibition against leaving is to prevent neglect of the sick, or to console the poor who cannot afford to leave. The passage shows that the ruling is not absolute but depends on intention and belief.

Key Terms
الوباء (al-waba'): A general term for any widespread disease, including plague and others.
الطاعون (al-ta'un): A specific type of plague, which is a severe epidemic disease.
الدعاء (al-du'a): Supplication to Allah for removal of affliction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one of the reasons given for the prohibition against leaving a plague-stricken area, other than belief?
A) To avoid spreading the disease to other lands
B) To prevent neglect of the sick and those who die
C) Because leaving is a sign of ingratitude
D) Because the plague is a punishment from Allah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on entering/exiting a plague area is not absolute but depends on the person's belief in divine decree: one with correct tawakkul may act, while one with weak belief must avoid to protect his faith.

Definition and Ruling of Salat al-Istisqa'
Defines istisqa' and states its ruling as permissible not sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of istisqa', identify its conditions, and explain why it is considered ja'iz but not sunnah.

Core Idea
Salat al-Istisqa' is permissible but not a confirmed sunnah; the imam may choose to perform it or rely on istighfar alone.

Many assume that since the Prophet (PBUH) prayed for rain, the act must be a confirmed sunnah. But the Hanafi school distinguishes between what the Prophet did and what he did consistently. This lesson unpacks the legal definition of istisqa', its conditions, and the evidence behind its classification as permissible rather than sunnah, as recorded in the commentary on Maraqi al-Falah.

Guided Path
1
Define Istisqa' linguistically and legally
Break down the term: 'istisqa'' is derived from the root s-q-y, with sin and ta for request. In language it means requesting water; in law it specifically means requesting rain from Allah in a prescribed manner.
Note the difference between the linguistic and technical meanings.
2
Identify the conditions that trigger istisqa'
Determine when the prayer is appropriate: when a community lacks sufficient natural water sources (rivers, wells) or when existing sources are insufficient. If water is sufficient, no prayer is held.
The condition is need (hajah), not mere drought.
3
Examine the evidence from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma
Review the dalil: Quranic verse commanding istighfar (Hud 11:52), Prophetic practice (including the miracle of rain through the young Prophet), and consensus of the ummah.
All three sources are cited in the text.
4
Analyze the Hanafi ruling: ja'iz not sunnah
Understand why the Hanafi school classifies it as permissible without dislike, but not sunnah. The key proof is that Umar, the most adherent to the Sunnah, only performed istighfar when seeking rain, not the specific prayer.
Lack of consistent Prophetic practice (mudawamah) negates sunnah status.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school holds it as sunnah mu'akkadah. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's action does not imply sunnah because it was not done consistently; Umar's practice shows flexibility.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاستسقاء مناسبته للكسوف أنهما يؤديان حال الخوف جوهرة. قوله : (هو طلب السقيا الخ) هذا التعريف لمعناه الشرعي فالسين والتاء للطلب والإضافة من إضافة المصدر إلى مفعوله والسقيا بالضم الماء وذكر بعضهم أنه في اللغة طلب الماء مطلقاً، وغلب في الشرع على طلب المطر من الله تعالى على وجه مخصوص، وهو مسنون عند الحاجة إليه في موضع لا يكون لأهله، أودية، وأنهار وآبار يشربون منها ويسقون مواشيهم وزروعهم، أو كان لهم ذلك لكن لا يكفيهم، فإن كان كافياً لا يستسقون كذا في القهستاني، وقوله على طلب المطر من تعالى الأولى أن يقال : طلب الماء ليعم طلب زيادة الأنهار لمن له نهر لا يكفيه كالنيل إذا كان لا يكفي، وفي المطالع سقاه، وأسقاه بمعنى واحد وقيل : سقاه ،ناوله، وأسقاه جعل له سقياً، وقيل : سقاه لشفتيه وأسقاه لماشيته، وأرضه أود له عليه قوله : (بالاستغفار) الباء بمعنى مع وليس صلة للطلب لأن الوارد الطلب بنحو اللهم اسقنا غيثاً مغيثاً إلى آخر ما يأتي، ويحتمل أن الطلب يكون بالاستغفار لأن الله تعالى رتب إرسال السماء عليه فقال تعالى : استغفروا ربكم [هود/ ١١] الآية ولما روي أن عمر استسقى فلم يزد على الاستغفار . قوله : (وشرع بالكتاب) وهو قوله تعالى حكاية عن نوح عليه السلام فقلت استغفروا ربكم الآية روي أن قوم نوح كذبوه بعد طول تكريره الدعوة حبس عنهم القطر، وأعقم أرحام نسائهم أربعين سنة، وقيل: سبعين سنة ووعدهم أنهم إن آمنوا رزقهم الله الخصب، ورفع عنهم ما كانوا عليه، وشرع من قبلنا شرع لنا إذا قصه الله ورسوله من غير إنكار، وهذا كذلك كذا في الشرح. قوله : (والسنة) صح في كثير الآثار أنه لا استسقى، وكذا الخلفاء بعده ، وقد استسقى به وهو صغير أخرج ابن عساكر عن عرفطة ابن الحباب الأزدي رضي الله عنه قاله: قدمت مكة، وهم في قحط، فقالت قريش يا أبا طالب أقحط الوادي وأجدب العيال فهلم فاستسق، فخرج أبو طالب، ومعه غلام كأنه شمس تجلت عنها سحابة قتماء وحوله أغيلمة فأخذه أبو طالب، وألصق ظهره بالكعبة ولاذ الغلام بأصبعه وما في السماء قزعة فأقبل السحاب من ههنا وههنا، وأغدق واغدودق، وانفجر له الوادي، وأخصب النادي والبادي وفي ذلك يقول أبو طالب: وأبيض يستسقى الغمام بوجهه ثمال اليتامي عصمة للأرامل قوله: (والإجماع) أجمعت عليه الأمة سلفاً وخلفاً من غير نكير كذا في البحر. قوله : (جائزة بلا كراهة وليست (سنة) روي أنه لما شكي عليه القحط رفع يديه يستسقي، ولم يذكر فيه صلاة، ولا قلب رداء فلم يدل على السنية إذا لم توجد المواظبة في أغلب الأحوال فالإمام مخير إن شاء فعلها، وإن شاء تركها كذا في غاية البيان عن شرح مختصر الطحاوي . قوله: (حين استسقى) روي عنه رضي الله عنه أنه خرج يستسقي فما زاد على الاستغفار. قوله : لأنه كان أشد الناس اتباعاً لرسول الله علة للعلية والمعنى لأنه كان كذلك بعد الصديق
Chapter of Istisqa'. Its connection to the eclipse: both bring about a state of fear, as stated in Jawhara. His statement: 'It is the request for rain (al-suqya)' etc. This is a definition according to its legal meaning. The letters sin and ta are for request, and the addition is of the masdar to its object. Al-suqya (with damm) means water. Some have mentioned that in language it is the request for water absolutely, but in law it is predominately used for the request for rain from Allah in a specific manner. It is sunnah when there is need for it, in a place where the people do not have valleys, rivers, or wells from which they drink and water their livestock and crops, or if they have them but they are insufficient. If they are sufficient, they do not pray for rain. This is as in al-Qahistani. His statement: 'for the request for rain from the Most High', it is better to say: 'request for water' to include the request for increase of rivers for one who has a river that is insufficient, like the Nile when it is insufficient. In al-Matali', saqahu and asqahu are synonymous. It was said: saqahu means he gave him to drink, asqahu means he made a watering place for him. And it was said: saqahu for his lips, asqahu for his livestock and his land. He has a valley there? His statement: 'with istighfar' the ba is for accompaniment, not a connection to the request, because what is reported is the request in the form 'O Allah, give us a beneficial rain' etc. It is also possible that the request is through istighfar because Allah tied the sending of rain to it, as He said: 'Seek forgiveness of your Lord' (Quran 11:??). And it is narrated that Umar prayed for rain and did not add more than istighfar. His statement: 'And it is legislated by the Book' is His statement narrating from Nuh: 'So I said, seek forgiveness of your Lord' etc. It is narrated that Nuh's people denied him after long repetition of the call, so rain was withheld from them, and the wombs of their women became barren for forty years, some say seventy years, and he promised them that if they believed, Allah would give them abundance and remove what they were in. And the law of those before us is a law for us if Allah and His Messenger relate it without disapproval, and so it is, as in the Sharh. His statement: 'and the Sunnah' is established in many traditions that he (the Prophet) prayed for rain, and likewise the caliphs after him. And he (the Prophet) prayed for rain when he was a child. Ibn Asakir narrated from Urfata ibn al-Habbab al-Azdi: I came to Mecca and they were in a drought. Quraysh said: O Abu Talib, the valley has dried up and the families have become bare, so come and pray for rain. So Abu Talib came out, and with him was a boy like a sun emerging from a dark cloud, surrounded by young boys. Abu Talib took him and pressed his back against the Kaaba, and the boy clung with his finger, and there was not a cloud in the sky. Then clouds came from here and there, and it rained heavily, and the valley burst forth, and the settled and nomadic areas became verdant. In that Abu Talib said: 'And a white-faced one through whose face rain is sought from the clouds, a shelter for orphans, a protection for widows.' His statement: 'and consensus' - the ummah, past and present, has agreed upon it without objection, as in al-Bahr. His statement: 'It is permissible without dislike and it is not sunnah' - it is narrated that when he was complained to about the drought, he raised his hands praying for rain, and no prayer or turning of the cloak is mentioned, so it does not indicate sunnah, since there was no persistence in most cases. So the imam has a choice: if he wishes he may perform it, and if he wishes he may leave it. This is as in Ghayat al-Bayan from the Sharh of Mukhtasar al-Tahawi. His statement: 'when he prayed for rain' - it is narrated that Umar went out to pray for rain and did not increase beyond istighfar. His statement: 'because he was the most following of the people of the Messenger of Allah' is the cause for the causality, meaning he was like that after Abu Bakr.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on Istisqa' (the prayer for rain) in the commentary. The author first notes the connection between the chapter on eclipses and this chapter, as both involve fear. He then explains the definition: 'istisqa' means requesting al-suqya (rain).' The term is derived from the sin and ta for request, and it is a verbal noun. In language, it means requesting water absolutely, but in Islamic law, it is specifically the request for rain from Allah in a prescribed manner. The ruling is that it is sunnah (recommended) when there is need—when a community lacks sufficient water sources like rivers or wells, or when existing sources are insufficient. If water is sufficient, no prayer is sought. The author then discusses the evidence: from the Quran (the story of Prophet Nuh, where istighfar leads to rain), from the Sunnah (the Prophet himself prayed for rain, and the caliphs after him), and from consensus of the ummah. However, a key point is made: even though the Prophet prayed for rain, the action is not considered a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) because it was not performed consistently. The proof is that Umar, known for his strict adherence to the Sunnah, only performed istighfar without the specific prayer when he prayed for rain. Therefore, the prayer for rain is permissible (ja'iz) without dislike, but it is not sunnah. The imam has the option to perform it or not. This is the Hanafi position: it is not a sunnah in the sense of being regularly practiced.

Key Terms
الاستسقاء (al-istisqa'): A specific legal act: requesting rain from Allah through prayer and supplication, often with a prescribed form.
السقيا (al-suqya): Rain or water that is requested; also the act of giving water.
الاستغفار (al-istighfar): Seeking forgiveness from Allah, which is a primary means of bringing rain according to the Quran and practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Salat al-Istisqa' considered 'ja'iz' (permissible) but not 'sunnah' according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the Quran does not mention it
B) Because Umar did not perform it when he prayed for rain
C) Because the Prophet prohibited it
D) Because it requires fasting beforehand

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Istisqa' is permissible when needed, but not a confirmed sunnah; the imam may choose to pray or suffice with istighfar.

Salat al-Istisqa: Permissible vs. Sunnah
Defines Istisqa, presents proofs, and explains Hanafi permissibility vs. sunnah status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Salat al-Istisqa and explain why it is considered permissible but not Sunnah, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i view and identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Salat al-Istisqa is permissible but not Sunnah; Umar's practice shows the Sunnah is istighfar, not prayer.

The prayer for rain (Salat al-Istisqa) is a well-known practice, but its legal status differs among schools. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position, which holds that formal prayer is merely permissible (ja'iz) and not a regular Sunnah. The author of Hashiya al-Tahtawi presents the proofs from the Quran, the practice of Umar, and the weakness of contrary reports, while also addressing intra-Hanafi differences on whether to pray individually or in congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
Determine the exact point of contention: Is Salat al-Istisqa a Sunnah (recommended) or merely permissible (ja'iz)? The Hanafi school says ja'iz; the Shafi'i school and some early Muslims consider it Sunnah.
The term 'Sunnah' here implies a regularly performed practice of the Prophet that one should follow.
2
Follow the Hanafi dalil
Examine the Hanafi evidence: the Quranic command to seek forgiveness (istighfar) in Surah Nuh and Surah Hud, and the practice of Umar who only used istighfar when praying for rain. The Hanafi argument: Umar was the most diligent follower of the Prophet; if formal prayer were Sunnah, he would have performed it.
The Hanafi school regards the verse as the primary legislative basis, not the prayer itself.
3
Examine the opposing proof
Review the opposing argument: the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs for rain, and the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zayd. These reports purport to show the Prophet establishing a formal prayer.
The Shafi'i school and others accept these as evidence for Sunnah mu'akkadah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand why the Hanafi school rejects these hadith as sufficient for Sunnah: they are solitary (shadhdh) and not widely transmitted in the early period. The well-known practice of the Prophet and the caliphs was only dua and istighfar. A solitary report cannot establish a regular Sunnah in Hanafi usul.
The Hanafi school requires widespread transmission (shuhrah) to elevate an act to Sunnah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, omitting Salat al-Istisqa incurs no sin, and the imam may choose whether to lead it. In schools that consider it Sunnah, omission is a missed recommended act. The Hanafi view gives the imam flexibility.
This also affects whether congregational prayer is encouraged or merely allowed.

كتاب الصلاة
،
٥٤٩
رسول الله له بجميع الصحابة، ولو ثبت صلاته فيها لاشتهر نقله اشتهاراً واسعاً، ولم يتركها عمر رضي الله عنه ،وبتركه لم ينكروا عليه وقد ورد شاذاً صلاته للإستسقاء فقلنا بجوازها (من غير جماعة) عند الإمام كما قال إن صلوا وحدانا، فلا بأس به وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : يصلي الإمام ركعتين يجهر فيهما بالقراءة كالعيد لما رواه ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أنه صلى فيهما ركعتين كصلاة العيد في الجهر بالقراءة والصلاة بلا أذان وإقامة قال شيخ الإسلام فيه دليل على الجواز وعندنا يجوز لو صلوا بجماعة لكن ليس بسنة (وله (استغفار) لقوله تعالى: (فقلت استغفروا ربكم إنه كان غفاراً يرسل السماء عليكم مدرارا ويستحب الخروج له أي للإستسقاء ثلاثة أيام متتابعات ولم ينقل أكثر منها
رضي الله عنهم أجمعين . قوله: (ولم يتركها عمر المناسب زيادة، ولا أنكروا عليه ليناسب قوله : وبتركه لم ينكروا عليه وواوه للحال . قوله : (وقد ورد شاذاً صلاته للاستسقاء) ذكر الشهيد في الكافي الذي هو جمع كلام محمد قال : لا صلاة في الاستسقاء إنما فيه الدعاء بلغنا عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه خرج ودعا، وبلغنا عن عمر أنه صعد المنبر فدعا واستسقى، ولم يبلغنا عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في ذلك صلاة إلا حديث واحد شاذ لا يؤخذ به اهـ، ولم تشتهر رواية الصلاة في الصدر الأول، بل هو عن ابن عباس وعبد الله بن زيد على اضطراب في كيفيتها، والحاصل لما اختلفت في الصلاة بالجماعة وعدمها على وجه لا يصلح به إثبات السنة لم يقل أبو حنيفة بسنيتها، ولا يلزم من عدم قوله بسنيتها قوله : بأنها بدعة كما نقله عنه بعض المشنعين بالتعصب، بل هو قائل بالجواز كذا في الحلبي قوله : (كالعيد) إلا أنه ليس فيها تكبيرات مثلا مسكين، ثم يخطب بعد الصلاة لكن عند محمد خطبتين يجلس بينهما، وقال أبو يوسف: خطبة واحدة بغير جلسة، ثم يستقبل القبلة، ويقلب رداءه، ويدعو بدعاء الاستسقاء. قوله: (في الجهر الخ) أي لا في التكبيرات قوله : (قال شيخ الإسلام الخ) ذكر ابن أمير حاج : لو صلوا بجماعة هل يكره عند الإمام فذكر الحاكم الشهيد في باب صلاة الكسوف من الكافي ما يفيد الكراهة حيث قال : يكره التطوع بجماعة ما خلا قيام ،رمضان والكسوف لكن كلام شيخ الإسلام في هذا المقام يفيد الجواز ،بدونها، وهو متجه نظراً للدليل، فليكن عليه التعويل. قوله : (يرسل السماء عليكم مدراراً) قال في المضمرات: السماء المطر، والمدرار كثير الدر اهـ. قوله: (ويستحب الخروج له ثلاثة أيام إلى الصحراء للاتباع، ولأنه أقرب إلى التواضع، وأوسع للجمع، ولأنهم يسألون المطر فينبغي أن يكون حيث يصيبهم وفي المجتبى، والأولى أن يخرج الإمام بالناس، وإن لم يخرج بنفسه، وأمرهم بالخروج جاز وإن خرجوا بغير إذنه جاز أيضاً، وفي الخلاصة إذا غارت الأنهار، وانقطعت الأمطار يستحب للإمام أن يأمر الناس أولاً بصيام ثلاثة أيام، وما أطاقوا من الصلاة والخروج عن المظالم والتوبة من المعاصي، ثم يخرج بهم في اليوم الرابع، وفي الحموي عن النظم الهاملي إذا سقوا قبل الخروج، وقد كانوا
The Book of Prayer. By the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma, it (the prayer for rain) is permissible, without dislike, and it is not Sunnah because Umar - may Allah be pleased with him - did not perform it when he prayed for rain, for he was the most following of the people of the Messenger of Allah, and he prayed for rain. The definition for its legal meaning: the sin and ta are for request, and the addition is the addition of the verbal noun to its object. Suqya (with damm) means water. Some mentioned that in language it is the request of water absolutely, and in sacred law it is predominantly applied to the request of rain from Allah Almighty in a specific manner. It is recommended (masnun) when there is need for it in a place that does not have rivers, streams, and wells from which they drink and water their livestock and crops, or if they have that but it does not suffice them. If it is sufficient, they do not pray for rain. This is in al-Qahistani. And his saying 'the request of rain from Allah Almighty' - it is better to say 'the request of water' to include the request for increase of rivers for one who has a river that does not suffice him, like the Nile when it does not suffice. And in al-Matali': saqahu and asqahu are synonymous. It is said: saqahu means he gave him to drink, and asqahu means he made a water source for him. It is said: saqahu is for his lips and asqahu for his livestock and land. ... His saying: 'with seeking forgiveness' - the ba (bi) means 'with' and is not a connection to the request, because what is transmitted is the request with something like 'O Allah, give us abundant rain' etc. It is possible that the request is through seeking forgiveness because Allah Almighty linked sending the sky to it. He said: 'Seek forgiveness of your Lord' [Hud: 11] and because it is narrated that Umar prayed for rain and did not add to seeking forgiveness. His saying: 'and it is legislated by the Book' - it is His saying, narrating from Nuh: 'I said: Seek forgiveness of your Lord' etc. It is narrated that the people of Nuh denied him after his long repetition of the call, so rain was withheld from them and the wombs of their women became barren for forty years - it is said: seventy years - and he promised them that if they believed, Allah would provide them with plenty and remove what they were suffering. And the legislation of those before us is legislation for us if Allah and His Messenger narrate it without objection, and this is similar. This is in al-Sharh. His saying: 'and the Sunnah' - it is authentically established in many narrations that he (the Prophet) prayed for rain (without prayer), and likewise the caliphs after him. And he (the Prophet) prayed for rain (with prayer) when he was young. Ibn Asakir narrated from Urfata ibn al-Habbab al-Azdi: 'I came to Makkah while they were in drought. The Quraysh said: O Abu Talib, the valley has become dry and the families have become destitute, so come and pray for rain. Abu Talib went out with a boy who was like a sun that had appeared from a dark cloud, and around him were young boys. Abu Talib took him and placed his back against the Kaaba, and the boy pointed with his finger while there was no cloud in the sky, then clouds came from here and there, and it rained heavily, the valley flowed, and both the town and desert became fertile.' In that Abu Talib said: 'And a white-faced one by whose face rain is sought from the clouds, the protector of orphans, the refuge of widows.' His saying: 'and Ijma' - the Ummah agreed upon it, early and late, without objection, as in al-Bahr. His saying: 'it is permissible without dislike, and it is not Sunnah' - it is narrated that when drought was complained about to him (the Prophet), he raised his hands to pray for rain, and no prayer nor turning of cloak is mentioned therein. So it does not indicate sunniyyah, since regular practice in most cases is not found. So the imam may choose: if he wishes, he performs it; if he wishes, he leaves it. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan from Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi. His saying: 'when he prayed for rain' - it is narrated from him that he went out to pray for rain and did not add to seeking forgiveness. His saying: 'for he was the most following of the people of the Messenger of Allah' is a cause for the causality, meaning he was like that after al-Siddiq. ... The Messenger of Allah had more following among all the Companions. If his prayer (the Prophet's) for rain had been established, its transmission would have been widely known, and Umar would not have left it. And by his leaving it, they did not object to him. And a solitary report has come that he prayed for rain, so we said it is permissible (without congregation) according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], as he said: If they pray individually, there is no harm. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The imam should pray two rak'ahs, reciting aloud as in the 'Eid prayer, because Ibn 'Abbas narrated that he prayed two rak'ahs like the 'Eid prayer in raising the voice and praying without adhan and iqamah. Shaykh al-Islam said: In this is evidence for permissibility. According to us, it is permissible if they pray in congregation, but it is not Sunnah. And he has seeking forgiveness because of His saying: 'I said: Seek forgiveness of your Lord; indeed, He is ever forgiving; He will send rain from the sky upon you in abundance.' And it is recommended to go out for it, i.e., for the rain prayer, for three consecutive days, and no more than that has been transmitted. ... His saying: 'and Umar did not leave it' - the appropriate addition is 'and they did not object to him' to correspond to his saying 'and by his leaving it they did not object to him', and the waw is for the circumstantial clause. His saying: 'and a solitary report has come that he prayed for rain' - al-Shahid mentioned in al-Kafi, which is a compilation of the statements of Muhammad: He said: There is no prayer in the rain prayer; it is only supplication. It has reached us that the Prophet went out and supplicated, and that Umar ascended the minbar and supplicated and prayed for rain. And it has not reached us regarding the Prophet any prayer in that except one solitary hadith which is not acted upon. And the narration of the prayer was not well-known in the early generation; rather it is from Ibn 'Abbas and 'Abdullah ibn Zayd with variation in its manner. The conclusion: since the reports differed regarding prayer in congregation and its absence in a way that does not establish it as Sunnah, Abu Hanifa did not declare it Sunnah. And it does not follow from not deeming it Sunnah that he said it is a bid'ah, as some false accusers with fanaticism have transmitted from him. Rather, he holds it permissible. This is in al-Halabi. His saying: 'like the 'Eid prayer' - except that there are no extra takbirs in it. Then he delivers a sermon after the prayer. According to Muhammad, two sermons with a sitting between them. Abu Yusuf said: One sermon without a sitting. Then he faces the qibla, turns his cloak, and supplicates with the supplication for rain. His saying: 'in raising the voice, etc.' - meaning not in the takbirs. His saying: 'Shaykh al-Islam said' - Ibn Amir Hajj mentioned: If they pray in congregation, is it disliked according to Imam? Al-Hakim al-Shahid mentioned in the chapter on eclipse prayer in al-Kafi that it indicates dislike: 'Voluntary prayer in congregation is disliked except during the nights of Ramadan and eclipse.' But the statement of Shaykh al-Islam in this context indicates permissibility without it (without congregation?), and it is sound considering the evidence, so reliance should be on it. His saying: 'He will send rain from the sky upon you in abundance' - in al-Mudmarat: al-sama' means rain; al-midrar means abundant rain. His saying: 'it is recommended to go out for it for three days to the desert' - for following the Sunnah, and because it is closer to humility, more spacious for gathering, and because they ask for rain so it should be where it falls. In al-Mujtaba: It is better that the imam goes out with the people; if he does not go out himself and orders them to go out, it is permissible; and if they go out without his permission, it is also permissible. In al-Khulasa: When rivers dry up and rains cease, it is recommended for the imam to order the people first to fast for three days and perform as much prayer as they can, to exit from injustices and repent from sins, then go out with them on the fourth day. In al-Hamawi from al-Nazm al-Hamili: If they receive rain before going out, and they had intended...

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the ruling on Salat al-Istisqa (prayer for rain). The author begins by defining Istisqa legally: it is the request for rain from Allah in a specific manner, often by supplication or prayer. It is legislated by the Quran (the story of Nuh and the verse 'Seek forgiveness of your Lord'), the Sunnah (the incident of the Prophet as a child with Abu Talib, and the practice of Umar who only used istighfar), and Ijma (consensus of the Ummah). The Hanafi position is that Salat al-Istisqa is permissible (ja'iz) without dislike (karahah) but it is not Sunnah. This is because Umar, who was the most diligent in following the Prophet, did not pray it when he prayed for rain; he only sought forgiveness. The text addresses the objection that the Prophet himself prayed for rain with a prayer (salat). It explains that the report is solitary (shadhdh) and not widely transmitted, so it cannot establish sunniyyah. The author then discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding congregational prayer: Imam Abu Hanifa permits it without congregation (individual prayer is fine), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) recommend the imam to pray two rak'ahs aloud, similar to 'Eid prayer, in congregation. However, they all agree it is not Sunnah; it is merely permissible. The passage also covers recommended practices: going out to the desert for three consecutive days, combined with fasting, repentance, and charity before the fourth day. The author notes that turning the cloak and supplication after the prayer is also recommended, but no extra takbirs are added. The overall message is that the Hanafi school upholds the permissibility of the prayer while firmly rejecting it as a regular Sunnah, based on the practice of Umar and the weakness of contrary evidence.

Key Terms
الاستسقاء (al-istisqā'): The request for water/rain from Allah, either by supplication or prayer, in a legislated manner.
السنة (al-sunnah): The recommended practice of the Prophet that is regularly performed; omission is not sinful but leaves one holding to a lesser merit.
الجائز (al-jā'iz): Permissible; an act that one may do or leave without any sin or reward beyond the intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on Salat al-Istisqa (prayer for rain)?
A) It is Sunnah mu'akkadah and recommended.
B) It is permissible (ja'iz) but not Sunnah.
C) It is disliked (makruh) to pray it.
D) It is forbidden (haram) because it is an innovation.

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Istisqa is permissible (ja'iz) in the Hanafi school but not a regular Sunnah; the primary means of seeking rain is istighfar.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Etiquettes and Procedure of Istisqa Prayer
Describes recommended actions and imam's role in rain prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended etiquettes of Istisqa and explain the imam's procedure for the rain prayer according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Rain prayer follows the sunnah of humility, charity, and specific supplication as taught by the Prophet.

This lesson details the sunnah muakkadah of Istisqa (prayer for rain) according to the Hanafi school. The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi outlines the recommended actions for the congregation and the imam, supported by hadith and practice of the Salaf. You will learn the proper attire, accompanying acts, location preferences, and the sequence of the imam's supplication, including an intra-Hanafi difference regarding when the supplication occurs relative to the prayer and khutbah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended preparations
List the etiquettes before going out: wearing worn washed clothes (preferably patched), giving charity, renewing repentance, seeking forgiveness, returning wrongs, and bringing out animals, elderly, and children.
These actions display humility and invite mercy through the weak.
2
Understand the location ruling
Note that Istisqa is held in the desert (open area) except in Mecca, Jerusalem, and Medina, where it is performed in the respective mosques.
Exception due to the honor of these places and increased descent of mercy.
3
Learn the imam's actions during the prayer
The imam stands facing qibla, raises hands until armpits show, then turns his back to the people with the congregation seated facing qibla, saying amen.
The specific supplication is reported: 'O Allah, give us a relieving, wholesome, and beneficial rain.'
4
Grasp the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on sequence
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the imam supplicates after the salah; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that he prays, then delivers khutbah, then turns his cloak and supplicates standing.
The passage presents both without tarjih; later Hanafi works often prefer the Sahibayn's view.

أي لا ينغصه شيء، أو ينمي الحيوان من غير ضرر (مريئاً) بفتح أوله وبالمد والهمز أي محمود العاقبة والهنيء النافع ظاهراً والمريء هذه أو ذا رحمة وفي التعبير عنه بالرحمة ما لا يخفى من عظيم اتصافه بها، وشمل العالمين الكفار في الدنيا فمنع عنهم الخسف، والمسخ، أو عن غالبهم، وأصاب جبريل من الرحمة شيء فقد أمن به من السلب وخص العالمين لشرفهم، وإلا فرحمته عمت البهائم، والأشجار والأحجار. قوله : (فيتوسل إليه بصاحبيه ذكر بعض العارفين أن الأدب في التوسل أن يتوسل بالصاحبين إلى الرسول الأكرم ثم به إلى حضرة الحق جل جلاله وتعاظمت أسماؤه، فإن مراعاة لواسطة عليها مدار قضاء الحاجات. قوله : فلا مانع) تفريع على قوله : إذ لا يستغاث الخ، والأولى فينبغي كما ذكره في المتن قوله : (وإيقاف) عطف على الإجتماع. قوله : ( ويقوم الإمام) أي على الأرض ليراه القوم، ويسمعوا كلامه، ويجوز إخراج المنبر لها، ثم إذا صلى فعند الإمام الدعاء بعد الصلاة وعندهما يصلي، ثم يخطب، فإذا مضى صدر من خطبته قلب رداءه، ودعا قائماً مستقبلاً للقبلة جوهرة. قوله : (مستقبل القبلة لأنه أفضل، وأقرب إلى الإجابة قال النووي: ويلحق الدعاء جميع الأذكار، وسائر الطاعات إلا ما خص بدليل كالخطبة. قوله : رافعاً يديه) ولم يرفع يديه الرفع البليغ بحيث يرى بياض إبطيه إلا في الاستسقاء، وعنه و أنه قال : إن الله حيي يستحي إذا رفع العبد يديه أن يردهما صفرا يعني فارغتين خائبتين، ثم السنة في كل دعاء لسؤال شيء، وتحصيله أن يجعل بطون كفيه نحو السماء، ولرفع بلاء كالقحط يجعل بطونهما إلى الأرض، وذلك معنى قوله تعالى: ﴿ويدعوننا رغباً ورهبا كذا في شرح البدر العيني على الصحيح، وفي التحفة والمحيط الرضوي، والتجريد إن رفع يديه نحو السماء فحسن وإن لم يفعل، وأشار بأصبعه السبابة من يده اليمنى فحسن وذكره في المبسوط والبدائع، وغيرهما عن أبي يوسف لكن من غير تقييد الأصبع بالسبابة قال ابن أمير حاج وقد ورد الكل في السنة .اهـ. قوله : (قريباً من الزوراء) هي دار عالية البناء كان يؤذن بلال قوله : (ولم يزل يجافي في الرفع يشير به إلى أن ما ذكر في حديث عمر من قوله لا يجاوز بهما رأسه كان في ابتداء الرفع. قوله : (بما ورد متعلق بدعائه. قوله : (أي من الشدة) فيغيثهم ويروبهم ويشبعهم. قوله : (أي محمود العاقبة) أما بأن ينفع الاحشاء، منقذاً
And they go out (walking in worn, washed clothes) not patched (or patched) and that is better, manifesting the quality of being (humble, submissive, fearful of Allah the Exalted, lowering their heads, giving charity every day before their departure). And they renew repentance and seek forgiveness for the Muslims and return wrongful possessions. (And it is recommended to bring out animals) with their young and to separate them so that clamor arises due to needs. (And) the going out (of the elderly and children) because mercy descends through them. He said: 'Are you given provision and victory except through your weak ones?' narrated by Bukhari, and in a report: 'If there were not young men who are humble, grazing animals, elderly who bow, and suckling infants, punishment would have been poured upon you.' (And) they go out to the desert except in Mecca and Jerusalem, for (they gather in the Sacred Mosque and al-Aqsa Mosque) following the predecessors and successors, and due to the honor of the place and increased descent of mercy therein, and there is no doubt. (And that is recommended) i.e., gathering for istisqa in the Prophet's Mosque (also for the people of the Prophet's city). And this is clear, for help and mercy are not sought in his enlightened city without his presence and witnessing in a calamity of the Muslims, and 'We have not sent you except as a mercy to the worlds', and he is the intercessor for sinners, so they seek intercession through his two companions, and they seek intercession through all to Allah. So there is no impediment to gathering at his presence and stopping animals at the door of the mosque for his intercession. And the imam stands facing the qibla during his supplication, raising his hands, based on what was narrated from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he saw the Prophet praying for rain near the stones of olive close to al-Zawra, standing raising his hands before his face not exceeding his head, end. And he continued raising until the whiteness of his armpits appeared. Then he turned his back to the people while the people sat facing the qibla saying amen to his supplication, according to what was reported from the Prophet (ﷺ), and among it is what he textually stated: 'O Allah, give us a rain that is relieving (i.e., delivering from hardship), wholesome (i.e., nothing spoils it, or it grows animals without harm), with good consequence (i.e., praiseworthy outcome). And the wholesome is beneficial outwardly, and the good consequence is this or a mercy. And in expressing it as mercy, what is not hidden of His great attribute with it. And it included the worlds, the disbelievers in the world, so He prevented from them destruction and metamorphosis, or from most of them. And Jibril received something of mercy, so he was safe from deprivation. And He specified the worlds for their honor; otherwise His mercy encompasses animals, trees, and stones. His statement: 'So he seeks intercession through his two companions' - some arifs mentioned that the etiquette in tawassul is to seek intercession through the two companions to the noble Messenger, then through him to the presence of the Truth (Glorious and Exalted be His names), for observing the intermediary is the basis for fulfilling needs. His statement: 'So no impediment' is a branch of his statement: 'for help is not sought', etc., and the better is 'it is recommended' as mentioned in the text. His statement: 'and stopping' is conjuncted to 'gathering'. His statement: 'And the imam stands' i.e., on the ground so that the people see him and hear his speech, and it is permissible to bring out the minbar for it. Then when he prays, according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) the supplication is after the prayer, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he prays then delivers the khutbah. Then when he passes a portion of his khutbah, he turns his cloak and supplicates standing facing the qibla (as a jewel). His statement: 'facing the qibla because it is best and closest to acceptance' - al-Nawawi said: 'Supplication includes all remembrances and all acts of obedience except what is specified by evidence, like the khutbah.' His statement: 'raising his hands' - he did not raise his hands in extreme raising such that the whiteness of his armpits is seen except in istisqa. And it is reported from him that he said: 'Indeed Allah is shy; if the servant raises his hands, He is shy to return them empty, i.e., empty of reward.' Then the sunnah in every supplication for asking something and obtaining it is to make the palms of his hands towards the sky, and for repelling affliction like drought, he makes the backs towards the ground. And that is the meaning of His statement: 'And they call upon Us in hope and fear' as in Sharh al-Badr al-Ayni on al-Sahih, and in al-Tuhfa, al-Muhit al-Radawi, and al-Tajrid: if he raises his hands towards the sky, that is good, and if he does not, and he points with his forefinger of his right hand, that is good. And it was mentioned in al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i and others on the authority of Abu Yusuf, but without restricting the finger to the forefinger. Ibn Amir Haj said: 'All have been reported in the Sunnah.' End. His statement: 'near al-Zawra' - it is a tall building where Bilal used to give the call to prayer. His statement: 'and he continued raising' - it indicates that what was mentioned in the hadith of Umar 'not exceeding his head' was at the beginning of raising. His statement: 'according to what was reported' is attached to 'his supplication'. His statement: 'i.e., from hardship' - so He gives them relief, quenching, and satiation. His statement: 'i.e., praiseworthy outcome' - either by benefiting the innards, delivering.
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details the recommended etiquettes and procedure of the Istisqa (prayer for rain) according to the Hanafi school. It is a ruling with proof, as the author cites hadith to support the practices. The passage begins by describing the outward state of those going out for istisqa: they should walk, wear old washed clothes (patched or unpatched, with patched being better), and exhibit humility, submissiveness, and fear of Allah, with heads lowered. They are to give charity daily before departure, renew repentance, seek forgiveness for all Muslims, and return any wrongfully taken property. The text then recommends bringing out animals with their young and separating them so that their clamor (due to separation) adds to the supplication. Similarly, the elderly and children should go out because mercy descends through the weak; a proof is cited from Bukhari: 'Are you given provision and victory except through your weak ones?' and another report that without humble youth, grazing animals, bowing elders, and suckling infants, punishment would pour down. Regarding location, the people go out to the desert (open area) except in Mecca and Jerusalem, where they gather in the Sacred Mosque and al-Aqsa Mosque respectively, following the precedent of early and later generations and due to the honor and increased mercy in those places. The same applies to Medina: gathering in the Prophet's Mosque is recommended, as help and mercy are sought through the Prophet's presence. Tawassul through the two companions (Abu Bakr and Umar) to the Prophet and then to Allah is mentioned, and there is no impediment to gathering at his grave and stopping animals at the mosque door for his intercession. The imam then stands facing the qibla while supplicating, raising his hands. A hadith from Umar describes the Prophet raising his hands until the whiteness of his armpits appeared, then turning his back to the people while they sit facing qibla and saying amen. The specific supplication includes: 'O Allah, give us a rain that is relieving, wholesome, and with good consequence.' The commentary then elaborates on the meanings of these terms, the etiquette of raising hands (palms up for asking, backs up for repelling affliction), and various opinions on hand positions during supplication. It also notes the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the sequence: according to Imam, supplication comes after the prayer; according to the two, the prayer is followed by the khutbah, and then the imam turns his cloak and supplicates standing. The passage emphasizes that the sunnah is to raise the hands in supplication, and points to the hadith that Allah is shy to return empty hands. Various authorities like al-Ayni, al-Tuhfa, al-Muhit, al-Tajrid, al-Mabsut, and al-Bada'i are cited, along with Ibn Amir Haj's statement that all methods are reported in the Sunnah.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa): A special prayer and supplication for rain during times of drought.
مغيثاً (mughtithan): Meaning 'relieving' or 'delivering' from hardship and distress.
هنيئاً (hani'an): Wholesome, free from harm or spoilage; rain that benefits without causing damage.
مريئاً (mari'an): With good consequence or praiseworthy outcome; rain that leads to prosperity and health.
توسل (tawassul): Seeking nearness to Allah through an intermediary, here through the Prophet and his companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the recommended clothing for those going out for the Istisqa prayer?
A) New and colorful clothes
B) Worn, washed clothes (preferably patched)
C) Silk and luxury garments
D) Formal religious attire

Key Takeaway
Istisqa is a sunnah muakkadah performed with humility, charity, and specific supplication, following the prophetic model as transmitted by the Hanafi school.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
The Imam's Actions and Supplication in Istisqa Prayer
Commentary on the istisqa prayer etiquette and supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions of the imam during the istisqa prayer and explain the evidence for each, including the prophetic practice and the intra-Hanafi difference on the order of prayer, khutbah, and supplication.

Core Idea
Istisqa supplication: imam faces qibla, raises hands high, then turns for congregation's amin.

In this passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi, we examine the specific etiquettes of the istisqa prayer for rain. The commentary explains the imam’s posture and supplication, drawing from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Learning these details will help you understand the sunnah rulings and the weight of prophetic actions in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the imam doing during the istisqa supplication? (facing qibla, raising hands, turning for amin). The ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
The actions are based on the Prophet's consistent practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Umar describing the Prophet's practice near the stones of Zayt. Note that it is a fi'l (action) of the Prophet, which indicates recommendation in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the sunnah? The Prophet's action of raising hands until armpits appear, facing qibla, and turning to the people shows emphasis. In Hanafi usul, a voluntary fi'l without a command indicates sunnah.
The Prophet's consistency (continuation) makes it sunnah muakkadah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, there is a dispute on the order: Abu Hanifa holds that supplication is after prayer; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that it is after the khutbah.
Both views are based on different evidence.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Later practice often follows the Sahibayn (prayer, then khutbah, then supplication). The mufta bihi is that both sequences are valid, but the latter is more common.
The text does not explicitly resolve the ikhtilaf.

المذنبين فيتوسل إليه بصاحبيه ويتوسل بالجميع إلى الله فلا مانع من الاجتماع عند حضرته وإيقاف الدواب بباب المسجد لشفاعته ويقوم الإمام مستقبل القبلة) حالة دعائه (رافعاً يديه) لما روي عن عمر رضي الله عنه أنه رأى النبي يستسقي عند أحجار الزيت قريباً من الزوراء قائماً رافعاً يديه قبل وجهه لا يجاوز بهما رأسه انتهى ولم يزل يجافي في الرفع حتى بدا بياض إبطيه ، ثم حوّل إلى الناس ظهره والناس قعود مستقبلين القبلة يؤمنون على دعائه) بما ورد عن النبي ومنه ما نص عليه بأن يقول اللهم اسقنا غيثاً) أي مطراً (مغيثاً) بضم أوله أي منقذاً من الشدة (هنيئاً) بالمد والهمز أي لا ينغصه شيء، أو ينمي الحيوان من غير ضرر (مريئاً) بفتح أوله وبالمد والهمز أي محمود العاقبة والهنيء النافع ظاهراً والمريء النافع باطناً مريعاً) بضم الميم وبالتحتية أي آتياً بالربع وهي الزيادة من الخصب (غدقاً) أي كثير الماء (مجلّلاً) بكسر اللام أي ساتراً بالأفق لعمومه (سحا) بفتح السين وتشديد الحاء أي شديد الوقع بالأرض (طبقاً) جرى بفتح أوله أي يطبق الأرض حتى يعمها (دائماً) إلى انتهاء الحاجة إليه (و) يدعو أيضاً بكل ما أشبهه (سراً أو جهراً) وثبت عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : اللهم اسقنا غيثاً مغيثاً نافعاً غير ضار عاجلاً غير آجل اللهم اسق عبادك وبهائمك وانثر رحمتك وأحي بلدك الميت اللهم أنت الله لا إله إلا أنت الغني ونحن الفقراء أنزل علينا الغيث واجعل ما أنزلت لنا بلاغاً إلى خير ... وروى أبو داود عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: شكا الناس إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم تحوط المطر فأمر بمنبر فوضع له في المصلى ووعد الناس يوماً يخرجون فيه فخرج له حين بدا حاجب الشمس فقعد على المنبر فكبر وحمد الله عز وجل ثم قال: إنكم شكوتم جدب دياركم واستثخار المطر عن إبان زمانه عنكم وقد أمركم الله سبحانه وتعالى أن تدعوه ووعدكم أن يستجيب لكم قال: الحمد لله رب العالمين الرحمن الرحيم مالك يوم الدين لا إله إلا الله يفعل ما يريد أنت الله الغني ونحن الفقراء أنزل علينا الغيث واجعل ما أنزلت لنا بلاغاً إلى خير. قوله: (أنت الله الغني وفي نسخة أنت الله لا إله إلا أنت الغني) اهـ. انعامك.
The sinners thus seek intercession through his two companions and seek intercession through all to Allah, so there is no prohibition of gathering in his presence and stopping animals at the door of the mosque for his intercession. And the imam stands facing the qibla during his supplication, raising his hands, because it is narrated from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) praying for rain near the stones of Zayt, close to al-Zawra, standing and raising his hands before his face, not going beyond his head. He continued to raise them until the whiteness of his armpits appeared. Then he turned his back to the people while they were sitting, facing the qibla, saying amin to his supplication, based on what came from the Prophet (peace be upon him). Among what is prescribed is that he says: 'O Allah, give us rain' i.e., rain, 'aiding' with damma on the first letter, i.e., rescuing from hardship, 'wholesome' with madd and hamza, i.e., nothing spoils it, or it makes animals grow without harm, 'salutary' with fatha on the first letter and with madd and hamza, i.e., praiseworthy outcome, the wholesome beneficial outwardly and the salutary beneficial inwardly, 'fertile' with damma on the meem and with tahtaiyya, i.e., bringing fertility, which is increase of greenery, 'abundant' i.e., much water, 'covering' with kasra on the lam, i.e., covering the horizon by its generality, 'pouring' with fatha on the seen and shaddah on the ha, i.e., heavy falling on the ground, 'encompassing' with fatha on the first letter, i.e., covering the earth until it encompasses it, 'permanent' until the need ends, and he also supplicates with everything similar to it, secretly or publicly. It is established from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'O Allah, give us rain, aiding, beneficial, not harmful, immediate, not delayed. O Allah, give water to Your servants and Your animals, spread Your mercy, and revive Your dead land. O Allah, You are Allah, there is no god but You, the Self-Sufficient, and we are the poor. Send down upon us the rain and make what You send down for us a provision towards good.' ... And Abu Dawud narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the people complained to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) about the lack of rain, so he ordered a pulpit to be set up for him in the prayer ground and promised the people a day to go out. She said: He went out when the edge of the sun appeared, sat on the pulpit, said takbir and praised Allah, then said: 'You have complained of the drought of your lands and the delay of rain from its season upon you, and Allah has commanded you to supplicate Him and promised to respond. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, Master of the Day of Judgment, there is no god but Allah, He does what He wills. You are Allah, the Self-Sufficient, and we are the poor. Send down upon us the rain and make what You send down for us a provision towards good.' His saying: 'You are Allah, the Self-Sufficient' and in another version 'You are Allah, there is no god but You, the Self-Sufficient' end. Your blessings.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi comments on the etiquette of the istisqa (rain prayer). It begins with a discussion on tawassul (seeking intercession) through the Prophet's companions and the permissibility of gathering for istisqa. The main ruling: the imam should face the qibla while supplicating and raise his hands. The proof is the hadith of Umar describing the Prophet's practice at the stones of Zayt near al-Zawra. The Prophet raised his hands until his armpits were visible, then turned his back to the people while they remained seated facing qibla, echoing his supplication with 'amin'. The text then details the recommended supplication, explaining each term: 'ghaythan' (rain), 'mughtihan' (aiding from hardship), 'hani'an' (wholesome), 'mari'an' (salutary), 'muri'an' (fertile), 'ghadaqan' (abundant), 'mujallalan' (covering), 'sahan' (pouring), 'tabaqan' (encompassing), and 'da'iman' (permanent). The hadith from Aisha about the Prophet's istisqa sermon on the pulpit is also cited, showing the complete procedure. The passage highlights that the imam's actions are sunnah based on prophetic practice, and the hands should be raised higher than usual in istisqa, unlike other supplications.

Key Terms
الاستسقاء (al-istisqa): The prayer and supplication for rain when there is drought.
مستقبل القبلة (mustaqbil al-qiblah): Facing the qibla (direction of the Kaaba) during the supplication.
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during supplication, in istisqa raised higher than usual until armpits show.
غيث (ghayth): Rain that brings rescue and relief from drought.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He raises them until his armpits are visible, palms facing the sky.
C) He raises them to his chest, then turns them to the ground.
D) He does not raise his hands at all.

Key Takeaway
The istisqa supplication is a sunnah act with specific postures (facing qibla, raising hands high, turning for amin) established by the Prophet's practice.

Beneficial Rain and Cloak-Turning in Istisqa
Commentary defining beneficial rain and stating Hanafi ruling on cloak-turning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on turning the cloak during istisqa and distinguish it from the practice of other schools.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, turning the cloak during the prayer for rain is not part of the sunnah, contrary to other schools.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi explains the linguistic descriptions of beneficial rain and then addresses a disputed practice: turning one's cloak during the istisqa prayer. The commentator clarifies that according to Imam Abu Hanifah, this action is not part of the prescribed sunnah, distinguishing the Hanafi position from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Understand the lexical descriptions of beneficial rain
Identify the various terms (mura'ah, ghadaq, mujallal, sahhan, tabaq, da'im) which describe rain that brings increase, abundance, coverage, heavy fall, and duration. These are not legal rulings but linguistic elaborations.
The focus is on vocabulary, not fiqh.
2
Recognize the sunnah supplication (dua) for rain
The passage quotes the authentic supplication of the Prophet (ﷺ) for rain, indicating that the core act of istisqa is supplication, said secretly or openly.
The dua is the essence of istisqa.
3
Note the post-rain and removal supplications
When rain falls, one says 'O Allah, a beneficial rain'; when asking to lift it from certain places, one says 'around us, not on us, on the hills...'.
These are recommended expressions.
4
Focus on the key ruling: no turning of the cloak
The passage explicitly states: 'وليس فيه أي الاستسقاء قلب رداء عند أبي حنيفة' – there is no turning of the cloak in istisqa according to Abu Hanifah. This is the central legal point.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position.
5
Recognize the intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab difference
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani reportedly allowed turning the cloak based on hadith, but Abu Hanifah holds it is abrogated or not required. Other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) consider it sunnah. The mufta bihi (relied-upon view) is Abu Hanifah's position.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

The Book of Prayer. The beneficial rain: it is beneficial inwardly, bringing increase (muri'an) with damm on the meem and tahtaniyyah, meaning bringing the fourth (rub') which is increase of fertility... (gadaqan) meaning abundant water... (mujallalan) meaning covering the horizon due to its generality or the earth with vegetation like the covering of a horse... (sahhan) meaning severe in falling on the earth from sahha... (tabaqan) meaning covering the earth until it encompasses it... (da'iman) until the need for it ends. And he also supplicates with everything similar to what we have mentioned suitable to the occasion, secretly or openly. And it is established from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'O Allah, give us a beneficial rain, nourishing, not harmful, soon not delayed; O Allah, give water to your servants and your animals, spread your mercy, and revive your dead land. O Allah, You are Allah, there is no god but You, the Self-Sufficient, and we are the poor, send down upon us rain, and make what You send down a provision for good.' ... (and so on). And there is no turning of the cloak in the istisqa according to Abu Hanifah.
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (hashiya) on the matn of Maraqi al-Falah, explaining the description of beneficial rain (al-mura'ah) and the supplication for rain. The commentator first defines various terms for beneficial rain: 'muri'an' meaning bringing increase and fertility; 'ghadaq' meaning abundant water; 'mujallal' meaning covering the earth like a horse's blanket; 'sahh' meaning heavy downpour; 'tabaq' meaning covering all; 'da'im' meaning lasting until the need is satisfied. Then it states that one may supplicate with any similar words, either silently or aloud. The authentic supplication of the Prophet (ﷺ) is quoted: 'O Allah, give us a beneficial rain...' Then the passage mentions that when rain falls, one says: 'O Allah, a beneficial rain'; and when asking to lift it from certain places, one says: 'O Allah, around us, not on us, on the hills, mountains, valleys, and tree plantations.' The key ruling stated here is that, according to Imam Abu Hanifah, there is no turning of the cloak (heart of the garment) during the istisqa prayer. This is a distinctive Hanafi position, as other imams consider it sunnah.

Key Terms
المراعة (al-mura'ah): A type of beneficial rain that increases vegetation and fertility
قلب رداء (qalb al-rida'): Turning one's cloak or garment (reversing it) during the istisqa prayer
استسقاء (istisqa'): Prayer for rain

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is sunnah
B) It is obligatory
C) It is not part of the istisqa
D) It is recommended only in severe drought

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, turning the cloak during istisqa is not a prescribed sunnah; the relied-upon position is that it is not part of the prayer, though other schools practice it.

The Du'as of Rain and Their Etiquette
Recommended acts during rain and thunder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended supplications for rain and thunder and explain the sunnah of exposing oneself to the rain based on Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Rain is a blessing; supplication is recommended, and exposing to it seeks barakah.

Rainfall is a moment of divine mercy. The Hanafi school teaches specific supplications and etiquettes for this time. This lesson draws from the commentary on Maraqi al-Falah to outline the sunnah acts and ad'iyah when rain falls or thunder is heard.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two key supplications
Identify the supplication for beneficial rain: 'Allahumma sayyiban nafi'an' and the supplication for diversion when rain is harmful: 'Allahumma hawalina wa la 'alayna'.
Both are recommended, not obligatory.
2
Understand the wisdom behind the diversion du'a
The du'a asks for rain to fall on distant lands (hills, valleys) rather than directly on homes and roads, showing that one should seek removal of harm while preserving benefit.
This exemplifies the principle of not rejecting Allah's decree but asking for ease.
3
Learn the sunnah of exposing the body to rain
The Prophet (saw) uncovered his arms during rain because it is a recent covenant with its Lord. This is a recommended act to receive barakah.
The private parts must remain covered.
4
Recite the thunder supplication
When hearing thunder, one should say: 'Subhana man yusabbihu ar-ra'du bihamdihi wa al-mala'ikatu' and add 'wa huwa 'ala kulli shay'in qadeer' for protection.
If struck by lightning, it is considered martyrdom (diya is due).
5
Summarize the etiquettes
Praise Allah for rain, avoid superstitious statements like 'we received rain due to such star', and supplicate during rainfall as it is a time of acceptance.
All these acts are mustahabb (recommended).

Upon us the rain, and make what You have sent down a strength and a provision until a time. Then when they were rained upon, they said by way of recommendation: O Allah, a beneficial downpour. And when they sought its removal from places, they said: O Allah, around us and not upon us, on the hills, the small mountains, the valleys, and the thickets of trees. (And there is in it – i.e., the istisqa' – no reversal of the cloak) according to Abu Hanifa. Then he raised his hands and continued raising until the whiteness of his armpits appeared, then he turned his back to the people and reversed (his cloak), or he reversed his cloak while raising his hands, then he faced the people, descended, and prayed two rak'ahs. Then Allah Almighty created a cloud which thundered and lightened, then it rained by Allah's permission, and he did not come to his mosque until the torrents flowed. When he saw their haste to shelter, he laughed until his molars appeared and said: I bear witness that Allah is capable of all things and that I am His slave and messenger. His statement: 'to a time' – the narration is with kha' and ya' and ra', meaning against evil. His statement: 'O Allah, a downpour' – it is an object with the verb omitted, meaning 'make it a downpour', and the downpour is rain. And in a narration of Nasa'i: 'O Allah, make it a beneficial flood' and another: 'a gentle downpour', so all narrations are reconciled. And one says 'We have been given rain by Allah's favor and mercy' and not by such and such asterism, due to the prohibition. And it is recommended to supplicate at the descent of rain because it is a time when supplication is answered, and to expose the body except the private parts so it hits him and he purifies from it, and to praise Allah Almighty. Based on Anas: Rain fell upon us while we were with the Messenger of Allah, so he uncovered his garment until the rain hit him. We said: O Messenger of Allah, why did you do this? He said: Because it has a recent covenant with its Lord. That is, its formation and descent. And from Ibn Abbas: When rain came, he used to order a servant of his to bring his bed out to the rain, and when asked why, he said: Have you not read 'And We sent down from the sky blessed water'? So I love that some of its blessing reaches me. And it is recommended for one who fears thunder to say: Glory be to Him whom the thunder glorifies with His praise and the angels. It was reported from Umar. And Ibn Abbas said: Whoever hears the thunder and says that, adding 'and He is capable of all things' – if he is struck by a thunderbolt, then his blood money is due. His statement: 'and when they sought' is passive; it is better to say 'they sought' to match 'they said'. His statement: 'O Allah, around us' – with fatha on the lam, meaning 'make it around us', and he explained it as 'on the hills', i.e., on places where rain does not harm, not on buildings and roads. His statement: 'and not upon us' – do not make it upon us. His statement: 'O Allah, on the hills' – the hills are piles of earth, and the small mountains are small mountains. The teacher said: In this is guidance to teach us etiquette in this supplication, since he did not ask for its removal absolutely because it is needed continuously for some valleys and farms until sufficiency which Allah knows, so he asked for prevention of its harm and continuation of its benefit. And in it is notification that when a blessing is accompanied by a hindrance, one should not be resentful, so he asks Allah to remove the hindrance and preserve the blessing. And supplication for removal of harm does not contradict trust and delegation. His statement: 'and the valleys' – because with the accumulation of water there is benefit from irrigation and drinking for animals and birds. His statement: And Abu Yusuf in one narration from him, and what Muhammad narrated is interpreted as good omen. And he does not deliver a sermon according to Abu Hanifa because it is subsidiary to the congregational prayer, and there is no congregation in his view. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does deliver a sermon, but according to Abu Yusuf it is one sermon, and according to Muhammad it is two sermons. And no dhimmi attends it (the istisqa'), due to Umar's prohibition, and they should not be allowed to go out alone either because they might be given rain and thus the weak-minded may be tempted.
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the istisqa' (rain prayer) section from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah. It begins by discussing the recommended supplications when rain falls and when seeking its diversion. The author cites a hadith describing the Prophet's actions during istisqa', including raising hands, reversing the cloak, and praying two rak'ahs, after which rain came. The commentary then explains the wording of various supplications: 'اللهم صيبا نافعا' (O Allah, a beneficial downpour) and 'اللهم حوالينا ولا علينا' (O Allah, around us and not upon us). It mentions the virtue of supplication at the time of rain and the sunnah of exposing the body to the rain, based on hadith. The passage also covers the etiquette of hearing thunder and the recommended supplication. The second part of the passage addresses three intra-Hanafi disputes: (1) the reversal of the cloak by the imam—Abu Hanifa holds it is not part of the sunnah, but the Sahibayn differ; (2) the khutbah (sermon) in istisqa'—Abu Hanifa says there is no khutbah, while Abu Yusuf says one sermon and Muhammad says two; (3) the attendance of dhimmis—they are prohibited from attending because their presence may lead to fitnah if Allah answers their supplication. The author explains the reasoning: the imam's cloak reversal is not required because the reported action about the Prophet was done by him specifically, not commanded generally. The difference regarding the khutbah stems from whether the istisqa' prayer is considered a congregational prayer (Abu Hanifa sees it as having no congregation in the sense that the khutbah is not prescribed). The prohibition of dhimmis is based on Umar's practice and fear of fitnah.

Key Terms
صيب (sayyib): A heavy downpour of rain.
حوالينا ولا علينا (hawalina wa la 'alayna): Supplication requesting rain to fall around, not directly on, one's location.
رعد (ra'd): Thunder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) اللهم حوالينا ولا علينا
C) مطرنا بفضل الله
D) سبحان من يسبح الرعد

Key Takeaway
The sunnah teaches us to ask for benefit and protection from harm simultaneously during rainfall.

intermediate

Intra-Hanafi Disputes on Istisqa' Prayer: Cloak Reversal, Khutbah, and Dhimmi Attendance
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on istisqa' rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three points of difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the istisqa' prayer and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa's view — no cloak reversal, no khutbah, no dhimmi attendance — is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

The istisqa' prayer, while established in the sunnah, has specific rulings that differ among the Hanafi imams. This passage details the three main disputes: reversal of the cloak, the number of khutbahs, and the attendance of dhimmis. Understanding these ikhtilafat helps in applying the correct practice.

Guided Path
1
State the three issues
Identify (a) the ruling on the imam reversing his cloak, (b) the number of khutbahs, (c) the attendance of dhimmis. These are the points of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
The text also mentions the differing views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
2
Present Abu Hanifa's position on each
Abu Hanifa holds: (a) No cloak reversal; (b) No khutbah; (c) Dhimmis are prohibited from attending.
His reasoning: the cloak reversal was a specific action of the Prophet, not a general command; the istisqa' prayer is not a congregational prayer that warrants a khutbah.
3
Present the Sahibayn's positions
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold: (a) Cloak reversal is sunnah; (b) Khutbah is given — Abu Yusuf says one, Muhammad says two; (c) They also prohibit dhimmis (no disagreement).
Their evidence is the hadith of the Prophet's actions.
4
Analyze the evidence for the disputes
For the cloak reversal, the hadith shows the Prophet did it, but Abu Hanifa sees it as a specific action (fi'l) not a general sunnah; the Sahibayn see it as a general sunnah. For the khutbah, the dispute stems from whether the prayer is considered a congregational prayer.
The prohibition of dhimmis is based on Umar's practice to avoid fitnah.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The author presents Abu Hanifa's views first and the tone suggests they are the relied-upon positions. In practice, Hanafis do not reverse the cloak and do not deliver a khutbah during istisqa'.
Dhimmis are also not allowed to attend.
