⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علينا الغيث، واجعل ما أنزلت لنا قوة وبلاغاً إلى حين فإذا أمطروا قالوا استحباباً : اللهم صيبا نافعاً وإذا طلب رفعه عن الأماكن قالوا : اللهم حوالينا ولا علينا على الأكام والظراب وبطون الأودية، ومنابت الشجر (وليس فيه أي الاستسقاء قلب رداء) عند أبي حنيفة [؟] ثم رفع يديه فلم يزل في الرفع حتى بدا بياض إبطيه ثم حوّل إلى الناس ظهره وقلب، أو حوّل رداءه وهو رافع يديه، ثم أقبل على الناس، ونزل فصلى ركعتين فأنشأ الله تعالى سحابة فرعدت، وبرقت، ثم أمطرت بإذن الله تعالى، فلم يأت مسجده حتى سالت السيول فلما رأى سرعتهم إلى الكن ضحك حتى بدت نواجذه وقال : أشهد أن الله على كل شيء قدير وأني عبده ورسوله قوله : (إلى حين الرواية بالخاء المعجمة، والياء المثناة من تحت والراء. المهملة ضد الشر. قوله : (اللهم (صيباً مصوب بفعل محذوف أي اجعله صيباً، والصيب المطر وهو بتشديد الياء، وفي رواية النسائي اللهم اجعله سيباً نافعاً بفتح السين المهملة، وسكون الياء قال الخطابي : أي نافعاً وفي رواية النسائي صيباً هيناً فيجمع بين الروايات كلها، ويقول مطرنا بفضل الله ورحمته بنوء كذا للنهي عنه، ويستحب الدعاء عند نزول الغيث لما ورد من استجابة الدعاء عنده، وأن يكشف عن غير عورته ليصيبه ويتظهر منه، ويحمد الله تعالى لما عن أنس أصابنا مطر ونحن مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فحسر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ثوبه حتى أصابه المطر، فقلنا: يا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لم صنعت هذا قال: لأنه حديث عهد بربه اهـ. أي تكوينه. وتنزيله وعن ابن عباس : كان إذا جاء المطر يأمر عبداً له أن يخرج فراشه إلى المطر فقيل له في ذلك، فقال: أما قرأت وأنزلنا من السماء ماء مباركاً فأحب أن ينالني من بركته، ويستحب قاله من خيفته فإن الرعد أن يقول سبحان من يسبح الرعد بحمده والملائكة . سمع عوفي من الرعد كما ورد عن عمر وقال ابن عباس : من سمع صوت الرعد، فقال ذلك وزاد: وهو على كل شيء قدير فإن أصابته صاعقة فعلى ديته. قوله : (وإذا طلب) بالبناء للمجهول، والأولى أن يقول طلبوا ليناسب قوله قالوا قوله : (اللهم حوالينا) بفتح اللام أي اجعله حوالينا، وفسره بقوله على الآكام أي اجعله على الأماكن التي لا يضرها المطر على على الأبنية والطرق. قوله : ( ولا علينا أي ولا تجعله علينا . قوله : (اللهم على الأكام) بكسر الهمزة كإم ويفتحها مع المد. أكمة بفتحات، وهو التراب المجتمع، والظراب بكسر الظاء المشالة جمع آخره باء موحدة جمع ظرب بفتح فسكون، وهو الجبل الصغير، ووهم من قاله بالضاد قال في الشرح : وفيه إرشاد لتعليمنا الأدب في هذا الدعاء حيث لم يدع برفعه مطلقاً لأنه يحتاج إليه مستمراً بالنسبة لبعض الأودية والمزارع إلى حصول الكفاية التي يعلمها الله فطلب منع ضرره، وبقاء نفعه، وفيه إعلام بأنه إذا قارن النعمة عارض لا يتسخط منه، فيسأل الله تعالى رفع العارض، وبقاء النعمة والدعاء برفع الضار لا ينافي التوكل، والتفويض. قوله: (وبطون الأودية) لأنه باجتماع الماء فيها يحصل ارتفاق بالسقي منها وشرب البهائم، والطيور. قوله: وأبي يوسف في رواية عنه وما رواه محمد محمول على التفاؤل، ولا يخطب عند أبي حنيفة لأنها تبع للصلاة بالجماعة ولا جماعة عنده وعندهما يخطب لكن عند أبي يوسف خطبة واحدة، وعند محمد خطيتين ولا يحضره) أي الاستسقاء (ذمي) لنهي عمر رضي الله عنه ولا فعله يمكنون من وحدهم أيضاً لاحتمال أن يسقوا فقد يفتن به ضعفاء العوام.
Upon us the rain, and make what You have sent down a strength and a provision until a time. Then when they were rained upon, they said by way of recommendation: O Allah, a beneficial downpour. And when they sought its removal from places, they said: O Allah, around us and not upon us, on the hills, the small mountains, the valleys, and the thickets of trees. (And there is in it – i.e., the istisqa' – no reversal of the cloak) according to Abu Hanifa. Then he raised his hands and continued raising until the whiteness of his armpits appeared, then he turned his back to the people and reversed (his cloak), or he reversed his cloak while raising his hands, then he faced the people, descended, and prayed two rak'ahs. Then Allah Almighty created a cloud which thundered and lightened, then it rained by Allah's permission, and he did not come to his mosque until the torrents flowed. When he saw their haste to shelter, he laughed until his molars appeared and said: I bear witness that Allah is capable of all things and that I am His slave and messenger. His statement: 'to a time' – the narration is with kha' and ya' and ra', meaning against evil. His statement: 'O Allah, a downpour' – it is an object with the verb omitted, meaning 'make it a downpour', and the downpour is rain. And in a narration of Nasa'i: 'O Allah, make it a beneficial flood' and another: 'a gentle downpour', so all narrations are reconciled. And one says 'We have been given rain by Allah's favor and mercy' and not by such and such asterism, due to the prohibition. And it is recommended to supplicate at the descent of rain because it is a time when supplication is answered, and to expose the body except the private parts so it hits him and he purifies from it, and to praise Allah Almighty. Based on Anas: Rain fell upon us while we were with the Messenger of Allah, so he uncovered his garment until the rain hit him. We said: O Messenger of Allah, why did you do this? He said: Because it has a recent covenant with its Lord. That is, its formation and descent. And from Ibn Abbas: When rain came, he used to order a servant of his to bring his bed out to the rain, and when asked why, he said: Have you not read 'And We sent down from the sky blessed water'? So I love that some of its blessing reaches me. And it is recommended for one who fears thunder to say: Glory be to Him whom the thunder glorifies with His praise and the angels. It was reported from Umar. And Ibn Abbas said: Whoever hears the thunder and says that, adding 'and He is capable of all things' – if he is struck by a thunderbolt, then his blood money is due. His statement: 'and when they sought' is passive; it is better to say 'they sought' to match 'they said'. His statement: 'O Allah, around us' – with fatha on the lam, meaning 'make it around us', and he explained it as 'on the hills', i.e., on places where rain does not harm, not on buildings and roads. His statement: 'and not upon us' – do not make it upon us. His statement: 'O Allah, on the hills' – the hills are piles of earth, and the small mountains are small mountains. The teacher said: In this is guidance to teach us etiquette in this supplication, since he did not ask for its removal absolutely because it is needed continuously for some valleys and farms until sufficiency which Allah knows, so he asked for prevention of its harm and continuation of its benefit. And in it is notification that when a blessing is accompanied by a hindrance, one should not be resentful, so he asks Allah to remove the hindrance and preserve the blessing. And supplication for removal of harm does not contradict trust and delegation. His statement: 'and the valleys' – because with the accumulation of water there is benefit from irrigation and drinking for animals and birds. His statement: And Abu Yusuf in one narration from him, and what Muhammad narrated is interpreted as good omen. And he does not deliver a sermon according to Abu Hanifa because it is subsidiary to the congregational prayer, and there is no congregation in his view. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does deliver a sermon, but according to Abu Yusuf it is one sermon, and according to Muhammad it is two sermons. And no dhimmi attends it (the istisqa'), due to Umar's prohibition, and they should not be allowed to go out alone either because they might be given rain and thus the weak-minded may be tempted.
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the istisqa' (rain prayer) section from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah. It begins by discussing the recommended supplications when rain falls and when seeking its diversion. The author cites a hadith describing the Prophet's actions during istisqa', including raising hands, reversing the cloak, and praying two rak'ahs, after which rain came. The commentary then explains the wording of various supplications: 'اللهم صيبا نافعا' (O Allah, a beneficial downpour) and 'اللهم حوالينا ولا علينا' (O Allah, around us and not upon us). It mentions the virtue of supplication at the time of rain and the sunnah of exposing the body to the rain, based on hadith. The passage also covers the etiquette of hearing thunder and the recommended supplication. The second part of the passage addresses three intra-Hanafi disputes: (1) the reversal of the cloak by the imam—Abu Hanifa holds it is not part of the sunnah, but the Sahibayn differ; (2) the khutbah (sermon) in istisqa'—Abu Hanifa says there is no khutbah, while Abu Yusuf says one sermon and Muhammad says two; (3) the attendance of dhimmis—they are prohibited from attending because their presence may lead to fitnah if Allah answers their supplication. The author explains the reasoning: the imam's cloak reversal is not required because the reported action about the Prophet was done by him specifically, not commanded generally. The difference regarding the khutbah stems from whether the istisqa' prayer is considered a congregational prayer (Abu Hanifa sees it as having no congregation in the sense that the khutbah is not prescribed). The prohibition of dhimmis is based on Umar's practice and fear of fitnah.

Key Terms
قلب رداء (qalb al-rida'): The action of the imam reversing his cloak (changing which side faces outward) during the istisqa' prayer.
خطبة الاستسقاء (khutbat al-istisqa'): The sermon delivered during the istisqa' prayer.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen of the Islamic state who is granted protection (dhimmah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, how many khutbahs are delivered in the istisqa' prayer?
A) Two khutbahs
B) One khutbah
C) No khutbah
D) A short sermon after the prayer

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's view—no cloak reversal, no khutbah, no dhimmi attendance—is the established Hanafi position for istisqa'.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Salat al-Khawf: Ruling and Linguistic Basis
Definition of Salat al-Khawf with its ruling and an explanation of its basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salat al-Khawf, identify its condition (shart), and explain the idafah (construct phrase) analysis of the term.

Core Idea
Salat al-Khawf is permissible even with mild fear; the imam does not reverse his cloak.

This lesson introduces the Chapter of Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer). The passage defines this special form of prayer, establishes its permissibility in the presence of an enemy, and clarifies that the Prophet's Companions did not reverse their cloaks during this prayer. Additionally, the author provides a subtle linguistic analysis of the term 'صلاة الخوف' (fear prayer), explaining whether 'fear' is a condition or a cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the phrase 'Salat al-Khawf is permissible in the presence of an enemy'. Note that the ruling is permissibility (jāʼiz), not obligation or Sunnah.
The Arabic phrase is 'جائزة بحضور عدو'.
2
Understand the condition (shart)
The permissibility is tied to the presence of an enemy. The commentary explains this as a condition—without an enemy, the normal prayer is performed.
The text says 'لوجود المبيح' i.e., due to the existence of the permissibility (the enemy).
3
Note the practice regarding cloak reversal
The passage denies the practice of reversing the cloak (qalb al-ridāʼ) in this prayer. The Imam (Abū Ḥanīfa) accepted the hadith about turning but did not consider it from the Sunnah.
The Companions like ʿUmar did not do it, so it is not recommended.
4
Analyze the idafah (construct phrase)
The phrase 'صلاة الخوف' is analyzed: does it add prayer to 'fear' as a condition (shart) or a cause (sabab)? The author of the hashya sides with condition, because the specific manner requires the enemy.
This linguistic point affects the legal reasoning: condition means prayer is invalid without it; cause means fear is the reason for the concession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الخوف أي صلاته بالصفة الآتية (جائزة بحضور عدو) لوجود المبيح وإن لم يشتد الخوف (وليس فيه قلب رداء ) لعدم فعل الصحابة له كعمر وغيره ولم ينكر الإمام التحويل الوارد في الأحاديث، بل أنكر كونه من السنة. مع قوله : (من إضافة الشيء إلى شرطه) باعتبار عدم جوازها بدونه، أو إلى سببه باعتبار الترخيص، وفي شرح السيد عن حاشية المؤلف أنها من إضافة الشيء إلى شرطه نظراً إلى الكيفية المخصوصة لأنّ هذه الصفة شرطها العدو، ومن قال أن سببها الخوف نظر إلى أنّ . سبب أصل
Chapter of the Fear Prayer: i.e., its prayer in the following manner (is permissible in the presence of an enemy) due to the existence of the permissibility, even if fear is not intense. (And there is no reversal of the cloak in it) because the Companions (like Umar and others) did not do it, and the Imam did not deny the turning reported in the hadith, but denied it being from the Sunnah. And his statement: (of adding a thing to its condition) considering that it is not permissible without it, or to its cause considering the concession. And in the commentary of al-Sayyid from the author's gloss, that it is adding a thing to its condition in view of the specific manner, because this quality has the enemy as its condition, and whoever says its cause is fear, looks to that. Reason origin.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage introduces the Chapter of Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer). It defines the prayer as a specific manner of praying that is permissible when an enemy is present, even if the fear is not severe. The text notes that in this prayer, the imam does not reverse his cloak (unlike in istisqa'), because the Companions like Umar did not do so, and the Imam (Abu Hanifa) did not deny the narration about turning but denied that it is from the Sunnah (i.e., not a recommended practice). The commentary then discusses the linguistic point: the phrase 'باب صلاة الخوف' is an example of idafah (construct phrase) where 'صلاة' is added to 'الخوف' either as a condition (shart) meaning the prayer is not valid without fear, or as a cause (sabab) meaning the fear is the reason for the concession. The author of the hashya (Tahtawi) notes that according to al-Sayyid, the idafah is to the condition because the specific manner of this prayer requires the enemy as a condition, while others say it is to the cause (fear). The text ends abruptly, but the main ruling is clear: Salat al-Khawf is a permissible form of prayer with its own conditions.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): The fear prayer performed in a specific manner when Muslims are in the presence of an enemy during battle.
عدو (aduw): An enemy of the Muslims who is present and poses a threat during prayer.
قلب رداء (qalb al-rida'): Reversing the cloak; here it is denied in Salat al-Khawf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the cloak reversal not performed in Salat al-Khawf?
A) Because the hadith about turning is weak.
B) Because the Companions did not do it.
C) Because it is required in istisqa' but not in khawf.
D) Because fear must be intense to permit it.

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf is a permissible form of prayer conditioned on the presence of an enemy, with no cloak reversal, and the term 'صلاة الخوف' is analyzed as an idafah to the condition (shart) rather than the cause (sabab).

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Rulings of Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer)
Commentary on the conditions and method of Salat al-Khawf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf, identify the conditions for its validity, and apply the rulings when fear intensifies.

Core Idea
Salat al-Khawf divides the congregation into two groups, each praying part with the imam, following the Quranic instruction.

The prayer of fear (ṣalāt al-khawf) is a special concession granted when the enemy is present or there is danger of drowning or burning. The Hanafi school adopts a specific method that is closest to the apparent meaning of the Quran. This lesson explains the procedure, the conditions for its validity, and the rulings when fear becomes extreme.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause (sabab)
Determine the presence of an enemy or fear of drowning/burning as the trigger for this form of prayer. The mere presence of the enemy suffices, not necessarily active combat.
2
Understand the division into two groups
The imam divides the congregation into two groups (ṭā'ifatayn). One group stands facing the enemy for guarding, while the other prays with the imam.
The minimum for a group is one person.
3
Follow the prayer sequence
For a two-rak'ah prayer (Fajr or shortened travel prayer), the imam prays one rak'ah with the first group. For four-rak'ah prayers or Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with the first group. The first group then proceeds to the enemy on foot.
The two-rak'ah unit (shaf‘) is a condition for division; praying unequal numbers invalidates the prayer.
4
Identify invalid scenarios
If the first group rides or walks in a direction other than facing the enemy, their prayer is invalid. If the imam prays one rak'ah with the first and two with the second (or vice versa inappropriately), both prayers are invalid.
Invalidation occurs because each group departs at an improper time.
5
Apply rulings for intense fear
If fear intensifies (e.g., surprise attack), the congregation may pray individually while riding or on foot with gestures, facing any direction, as per Quran 2:239.
This is only valid outside the city; praying while riding in the city is invalid even in necessity.

Source Text

بالإيماء، أو رجالاً واقفين كذلك أي إلى أي جهة قدروا والأصل فيه قوله تعالى : فإن خفتم فرجالاً أو ركباناً) والصلاة ركباناً إنما تكون في غير المصر لأن التنفل في المصر راكباً لا يصح فالفرض أولى وإن كان لضرورة
The Book of Prayer. (And with fear of drowning from a flood or burning from fire, and when the people dispute about praying behind one imam, he makes them two groups and stations one group facing the enemy for guarding, and the imam prays with the other group one rak‘ah of a two-rak‘ah prayer (Fajr and the shortened prayer in travel), and he prays with the first mentioned group two rak‘ahs of a four-rak‘ah prayer or Maghrib, because the two-rak‘ah unit is a condition for its division; if he prayed one rak‘ah with the first group and two with the second, both their prayers would be invalid because each departs at an improper time. And this group proceeds towards the enemy on foot; if they ride or walk not towards the direction of the line facing the enemy, their prayer is invalid. And that group which was guarding comes and enters the prayer with the imam, and he prays with them the remainder of the prayer, and the imam makes taslim alone because his prayer is complete. Then they go to the direction of the enemy on foot. Then the first group comes if they wish, or if they want they complete their prayer in their place without recitation because they are 'lāḥiq', so they are effectively behind the imam and do not recite. And they make taslim or go to the enemy. Then the other group comes; if they wish they pray what remains in their place after the imam finishes and they make up with recitation because they are 'masbūq'. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Salat al-Khawf in this manner, and many narrations have been reported about it, the most authentic of which are sixteen different narrations, and the Prophet prayed it twenty-four times, all of which are permissible. The best and closest to the apparent meaning of the Quran is the method we have mentioned. (And if fear intensifies) so that they cannot perform the prayer in that way due to a surprise attack, they pray while riding, even if fleeing out of necessity, not while pursuing because there is no necessity for them, individually, because splitting a single rak‘ah is not possible, and the first group is more entitled to it due to precedence. His statement: 'each departing at an improper time' — as for the first group it is obvious, and as for the second, because when they catch the second rak‘ah they become part of the first group due to catching the first unit, and they had departed at the time of their return, so it is invalid. This is stated in the Sharh. His statement: 'facing the enemy' is connected to 'alignment'. His statement: 'and they go to the enemy' — implies they remain in their place and do not move, so it would be better to say 'they turn towards the enemy', and if it is not in the direction of the qiblah, and perhaps it is related to the author's statement itself, not to his statement 'if they wish'. His statement: 'and it has been reported' — in Zad al-Ma‘ad it is said: its origins are six descriptions, and some have reached more, and these people whenever they see variation in narrators they make it a different action, but it is actually variation in narrators. In Fath al-Bari it is said: this is the relied-upon view. And in al-Durr it is authenticated that he prayed it in four places: Dhat al-Riqa‘, Batan Nakhla, ‘Usfan, and Dhi Qarad. His statement: 'the closest to the apparent meaning of the Quran' is His statement: 'When you are among them and lead them in prayer, let a group of them stand with you and let them take their weapons; when they prostrate, let them be behind you; and let another group who have not prayed come and pray with you' [al-Nisa' 4:102]. The aspect of closeness is that His statement 'when they prostrate, let them be behind you' indicates the departure of the first group after prostration and the coming of the second group who have not prayed, and they are like the first in action, and this is exactly the described method. Note: In al-Mujtaba it is said: one performs the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) in Salat al-Khawf due to the generality of the hadith, and those behind him follow him; the lāḥiq performs it at the end of his prayer. It is not prescribed for a sinner in travel, so it is not valid for rebels (baghah) because sins in travel are enemies of Allah, but it is prescribed for others when the enemy is present. This is noted by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'they pray while riding with gestures, or on foot standing likewise, i.e., towards any direction they are able, and the origin is His statement: 'If you fear, then pray on foot or riding' [al-Baqarah 2:239]. Praying while riding is only valid outside the city because praying while riding in the city is not valid for supererogatory prayers, so obligatory prayer takes precedence even if out of necessity.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (hashiya) on the conditions and method of Salat al-Khawf (the prayer of fear) from the Hanafi perspective. The author explains that Salat al-Khawf is permissible when an enemy is present, even if there is no actual fear of attack—the mere presence of the enemy suffices as the apparent cause for the license. Similarly, fear of drowning or burning justifies this prayer. The text then details the procedure when the congregation disputes about praying behind a single imam: the imam divides them into two groups. One group stands facing the enemy for protection, while the imam prays one rak‘ah with the other group (for a two-rak‘ah prayer) or two rak‘ahs (for four-rak‘ah prayers or Maghrib). The first group then goes to the enemy's direction on foot; if they ride or walk elsewhere, their prayer is invalid. The guarding group then joins the imam for the remainder of the prayer. The imam completes his prayer alone (since his prayer is finished) and makes taslim. The first group may then either complete their prayer in place without recitation (as they are lāḥiq, effectively following the imam) or after going to the enemy. The second group completes what they missed with recitation (as they are masbūq). The preferred method is based on the Quranic verse (4:102). In intense fear (e.g., a surprise attack), they may pray while riding or walking, with gestures, individually, because splitting a single rak‘ah is impossible. The commentary also addresses that the prostration of forgetfulness applies in Salat al-Khawf, and that this prayer is not valid for rebellious Muslims (baghah) because they are sinners. The overall ruling is that Salat al-Khawf is jā'iz (permissible) as a form, while the original prayer remains fard. The authority is from the Hanafi school, with evidence from the Quran and Sunnah.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (Ṣalāt al-Khawf): The prayer performed when there is fear of the enemy, with specific modifications in form and action.
طائفة (ṭā'ifah): A group of people; here, one of the two groups into which the congregation is divided for Salat al-Khawf.
لاحق (lāḥiq): A person who joins the imam late but has caught up with the imam's prayer before the imam completes it; he follows the imam in the remaining prayer and does not recite.
مسبوق (masbūq): A person who misses part of the prayer with the imam and must complete what he missed after the imam's taslim, reciting in the missed rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the imam prays one rak'ah with the first group and two with the second in a Fajr prayer, what is the ruling?
A) Both prayers are valid.
B) The first group's prayer is valid, the second's is invalid.
C) Both prayers are invalid.
D) The prayer is valid only if the first group goes to the enemy on foot.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi Salat al-Khawf uses a two-group system where each group prays part with the imam, and the method closest to the Quran is the preferred one.

Rulings and Method of Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer)
Explaining the method, proofs, and disputes regarding the fear prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of salat al-khawf and explain the ruling on carrying weapons, distinguishing the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i/Maliki view.

Core Idea
The fear prayer adapts the obligatory prayer to battle conditions; carrying weapons is recommended, not obligatory, because it is not part of the prayer's essential actions.

The fear prayer (salat al-khawf) is a unique adaptation of the obligatory prayer when facing the enemy. This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi details the preferred method based on the Prophet's practice and the Quranic verse (4:102). It also addresses a key dispute: whether carrying weapons is obligatory or merely recommended. By the end, you will not only know the method but understand the Hanafi reasoning behind the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that salat al-khawf is a sunnah method for performing the fard prayer in battle. The underlying prayer remains fard, but the form is sunnah muakkadah.
The passage begins by completing a ruling from the previous page, then details the method.
2
Outline the preferred method
Trace the sequence: first group prays one rak'ah with the imam, then goes to face the enemy on foot. The second group then prays the remaining rak'ah with the imam. The imam finishes alone, then the second group goes to face the enemy. The first group completes their prayer without recitation (as lahiqun), and the second group makes up with recitation (as masbuqun).
The text emphasizes that this method is closest to the apparent meaning of the Quran.
3
Locate the dalil
Identify the Quranic evidence (Surah An-Nisa 4:102) and the numerous sunnah narrations. The Prophet performed the fear prayer in many ways, all permissible.
The passage mentions sixteen authentic narrations and that the Prophet prayed it twenty-four times.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the Quranic verse indicates the method: 'And when they have prostrated, let them be behind you and let another group who has not prayed come and pray with you.' The command is taken as a recommendation (nadb), not obligation.
The Hanafi principle: commands regarding prayer actions are only for the prayer itself; weapons are extraneous.
5
Analyze the ikhtilaf on carrying weapons
Contrast the Hanafi view (mustahabb) with the Shafi'i/Maliki view (wajib). The Hanafi response: the Quranic command is for recommendation because carrying weapons is not among the essential actions of the prayer.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): leaving weapons is not sinful for Hanafis but would be for Shafi'is.

Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the fear prayer (salat al-khawf). It begins by completing a ruling from the previous page: if the first group incorrectly returns (e.g., riding or walking in the wrong direction) their prayer becomes void. Then it describes the correct method: the first group goes to guard, the second group prays one rak'ah with the Imam, then the Imam prays the remaining rak'ah alone and gives salam, and the second group goes to face the enemy. The first group then either completes their prayer in place (without recitation, as they are laahiqun) or goes to the enemy. The second group (the ones who guarded) either prays what remains in their place (since the Imam finished) and makes up with recitation (as they are masbuqoon). The author confirms that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) performed the fear prayer in this manner, and there are sixteen authentic narrations with variations, all permissible. The preferred method is the one described, as it matches the apparent meaning of Quran 4:102. If fear intensifies, one may pray on horseback or individually with gestures, because following an Imam is invalid due to the difference of place (except if riding behind the same mount). The prayer is not valid without actual presence of the enemy; if they mistake a shape for the enemy, they must repeat (but not the Imam). Carrying weapons during the fear prayer is recommended (mustahabb) in the Hanafi school, while Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i consider it obligatory (wajib) based on the command in the Quran. The Hanafi response is that the command is for recommendation because carrying weapons is not part of the prayer's actions. If the congregation does not dispute, it is better for each group to pray with a separate Imam, like in normal security, to avoid walking excessively. This is from Fath al-Qadir. The passage ends with a supplication.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): A specific way of performing obligatory prayers when facing the enemy in battle, with variations in form to maintain security.
لاحق (lahiq): A person who comes late but joins the imam during the prayer; he does not recite behind the imam.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who misses part of the prayer and makes up the remaining rak'ahs after the imam's salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits multiple methods for the fear prayer but emphasizes the two-group method and considers carrying weapons recommended, not obligatory.

Carrying Weapons in Salat al-Khawf: The Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on prayer during fear with inter-madhhab dispute on carrying weapons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that carrying weapons in fear prayer is mustahabb (recommended) and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Carrying weapons in fear prayer is recommended, not obligatory, because it is not an act of prayer.

The Quranic command to take weapons during fear prayer appears imperative, leading some schools to deem it obligatory. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes between the actions of prayer and external actions, classifying it as recommended. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and practical consequences of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school says carrying weapons in Salat al-Khawf is mustahabb (recommended). The text says 'يستحب حمل الصلاح'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i hold that it is obligatory (wajib) based on the imperative in the Quran.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their dalil is the verse: 'ولْيأخذوا أسلحتهم' (Surah al-Nisa 4:102). In Usul al-Fiqh, the imperative (amr) generally indicates obligation unless there is a qarina (indication) to the contrary.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that carrying weapons is not among the actions of prayer (laysa min a'mal al-salah). The imperative is therefore interpreted as recommendation (nadb) because the act is external; a qarina overrides the default obligation.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that commands related to non-prayer acts during prayer are for recommendation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Hanafis, omitting the weapon carries no sin; according to the opposing schools, it is sinful. This affects the ruling on the prayer's validity and the worshipper's accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يصح الاقتداء لاختلاف المكان إلا أن يكون رديفاً لإمامه ولم تجز صلاة الخوف بلا حضور عدو حتى لو ظنوا سواداً عدواً وتبين بخلافه أعادوها دون الإمام ويستحب حمل الصلاح في الصلاة عند الخوف وقال الإمام مالك والشافعي رحمهما الله تعالى بوجوبه للأمر، قلنا هو للندب لأنه ليس من أعمال الصلاة وإن لم يتنازعوا أي القوم في الصلاة خلف إمام واحد فالأفضل صلاة كل طائفة مقتدين بإمام واحد فتذهب الأولى بعد تمامها ثم تجيء الأخرى فتصلي بإمام آخر مثل حالة الأمن للتوقي عن المشي ونحوه كذا في فتح القدير وهو حسبي ونعم الوكيل .
It is valid to follow [an imam] due to difference of place unless he is riding behind his imam. And the prayer of fear is not valid without the presence of an enemy, so that even if they thought a black mass was an enemy and it turned out otherwise, they repeat it but not the imam. And it is recommended to carry weapons in prayer during fear. Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on them) said it is obligatory due to the command. We say it is for recommendation because it is not from the actions of the prayer. And if they do not dispute, i.e., the people, in prayer behind one imam, then the best is for each group to pray following one imam, so the first goes after completing it, then the other comes and prays with another imam, like the state of safety, to avoid walking and the like. Thus in Fath al-Qadir, and He is sufficient and the best Trustee.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage discusses rulings for Salat al-Khawf (fear prayer). First, it states that it is permissible for a follower to be in a different place from the imam, except when the follower is riding behind the imam (then they must be in the same place). The fear prayer itself is only valid when the enemy is actually present; if they mistakenly thought a black object was the enemy and it turned out not to be, they must repeat their prayer, but the imam's prayer is valid. Regarding carrying weapons during fear prayer, the Hanafi school holds it is recommended (mustahabb) based on the verse 'and let them take their weapons' [4:102] being interpreted as a recommendation since it is not an internal act of prayer. Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i consider it obligatory due to the imperative form. The Hanafi response is that the command is for recommendation because carrying weapons is not inherently part of the prayer's actions. If there is no dispute among the people, it is best for each group to pray individually behind their own imam, the first group finishes and then the second, to avoid walking during prayer. This is the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): Prayer performed during battle or imminent danger
الصلاح (al-silah): Weapons

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Recommended (mustahabb)
C) Permitted (mubah)
D) Prohibited (haram)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that carrying weapons in Salat al-Khawf is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory, because it is not an action intrinsic to the prayer.

Rulings on Prompting the Dying Person with the Shahada
Explanation of sunnah rulings for a dying person: turning to qibla and talqin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah rulings for a dying person (tawjeeh and talqin), explain the Hanafi position on the wording of talqin, and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute regarding the second shahada.

Core Idea
Turning the dying to qibla and prompting the shahada are sunnah, not wajib, to ease the departing soul.

In the final moments of life, the sunnah guides us to care for the dying person in a way that brings spiritual benefit and ease. This lesson explains two key practices: positioning the dying person to face the qibla, and gently reminding him of the testimony of faith. We examine the evidence, the recommended methods, and an important difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars regarding whether to include the second part of the shahada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sunnah acts
Recognize that the passage covers two distinct sunnah practices: turning the dying person to face the qibla (tawjeeh) and prompting him with the shahada (talqin).
Both are stated as 'يسن' (it is sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: 'لقنوا موتاكم لا إله إلا الله...' from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi. This is the primary evidence for talqin.
The hadith uses the imperative 'laqqinu'.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand why the imperative indicates recommendation (nadb) not obligation in Hanafi usul. The context of difficulty and the associated reward (saving from Fire) suggest it is sunnah, not wajib.
Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a qarinah (indicator) shifting it to nadb.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-madhhab dispute: whether to prompt only 'La ilaha illallah' or include 'Muhammad Rasul Allah'. Ibn Hajar al-Haytami and some scholars argue for both.
The author sides with the majority view (only first shahada).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine the mufta bihi position: the relied-upon view is to prompt only 'La ilaha illallah' for a Muslim, based on the authentic hadith and the fact the person is already a Muslim.
For a disbeliever, both shahadas are prompted with 'ashhadu'.

Source Text

يسن) توجيه المحتضر) أي من قرب من الموت (على يمينه) لأنه السنة (وجاز الإستلقاء) على ظهره لأنه أيسر لمعالجته (و) لكن (ترفع رأسه قليلاً) ليصير وجهه إلى القبلة دون السماء (و) يسن أن ( يلقن) وذلك (بذكر) الجنة) وإن لم يقلها عند مسلم ولو فاسقاً يموت على الإيمان يدخل الجنة ولو بعد طول العذاب وإنما اقتصرنا على ذكر الشهادة تبعاً للحديث الصحيح ولذا قال في المستصفى وغيره: ويلقن الشهادتين لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله معللاً بأن الأولى لا تقبل بدون الثانية لأنه ليس إلا في حق الكافر فكلامنا في تلقين المؤمن، ولهذا قال شيخ الإسلام ابن حجر وقول جمع: يلقن محمد رسول الله أيضاً لأنّ القصد موته على الإسلام، ولا يسمى مسلماً إلا بهما مردود بأنه مسلم وإنما المراد ختم كلامه بلا إله إلا الله ليحصل له ذلك الثواب، وأما الكافر فيلقنهما قطعاً مع أشهد لوجوبه إذ لا يصير مسلماً إلا بهما انتهى فتذكر الشهادة عند المسلم المحتضر (من غير الحاح لأن الحال صعب عليه فإذا قالها مرة ولم يتكلم بعدها حصل المراد (ولا يؤمر بها فلا يقال له : قل لأنه يكون في شدة فربما يقول لا جواباً لغير الآمر فيظن خلاف الخير وقالوا: إنه إذا ظهر منه ما يوجب الكفر لا يحكم بكفره حملاً على أنه زال عقله واختار بعضهم زوال عقله عند موته لهذا الخوف ومما ينبغي أن يقال له على جهة الاستتابة أستغفر
It is sunnah) to turn the dying person) i.e., one near death (onto his right side) because it is the sunnah. (And lying on the back is permissible) because it is easier for treating him. (And) but (his head is slightly raised) so that his face faces the qiblah and not the sky. (And) it is sunnah to prompt him by (mentioning) the word (of the testimony in his presence) due to his saying: 'Prompt your dying ones with 'La ilaha illallah,' for indeed no Muslim says it at the time of death except that it saves him from the Fire.' And due to his saying: 'Whoever's last words are 'La ilaha illallah' enters Paradise.' i.e., with the winners. Otherwise, every... for the servant, and the sanctity of the right is like the sanctity of its owner. Also, the funeral prayer is not prayer in every respect, and it is also related to an accident that is the last to occur to the living in the abode of obligation, and each of them necessitates delaying it among the types of prayer; how then when they have combined? His saying: (for the dead and the bier) i.e., both are for them. It is said: with kasr, the dead person himself; with fath, the bier; and it is said the opposite; and it is said: kasr is for the bier with the dead. And everything that weighs heavily on a people and causes them grief is a janazah, derived from 'janaza' the thing, 'yajnuzuhu' from the category of 'daraba' when he conceals it. Its plural is as in al-Qamus and al-Misbah etc. It is named thus because it is gathered and prepared, like 'miskin'. And death is an existential attribute created opposite to life, and it is said absence of life from one who is characterized by life, as in al-Talwih. His saying: (It is sunnah to turn the dying person) i.e., towards the qiblah. 'al-Muhtadaru' is a passive participle, i.e., one whom the angels of death have attended in reality, or one whom death has attended and overcome, its signs being the slackening of his feet, the curvature of his nostril, and the sinking of his temples. It is incumbent on every accountable person to frequently remember death and prepare for it by repentance and returning injustices, especially the sick. Asking for his supplication is loved, mentioned by Ibn Amir Haj. The stoned one is not turned. His saying: (on his right side) which is the sunnah in sleep and the grave. It is restricted to when it does not cause difficulty; if it is difficult, he is left as he is, per al-Nahr. Consideration of one killed by the sword in retribution: is he turned or not? Al-Hamawi says apparently yes, because the best of sessions is that facing the qiblah, so death upon it is more appropriate. His saying: (and lying on the back is permissible) and the washed and the one prayed over are placed thus; it is said in Sharh al-Tahawi that this is the custom among people. Al-Zad says the first is better because it is the sunnah, as in al-Mudmarat. His saying: (because it is easier for his treatment) i.e., for closing his eyes, tying his jaw, and easier than the curvature of his limbs. So it is an addition of the infinitive to its object, or for hastening the soul's departure of the dead, so it is an addition to its subject. In al-Tanwir it is said: it is placed as is convenient, on the correct view. His saying: (and it is sunnah to prompt) al-Nahr says: This prompting is recommended by consensus, and its time is at the throes of death before gargling. What is in al-Qunyah: it is obligatory on his brothers and friends to prompt him; it is permissible. The end. 'Talqin' means teaching and reminding, i.e., by mentioning. It is recommended that the prompter not be suspected of being pleased with his death, and that he be someone in whom goodness is believed, so he mentions it to him aloud so that he may utter it to be his last words. His saying: ('Prompt your dead') the majority hold that the meaning is metaphorical, i.e., those near death, not the dead literally, like his saying: 'Whoever kills a slain person, his spoils are his.' This is indicated by his later saying: 'For no Muslim says it except that it saves him from the Fire.' His saying: 'except that it saves him from the Fire' i.e., he never enters it at all; otherwise, every believer must be saved from it, even after entering it. His saying: ('enters Paradise') even if he did not say it at the time. A Muslim, even if a sinner, dies with faith and enters Paradise even after prolonged punishment. We limited ourselves to mentioning the testimony following the authentic hadith. Hence it is said in al-Mustasfa and others: the two testimonies are prompted: 'La ilaha illallah, Muhammad Rasul Allah,' reasoning that the first is not accepted without the second, because it is only for the disbeliever. So our discussion is about prompting the believer. For this reason, Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Hajar and a group said: he should also be prompted with 'Muhammad Rasul Allah' because the aim is his death upon Islam, and he is not called a Muslim except with both. This is refuted because he is a Muslim, and the aim is only to seal his speech with 'La ilaha illallah' to obtain that reward. As for the disbeliever, he is prompted with both definitely, with 'ashhadu' due to its obligation, since he does not become Muslim except with both. End. So the testimony is mentioned in the presence of the Muslim dying person (without insistence because his state is difficult; if he says it once and does not speak after it, the aim is achieved. (He is not commanded with it, so it is not said to him: 'Say,' because he is in distress, and perhaps he will say 'no' in response to someone other than the orderer, so good is thought contrary. And they said: if something that necessitates disbelief appears from him, he is not judged as disbeliever, assuming that his mind has left. Some chose that his mind leaves at death for this fear. Among the things that should be said to him by way of admonition: 'I seek forgiveness.'
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the rulings for a dying person (muhtadar). The ruling: it is sunnah to turn the dying person onto his right side so he faces the qibla, as this is the sunnah in sleep and burial. If difficult, he may lie on his back with his head slightly raised so his face faces the qibla. This is the author's explanation. The second sunnah is talqin: prompting the dying person to say 'La ilaha illallah' (the first shahada) without insistence. The proof is from two hadiths: 'Prompt your dying ones with La ilaha illallah...' and 'Whoever's last words are La ilaha illallah enters Paradise.' The author clarifies the meaning of 'your dead' as those near death, not already dead. The talqin should be done before the dying person reaches the point of gargling (ghurghura), and it is recommended (mustahab) by consensus. The prompter should be a righteous person who is not suspected of being pleased with the death. Regarding the wording, the author notes a dispute: some scholars say to include the second shahada ('Muhammad Rasul Allah') as well, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is to only prompt with 'La ilaha illallah' because the hadith mentions only that, and the dying person is already a Muslim. For a disbeliever, both shahadas are prompted. The passage also warns against commanding the dying person to say it, as they may reply negatively out of distress. If the dying person says something that appears to be disbelief, he is not judged as a disbeliever due to the possibility that his mental faculties had left him. Some scholars opine that the mind leaves at death for this reason.

Key Terms
توجيه المحتضر (tawjeeh al-muhtadar): Turning the dying person so that he faces the qibla, done by positioning him on his right side or back with head raised.
تلقیین (talqin): Promoting the dying person to say the shahada by mentioning it aloud in his presence so he may repeat it.
محضر (muhtadar): A person who is dying, i.e., one at the point of death with signs like slack feet and sunken temples.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on turning a dying person to face the qibla?
A) Wajib, it must be done even if difficult.
B) Sunnah, recommended unless it causes great difficulty.
C) Mubah, it is optional with no preference.
D) Haram, because it disturbs the dying person.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah at the time of death is to gently prompt the dying person with 'La ilaha illallah' and turn him toward the qibla, without insistence or command.

Talqeen: Prompting the Shahada at Death and After Burial
Rulings on prompting the shahada at death and after burial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talqeen for a dying Muslim and a deceased after burial, and apply the proper etiquette of prompting without insistence.

Core Idea
Prompt the dying gently; after burial, talqeen is a legislated sunnah.

Talqeen—prompting the shahada—is a sunnah at the time of death and after burial. However, the method matters: for a Muslim, it must be done without insistence to avoid distress, whereas for a disbeliever, commanding is necessary. This lesson explains the rulings, proofs, and etiquette based on the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its two contexts
Determine that talqeen applies to a dying Muslim (at deathbed) and after burial (at the grave). The ruling differs for a disbeliever.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each context
For a Muslim at death: sunnah to mention the shahada without insisting. For a Muslim after burial: sunnah muakkadah (mashru') to prompt. For a disbeliever: obligatory (wajib) to command with both shahadas.
The text emphasises 'min ghayri ilhah' (without insistence).
3
Understand the etiquette of prompting
Do not say 'say' (قل) directly; rather recite the shahada so the dying person hears and repeats naturally. Avoid causing distress or misunderstanding.
If the person says 'no' in response to another, it might be misinterpreted.
4
Identify the proof (dalil)
The hadith 'لقنوا موتاكم شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله' (Prompt your dead with the testimony...) is the primary evidence. It covers both dying and deceased according to Hanafi interpretation.
The imperative indicates recommendation (amr) for talqeen.
5
Note the ikhtilaf (dispute)
The Mu'tazila reject talqeen after burial; a third group says it is neither commanded nor forbidden. The Hanafi view relies on the hadith and practice of Ahl al-Sunnah.
The passage attributes the rejection to Mu'tazila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
مسلم ولو فاسقاً يموت على الإيمان يدخل الجنة ولو بعد طول العذاب وإنما اقتصرنا على ذكر الشهادة تبعاً للحديث الصحيح ولذا قال في المستصفى وغيره: ويلقن الشهادتين لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله معللاً بأن الأولى لا تقبل بدون الثانية لأنه ليس إلا في حق الكافر فكلامنا في تلقين المؤمن، ولهذا قال شيخ الإسلام ابن حجر وقول جمع: يلقن محمد رسول الله أيضاً لأنّ القصد موته على الإسلام، ولا يسمى مسلماً إلا بهما مردود بأنه مسلم وإنما المراد ختم كلامه بلا إله إلا الله ليحصل له ذلك الثواب، وأما الكافر فيلقنهما قطعاً مع أشهد لوجوبه إذ لا يصير مسلماً إلا بهما انتهى فتذكر الشهادة عند المسلم المحتضر (من غير الحاح لأن الحال صعب عليه فإذا قالها مرة ولم يتكلم بعدها حصل المراد (ولا يؤمر بها فلا يقال له : قل لأنه يكون في شدة فربما يقول لا جواباً لغير الآمر فيظن خلاف الخير وقالوا: إنه إذا ظهر منه ما يوجب الكفر لا يحكم بكفره حملاً على أنه زال عقله واختار بعضهم زوال عقله عند موته لهذا الخوف ومما ينبغي أن يقال له على جهة الاستتابة أستغفر الله العظيم الذي لا إله إلا هو الحي القيوم وأتوب إليه سبحانه لا إله إلا هو الحي القيوم لأنه قد يستضر بذكر ما يشعر أنه محتضر وأما الكافر فيؤمر بهما لما روى البخاري عن أنس الله رضي عنه قال : كان غلام يهودي يخدم النبي الله فمرض فأتاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يعوده فقعد عند رأسه فقال : أسلم فنظر إلى أبيه فقال له : أطع أبا القاسم، فأسلم فخرج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو يقول : الحمد لله أنقذه من النار (وتلقينه) بعد ما وضع (في القبر مشروع الحقيقة قوله : لقنوا موتاكم شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله أخرجه الجماعة إلا البخاري ونسب إلى أهل السنة والجماعة (وقيل لا يلقن في القبر ونسب إلى المعتزلة (وقيل لا يؤمر به ولا ينهى وكيفيته أن يقال : يا فلان بن فلان اذكر دينك الذي كنت عليه في دار الدنيا بشهادة أن لا إله إلا الله
The Book of Prayer. A Muslim, even if a fasiq, dies upon faith enters Paradise, even if after prolonged punishment. We only restrict to mentioning the shahada following the authentic hadith. Therefore, al-Mustasfa and others said: He is prompted with the two testimonies: 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah', reasoning that the first is not accepted without the second because it is only for the disbeliever. So our discussion is about prompting the believer. Hence, Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Hajar and a group said: He is prompted with 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' as well because the intention is that he dies upon Islam, and one is not called a Muslim except by both. This is rejected because he is Muslim; rather, the objective is to end his speech with 'There is no god but Allah' to obtain that reward. As for the disbeliever, he is prompted with both definitely along with 'I bear witness' due to its obligation, for he only becomes Muslim by both. End. So the shahada is mentioned to the Muslim at the point of death (without insistence because the situation is difficult for him. If he says it once and does not speak after it, the objective is achieved. He is not commanded to say it, so one does not say 'say' to him because he is in distress; perhaps he will say 'no' in response to someone other than the one commanding, and it will be thought to be evil contrary to good. They said: If something that necessitates kufr appears from him, he is not judged as a disbeliever, attributing it to loss of his mind. Some chose that his mind leaves at death due to this fear. Among what should be said to him as a call to repentance is: 'I seek forgiveness from Allah, the Mighty, besides whom there is no god, the Living, the Self-Subsisting, and I repent to Him, glory be to Him; there is no god but He, the Living, the Self-Subsisting' because he may be harmed by mentioning what suggests he is dying. As for the disbeliever, he is commanded to say both due to what Bukhari narrated from Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: There was a Jewish boy who served the Prophet (peace be upon him). He fell ill, so the Prophet visited him, sat at his head, and said: 'Accept Islam.' He looked at his father, who said: 'Obey Abu al-Qasim,' so he accepted Islam. The Prophet left saying: 'Praise be to Allah who saved him from the Fire.' (And his prompting) after being placed (in the grave is legislated) due to his saying: 'Prompt your dead with the testimony that there is no god but Allah.' This was narrated by all except al-Bukhari and attributed to Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. (And it is said: He is not prompted in the grave, attributed to the Mu'tazila. And it is said: He is not commanded nor forbidden. Its manner is to say: O so-and-so son of so-and-so, remember your religion which you had in the world by bearing witness that there is no god but Allah.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi discusses the ruling of talqeen (prompting the shahada) for a Muslim at the time of death and after burial. The author begins by affirming that any Muslim, even a fasiq, who dies with iman enters Paradise, though possibly after punishment. The focus is on prompting the believer with the shahada, following the authentic hadith. The author clarifies that for a believer, it is sufficient to prompt with 'La ilaha illallah' without insisting, because the situation is difficult. The shahada should be mentioned gently, not by commanding 'say', to avoid potential misunderstanding if the dying person utters 'no' in response to someone else. If the dying Muslim says something that appears kufr, it is not taken as actual kufr because it is attributed to loss of reason at death. The author then contrasts with a disbeliever, who must be prompted with both shahadas, citing the hadith of the Jewish boy who accepted Islam at the Prophet's visitation. After burial, talqeen at the grave is legislated (mashru') based on the hadith 'Prompt your dead with the testimony that there is no god but Allah.' This is the position of Ahl al-Sunnah, while some (Mu'tazila) reject it. The manner is to address the deceased by name and remind him of his testimony.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqeen): Prompting a dying person or a deceased in the grave to recite the shahada.
شهادة (shahada): The testimony of faith: 'La ilaha illallah, Muhammadur Rasulullah.'
إلحاح (ilhaah): Insistence or repeatedly urging the dying person to say the shahada, which is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How should the shahada be presented to a Muslim at the time of death?
A) By commanding him to say 'La ilaha illallah'
B) By mentioning the shahada gently without insistence
C) By prompting both shahadas and insisting until he says it
D) By not prompting at all for a Muslim

Key Takeaway
Talqeen for a dying Muslim must be gentle and without insisting; after burial, it is a sunnah based on the hadith, and the method is to address the deceased by name and remind him of the shahada.

beginner

Talqin for the Dying: Prompting the Shahada with Care
Explains the ruling on talqin for the dying with proof from the hadith of the Jewish boy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talqin for a dying Muslim and non-Muslim and cite the prophetic hadith as proof.

Core Idea
Talqin for the dying is recommended, but avoid explicitly mentioning death to a Muslim, while a disbeliever should be invited to Islam.

In this passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi, the author distinguishes between the rulings for a dying Muslim and a dying non-Muslim. The discussion is grounded in the prophetic practice, particularly the hadith of the Jewish boy who converted on his deathbed. Understanding this distinction ensures that talqin is performed appropriately, respecting the sensitivity of the situation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage presents two scenarios: a Muslim nearing death and a disbeliever nearing death. Identify each case and note that the rulings differ.
2
State the ruling for the Muslim
For a Muslim, one should not say anything that explicitly indicates death, as it may cause harm (istidrar). The implication is that talqin should be done indirectly, e.g., by reciting the shahada in the presence of the dying person.
This is based on the principle of avoiding harm.
3
State the ruling for the non-Muslim
For a disbeliever, the Prophet's command to the Jewish boy shows that he is ordered to recite the shahada. The imperative indicates recommendation (nadb) rather than obligation, but it is strongly encouraged.
The hadith is proof of the legitimacy of inviting a dying non-Muslim to Islam.
4
Analyze the proof
The hadith of the Jewish boy (narrated by Bukhari) is the primary dalil. The Prophet visited the boy, sat at his head, and said 'Accept Islam.' The boy looked at his father, who told him to obey, and he accepted. The Prophet praised God.
This hadith establishes the practice for non-Muslims.
5
Apply to contemporary practice
When visiting a dying person, a Muslim should be mindful of their state. For a believer, gentle reminders of faith are sunnah; for a non-believer, an invitation to Islam may be offered wisely.
The key is to avoid causing distress while fulfilling the duty of da'wah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة الله العظيم الذي لا إله إلا هو الحي القيوم وأتوب إليه سبحانه لا إله إلا هو الحي القيوم لأنه قد يستضر بذكر ما يشعر أنه محتضر وأما الكافر فيؤمر بهما لما روى البخاري عن أنس الله رضي عنه قال : كان غلام يهودي يخدم النبي الله فمرض فأتاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يعوده فقعد عند رأسه فقال : أسلم فنظر إلى أبيه فقال له : أطع أبا القاسم، فأسلم فخرج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو يقول : الحمد لله أنقذه من النار (وتلقينه) بعد ما وضع (في القبر مشروع الحقيقة قوله : لقنوا موتاكم شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله أخرجه الجماعة إلا البخاري ونسب إلى أهل السنة والجماعة (وقيل لا يلقن في القبر ونسب إلى المعتزلة (وقيل لا يؤمر به ولا ينهى وكيفيته أن يقال : يا فلان بن فلان اذكر دينك الذي كنت عليه في دار الدنيا بشهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمداً رسول الله ولا شك أن اللفظ لا يجوز إخراجه عن حقيقته إلا بدليل فائدته مطلقاً فيجب تعيينه بقوله : موتاكم حقيقة ونفي صاحب الكافي ممنوع نعم الفائدة الأصلية منتفية ويحتاج إليه لتثبيت الجنان للسؤال في القبر قال المحقق ابن الهمام، وحمل أكثر مشايخنا إياه على المجاز أي من قرب من الموت مبناه على أن الميت لا يسمع وأورد عليهم قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في أهل القليب: (ما أنتم بأسمع منهم) وأجابوا تارة بأنه مردود من عائشة وتارة بأنه خصوصية له وتارة بأنه من ضرب المثل ويشكل
Book of Prayer. The Great God, there is no god but Him, the Living, the Self-Subsisting, and I repent to Him. Glory be to Him, there is no god but Him, the Living, the Self-Subsisting, because he might be harmed by mentioning what indicates he is dying. As for the disbeliever, he is ordered to say both [shahadas] due to what Bukhari narrated from Anas, may God be pleased with him, who said: There was a Jewish boy who served the Prophet, and he fell ill. The Prophet visited him and sat at his head and said: 'Accept Islam.' He looked at his father, who said: 'Obey Abu al-Qasim,' so he accepted Islam. The Prophet left saying: 'Praise be to God who saved him from the Fire.' And his talqin after being placed in the grave is legitimate in reality. His statement: 'Prompt your dying [to say]: There is no god but Allah' – narrated by all except Bukhari, and attributed to Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. And it is said that talqin in the grave is not done, attributed to the Mu'tazila. And it is said: it is neither commanded nor prohibited. Its manner is to say: 'O so-and-so son of so-and-so, remember your religion which you had in the worldly life by testifying that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.' And there is no doubt that the word [mawtakum] cannot be taken out of its literal meaning without evidence, and its benefit is absolutely lacking, so it must be specified by saying 'your dead' literally. The denial of the author of al-Kafi is rejected. Yes, the original benefit is absent, but it is needed for strengthening the heart for the questioning in the grave. The investigator Ibn al-Humam said: Most of our scholars interpreted it metaphorically, i.e., those close to death, based on the fact that the dead do not hear. And it was objected against them by his statement, peace be upon him, regarding the people of the well: 'You are not more hearing than they.' And they replied sometimes that it is rejected by Aisha, and sometimes that it is a specific characteristic for him, and sometimes that it is a metaphorical expression. And it is problematic.
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi deals with the rulings on talqin – prompting the dying or the deceased to recite the shahada. The author begins by noting that for a dying Muslim, it is not appropriate to explicitly mention the imminence of death, as that may cause distress. However, for a dying non-Muslim, prompting to Islam is commanded, as demonstrated by the hadith of the Jewish boy who served the Prophet and converted on his deathbed. Next, the issue of talqin after burial is discussed. The author states that it is legitimate (mashru') in the Hanafi school, citing the hadith 'Lauqinu mawtaku...' (Prompt your dying [to say]...). This hadith is understood by most Hanafi scholars metaphorically – 'your dead' refers to those near death, because the dead do not hear. The Mu'tazila and some others reject talqin after burial. The author defends the practice, noting that even though the original benefit of converting the person is absent after death, it still has the benefit of strengthening the deceased during the questioning in the grave. The objection from the hadith of the people of the well (where the Prophet addressed the dead polytheists) is addressed by various explanations: it is rejected by Aisha, it was a special privilege of the Prophet, or it was a simile. Thus, the Hanafi position is that talqin after burial is recommended, though there is scholarly disagreement.

Key Terms
التلقين (al-talqin): Prompting a dying person or a deceased in the grave to recite the shahada or remember Islam.
موتاكم (mawtakum): Literally 'your dead'; interpreted by most Hanafi scholars as those near death, not the already deceased.
المحتضر (al-muhtadar): The person who is in the throes of death; the dying individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of the Jewish boy, what did the Prophet do?
A) He ordered the boy to convert.
B) He visited and invited him to Islam.
C) He remained silent.
D) He prohibited talqin.

Key Takeaway
Talqin for the dying is sunnah, but caution is required for Muslims to avoid distress; for non-Muslims, it is sunnah to invite them to Islam gently.

Talqin After Burial: Recommending the Shahada Over the Grave
Explains the ruling on talqin after burial with proofs and scholarly objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on talqin after burial, the proofs cited, and the objections raised by other groups.

Core Idea
Talqin after burial is recommended in the Hanafi school despite the debate over whether the dead can hear.

The second part of the passage addresses the practice of talqin after the deceased has been placed in the grave. This is a controversial issue: some schools accept it, others reject it. The author defends the Hanafi position that it is legitimate (mashru'), citing the hadith 'Laqinu mawtakum...' and addressing the objection that the dead do not hear by interpreting the hadith metaphorically. This lesson explores the evidences and the scholarly debate.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The author begins by affirming that talqin after burial is legitimate (mashru').
2
Identify the primary proof
The hadith 'Lauqinu mawtaku shahada an la ilaha illallah' is cited. It is attributed to Ahl al-Sunnah.
The hadith is narrated by all except Bukhari.
3
Understand the opposition
The Mu'tazila reject talqin after burial; another group says it is neither commanded nor prohibited.
These are minority positions.
4
Interpret the key term 'mawtakum'
The literal meaning is 'your dead'. However, most Hanafi scholars interpret it figuratively as 'those near death' (muhtadar), because the dead cannot hear.
This avoids contradiction with the principle that the dead do not hear.
5
Address the counter-argument
The objection from the hadith of the well (people of Badr) is answered in three ways: rejected by Aisha, a special case for the Prophet, or a simile.
These responses preserve the Hanafi position.

The Ruling of Talqin: Prompting the Dying and the Deceased
Critical refinement on the recommendation of talqin and the hearing of the dead.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talqin for the dying and the deceased, explain the evidence from the practice of the Companions, and reconcile the apparent contradiction between the Quranic verse on the dead not hearing and the hadith that the dead hear footsteps.

Core Idea
Talqin is recommended (mustahabb) for both the dying and the deceased after burial.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah addresses a critical refinement: how can talqin (prompting the shahada) after burial be beneficial if the dead do not hear? The author navigates between the Quranic verse denying hearing and the hadiths suggesting a form of perception, arriving at a reconciliation that upholds the recommended practice. Through this lesson, you will understand the Hanafi position, its proofs, and the interpretive method that harmonizes apparently conflicting evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what talqin is and the hukm level: sunnah ghayr muakkadah (recommended) for both the dying and after burial.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Find the key hadith: the practice of the Companions as narrated by Sa'id ibn Mansur and others, where they would say at the grave 'Say: La ilaha illa Allah' three times.
3
Recognize the objection
Identify the apparent contradiction: the Quranic verses (27:80, 35:22) indicate the dead do not hear, which seems to undermine the benefit of post-burial talqin.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine how the Hanafis reconcile the proofs: the majority interpret 'موتاكم' (your dead) metaphorically as those near death for talqin at the deathbed, while affirming post-burial talqin for its spiritual benefit in strengthening the deceased for the questioning.
5
Derive the mufta bihi
Conclude the operative ruling: talqin is mustahabb in both circumstances, and the benefit is not contingent on literal hearing but on spiritual strengthening and the reality of the questioning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله بشهادة أن لا إله إلا الله الباء للتصوير. قوله: (ولا شك أن اللفظ) أي وهو موتاكم قال البرهان الحلبي ولا مانع من الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز في مثل هذا اهـ. قوله: (فيجب تعيينه أي تعيين اللفظ باعتبار المعنى، أو تعيين هذا القيل، وهو مشروعية التلقين في القبر، وقوله: حقيقة منصوب على التمييز. قوله: (فائدته) بالنصب مفعول نفي، وذلك لأن العبرة بحال النزع فإن كان مسلماً فهو مثبت وإن كان كافراً لا ينفعه هذا التلقين، وقوله: مطلقاً حال فائدته أنه لا فائدة فيه أصلاً قوله: (ممنوع) بأن فيه فائدة التثبيت للجنان قوله: (نعم الفائدة الأصلية) وهي تحصيل الإيمان في هذا الوقت. قوله: (وحمل أكثر مشايخنا) مقول القول، وهو مبتدأ خبره قوله مبناه قوله: (مبناه على أن الميت لا يسمع عندهم على ما صرحوا به في كتاب الإيمان لو حلف لا يكلمه فكلمه ميتاً لا يحنث لأنها تنعقد على من يفهم والميت ليس كذلك لعدم السماع. قال تعالى: {وما أنت بمسمع من في القبور إنك لا تسمع الموتى} [النمل/27] وهذا التشبيه لحال الكفار في عدم إذعانهم للحق بحال الموتى، وهو يفيد تحقيق عدم سماع الموتى إذ هو فرعه قوله: (في أهل القليب) قليب بدر، وهو حفرة رميت فيها جيف كفار قريش فخاطبهم النبي بقوله: «إنا وجدنا ما وعدنا ربنا حقاً فهل وجدتم ما وعد ربكم حقاً» فقال عمر ما معناه: إنك تخاطب أجساماً أجيفت فأجابه بما ذكر قوله بأنه مردود من عائشة فإنها قالت: كيف يقول ذلك رداً عليهم ما في مسلم أن الميت يسمع قرع نعالهم إذا انصرفوا وتمامه بفتح القدير قلت: يمكن الجمع فيلقن عند الاحتضار لصريح قوله: فإنه ليس مسلم يقولها عند الموت إلا أنجته من النار، وعملاً بحقيقة موتاكم لتثبيته للسؤال في القبر لما روى سعيد بن منصور وسمرة بن وحكم بن عمير قالوا: إذا سوي على الميت قبره وانصرف الناس كانوا يستحبون أن يقال للميت عند قبره يا فلان قل لا إله إلا الله ثلاث مرات يا فلان قل ربي الله الإسلام ونبيي محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم اللهم إني أتوسل إليك بحبيبك المصطفى أن ترحم فاقتي بالموت على الإسلام والإيمان وأن تشفع فينا نبيك عليه أفضل الصلاة والسلام (ويستحب لأقرباء المحتضر) وأصدقائه وجيرانه الدخول عليه للقيام بحقه وتذكيره وتجريعه وسقيه الماء والأصح أن الأنبياء عليهم السلام لا يسألون وكذا أطفال المؤمنين واختلف في المشركين ودخولهم الجنة وفي الجوهرة والطفل يلقنه الملك فيقول: من ربك ثم يقول للطفل: قل: الله ربي وقيل: يلهمه الله تعالى كإلهام عيسى عليه السلام في المهد اهـ وفي شرح العلامة العيني على البخاري قال النووي: الصحيح المختار الذي ذهب إليه المحققون أن أطفال المشركين في الجنة لقوله تعالى: {وما كنا معذبين حتى نبعث رسولا} وإذا كان لا يعذب العاقل لكونه لم تبلغه الدعوة فغير العاقل أولى اهـ والأشهر أن السؤال حين يدفن وقيل في بيته تنطبق عليه الأرض كالقبر وفي البزازية السؤال فيما يستقر فيه الميت حتى لو أكله سبع فالسؤال في بطنه فإن جعل في تابوت أياما لنقله إلى مكان آخر لا يسأل ما لم يدفن كذا في حاشية الدرر للمؤلف.
His saying: 'by the testimony that there is no god but Allah' – the ba is for framing. His saying: 'and there is no doubt that the wording' – i.e., this is 'your dead'. Al-Burhan al-Halabi said: there is no impediment to combining the literal and metaphorical in such cases. His saying: 'so it is necessary to specify it' – i.e., to specify the wording in consideration of the meaning, or to specify this statement, which is the legislation of talqin at the grave. And his saying: 'literally' is in the accusative as a specification. His saying: 'its benefit' in the accusative is the object of negation – because the consideration is the state of dying: if he is a Muslim, it is confirming; if he is an unbeliever, this talqin does not benefit him. And his saying: 'absolutely' is a state of its benefit: that there is no benefit at all. His saying: 'is prevented' – because in it is the benefit of strengthening the heart. His saying: 'yes, the original benefit' – which is the acquisition of faith at that time. His saying: 'and the majority of our mashayikh interpreted it' – i.e., as metaphorical, i.e., those close to death. Its basis is that the dead do not hear, according to what they clarified in the book of Iman: if one swears not to speak to him and then speaks to a dead person, he does not break his oath because oaths are contracted with those who understand, and the dead are not like that due to lack of hearing. Allah Most High says: 'And you are not one to make hear those in the graves. Indeed, you do not make the dead hear' [Quran 27:? – actually 27:80, 35:22]. This analogy is for the state of the disbelievers in their non-compliance with the truth to the state of the dead, and it proves the non-hearing of the dead as it is its branch. His saying: 'concerning the people of al-Qalib' – Qalib Badr, which is a pit in which the carcasses of the Quraysh disbelievers were thrown. The Prophet addressed them: 'We have found what our Lord promised us true; have you found what your Lord promised you true?' So 'Umar said meaning: you address dead bodies? He answered him with what was mentioned. His saying: 'that it is rejected' from 'A'isha, for she said: 'how can he say that?' as a refutation against them – what is in Muslim that the dead hear the sound of their sandals when they leave. And its completion in Fath al-Qadir. I say: reconciliation is possible: he is prompted at the time of dying due to the explicit statement: 'there is no Muslim who says it at the time of death except that it saves him from the Fire', and acting upon the literal meaning of 'your dead' to strengthen him for the questioning in the grave because of what Sa'id ibn Mansur, Samura ibn and Hakam ibn 'Umayr narrated: when the grave of the deceased was leveled and the people left, they used to recommend saying to the deceased at his grave: 'O so-and-so, say: there is no god but Allah' three times, 'O so-and-so, say: my Lord is Allah, Islam is my religion, and Muhammad is my Prophet.' 'O Allah, I seek intercession through Your beloved chosen one that You have mercy on my neediness at death upon Islam and faith, and that You grant intercession to your Prophet for us.' And it is recommended for the relatives of the dying, his friends and neighbors to enter upon him to fulfill his right, remind him, give him drink, and provide water. And the correct view is that the prophets, peace be upon them, are not questioned, as well as the children of believers. There is disagreement concerning the polytheists and their entering Paradise. In al-Jawhara: the child is prompted by the angel, who says: 'Who is your Lord?' then says to the child: 'Say: Allah is my Lord.' It is also said that Allah inspires him, like the inspiration of Jesus, peace be upon him, in the cradle. In the commentary of al-'Ayni on al-Bukhari, al-Nawawi said: the correct chosen view of the verifiers is that the children of polytheists are in Paradise, due to His statement: 'And We were not to punish until We send a messenger' [Quran 17:15]. If the sane person is not punished because the call did not reach him, then the non-sane is more worthy. The most well-known is that the questioning occurs when he is buried; it is said: it occurs in his house, the earth closes over him like a grave. In al-Bazzaziyya: the questioning is where the deceased is interred, so if a beast eats him, the questioning is in its stomach. If he is placed in a coffin for days for transport to another place, he is not questioned until he is buried. This is in the hashya of al-Durar by the author.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This is a critical refinement (hashiya) by al-Tahtawi on the commentary of Maraqi al-Falah concerning the ruling of talqin (prompting the dying and the deceased to testify faith). The passage begins by analyzing the phrase 'by the testimony that there is no god but Allah' in the original matn, noting that the ba is for framing (taswir). The core issue is the interpretation of the word 'موتاكم' (your dead) in the hadith: does it literally refer to the deceased or metaphorically to the dying? The majority of Hanafi scholars interpret it metaphorically because they hold that the dead do not hear, as supported by the Quranic verse 'You do not make the dead hear' and the principle that an oath to speak to someone is only broken if the addressee can understand. However, there is a counter-narrative: the Prophet addressed the dead bodies at Badr, and the hadith in Muslim states that the dead hear the footsteps of those leaving. The objections to using the Badr incident as proof include that it was a miracle specific to the Prophet, or that it was a simile. Al-Tahtawi notes that these responses are rebutted by 'A'isha's rejection and the Muslim hadith. He suggests a reconciliation: talqin is performed at the moment of death due to the explicit promise of salvation for the one who says the shahada at death, and also after burial based on the literal meaning of 'your dead' to strengthen the deceased for the questioning. He cites reports from early authorities that it was recommended to say 'Say: La ilaha illa Allah' at the grave after burial. The passage then discusses the questioning of prophets and children, noting that prophets and children of believers are not questioned, while for children of disbelievers, the correct view is that they are in Paradise as they have not been reached by the call. Finally, the time and place of questioning are addressed: it occurs at the time of burial where the body is interred.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqin): Prompting the dying or the deceased to recite the shahada and affirm faith.
موتاكم (mawtākum): Literally 'your dead'; in the hadith, interpreted by most Hanafi scholars as those close to death (metaphorically) due to the belief that the dead do not hear.
السؤال في القبر (al-su'āl fī al-qabr): The questioning by the angels Munkar and Nakir after burial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the benefit of talqin after burial?
A) To make the deceased hear and respond.
B) To strengthen the deceased for the questioning in the grave.
C) To fulfill a wajib obligation.
D) To inform the deceased of worldly matters.

Key Takeaway
Talqin after burial is recommended (mustahabb) because it spiritually strengthens the deceased for the questioning, even though the dead do not hear in the usual sense.
