Spiritual Care at the Time of Death: Hope and Recitation
Commentary on practices for the dying person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on having good opinion of Allah and reciting Surah Yasin for the dying, and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
At death, hope in Allah's mercy is sunnah; Satan tempts with despair—recite Yasin to ease the soul's departure.

The moment of death is a critical spiritual juncture where the dying person is vulnerable to both divine mercy and satanic whispers. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi outlines two key practices: cultivating a good opinion of Allah (ḥusn al-ẓann) and reciting Surah Yasin. The commentary links these to authentic hadiths and explains the wisdom behind them, distinguishing between the states of health and illness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
Determine what actions are prescribed for the dying person: having good opinion of Allah and reciting Surah Yasin. Identify their legal status (sunnah, mustahabb, etc.).
The commentary states these are recommended based on commands in hadith.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the specific hadith proofs cited: (1) Muslim's hadith 'Let none of you die except while he thinks well of Allah', (2) the qudsi hadith 'I am with My servant's opinion of Me', and (3) the command to recite Yasin.
The hadiths are ahad, but considered reliable by Hanafis.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (point of evidence)
Analyze how each proof indicates the ruling. For good opinion: the imperative form 'لا يموتن' implies a command, and the qudsi hadith shows Allah's response depends on the servant's expectation. For Yasin: the command 'اقرؤوا على موتاكم يس' is a direct instruction.
The imperative in Hanafi usul indicates recommendation (nadb) unless there is a qarina for obligation; here context favors recommendation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
Observe that some later scholars approved reciting Surah al-Ra'd in addition to Yasin, based on a saying of Jabir that it eases the soul's departure. This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi difference.
The majority Hanafi position is to recite Yasin; al-Ra'd is an additional sunnah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is to recite Surah Yasin as sunnah muakkadah, and to encourage good opinion of Allah. The additional recitation of al-Ra'd is a recommended refinement from later authorities.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah for Yasin; al-Ra'd is from fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العطش يغلب لشدة النزع حينئذ، ولذلك يأتي الشيطان كما ورد بماء زلال ويقول: قل لا إله غيري حتى أسقيك نعوذ بالله منه ويذكرون فضل الله وسعة كرمه ويحسنون ظنه بالله تعالى لخبر مسلم : لا يموتن أحدكم إلا وهو يحسن الظن بالله أنه . يرحمه ويعفو عنه. وخبر الصحيحين قال الله تعالى : أنا عند ظن عبدي بي (ويتلون عنده سورة يس) للأمر به، وفي خبر ما من مريض يقرأ عنده بس إلا مات ريان وأدخل قبره ريان (واستحسن) بعض المتأخرين قراءة سورة الرعد) لقول جابر رضي الله عنه : فإنها تهون عليه خروج روحه قوله : (وسقيه الماء) عطف تفسير قوله : ( حينئذ ) أي حين النزع والأولى حذفه . قوله : (ولذلك) أي لغلبة العطش في هذا الحال قوله : (بماء) (زلال أي بارد. قوله: (لا يموتن أحدكم الخ) أخذ منه أنه يقدم حالة الرجاء في المرض، وأما في حالة الصحة فيقدم الخوف . قوله : (أنا عند ظن عبدي بي أي إن جزائي لعبدي يكون على حسب من خير وشر . قوله: (للأمر به) وهو اقرؤوا على موتاكم يس والحكمة في قراءتها أن أحوال القيامة، والبعث مذكورة فيها فتجدد له بذكرها والإيمان بها مزيداً اهـ من الشرح قوله : (فإنها تهون) بدل من قول جابر
Thirst overcomes due to the severity of the death throes at that moment. Therefore, Satan comes as has been reported with cool water and says: 'Say there is no god but me so that I may give you to drink.' We seek refuge in Allah from him. They mention Allah's bounty and the vastness of His generosity, and they think well of Allah Almighty due to the hadith of Muslim: 'Let none of you die except while he thinks well of Allah, that He will have mercy on him and forgive him.' And the hadith of the Two Sahihs: Allah Almighty said: 'I am with My servant's opinion of Me.' (And they recite Surah Yasin at his side) due to the command to do so, and in a hadith: 'No sick person has Surah Yasin recited at his side but he dies in a state of satisfaction (riyan) and enters his grave satisfied.' (And some later scholars approved) reciting Surah al-Ra'd due to the saying of Jabir, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Indeed it eases the departure of his soul.' His saying: (And give him water) is a conjunctive interpretation of his saying: (at that moment) meaning at the time of the death throes, and it is better to omit it. His saying: (Therefore) meaning due to the overpowering of thirst in this state. His saying: (with water) (cool) meaning cold. His saying: (Let none of you die...) derived from it is that he puts forward hope in illness, but in health he puts forward fear. His saying: (I am with My servant's opinion of Me) meaning My reward for My servant is according to what he expects of good or evil. His saying: (due to the command) which is 'Recite upon your dead Yasin', and the wisdom in its recitation is that the conditions of the Day of Resurrection and the resurrection are mentioned in it, so it renews for him through its mention and belief an increase. End from the commentary. His saying: (Indeed it eases) is a substitute for the saying of Jabir.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This is a hashya commentary on Maraqi al-Falah explaining the rulings of spiritual care for the dying person. It addresses three main points: the temptation of Satan at the moment of death, the importance of having a good opinion of Allah, and the recitation of Surah Yasin (and optionally Surah al-Ra'd). The text cites two hadith proofs: one from Muslim about dying with good opinion of Allah, and another from the Sahihain about Allah being with His servant's opinion. It also quotes a hadith on the merits of reciting Surah Yasin for the dying. The commentary clarifies that the phrase 'give him water' refers to quenching thirst during the death throes, and that the instruction to recite Surah Yasin is a command indicating recommendation. The opinion of some later scholars to recite Surah al-Ra'd is also mentioned with the hadith of Jabir that it eases the soul's departure. The overarching theme is to maintain hope in Allah's mercy at the time of death, as opposed to fear during health.

Key Terms
حسن الظن بالله (ḥusn al-ẓann billāh): Having a positive expectation of Allah's mercy and forgiveness at the time of death.
سورة يس (sūrat yāsīn): The 36th chapter of the Quran, recited at the bedside of the dying due to its mention of resurrection.
النزع (al-nazʿ): The death throes or the moment of soul's departure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the wisdom (hikmah) of reciting Surah Yasin at the side of the dying?
A) It mentions the conditions of the Day of Resurrection and belief in it, renewing faith.
B) It is a command that must be obeyed without question.
C) It quenches the thirst of the dying person.
D) It protects the dying from Satan's whisper of water.

Key Takeaway
The spiritual care for the dying includes encouraging hope in Allah's mercy and reciting Surah Yasin to ease the soul's departure, based on hadith proofs.

Expelling Menstruating and Impure Persons from the Dying
Ruling with proof on expelling impure persons from the dying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling (makruh tanzih) on removing menstruating, postpartum, and impure persons from the dying, identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and explain the hadith proof regarding angels.

Core Idea
Removal of impure persons from the dying is recommended to allow angels of mercy, but not obligatory if it causes hardship.

When death approaches, family often gathers — but some may be in a state of ritual impurity. Should they be asked to leave? This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya addresses a nuanced Hanafi ruling that balances the presence of angels with the duty of care. We will examine the proof, the disagreement, and the preferred position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the ruling
Who are the persons in question? The text mentions three categories: menstruating woman (ha'id), postpartum woman (nafsa'), and person in major impurity (junub).
2
State the Hanafi position
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi), removal is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked but recommended). It is better to have them leave if possible, but not obligatory.
3
Identify the proof
The basis for removal is that angels of mercy avoid places with menstrual or postpartum impurity, and they attend the death of a believer. Therefore, a pure environment is preferred.
This is a dalil naqli (textual proof) from hadith.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars, like al-Kaki, hold that presence of such persons is not prohibited at death, especially if they are needed for care. This disagreement reflects a tension between ritual purity and family duty.
5
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
The preferred position is to recommend removal (makruh tanzih) when easy, but allow them to remain if removal causes hardship. This is the view supported by later scholars like al-Tahtawi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلفوا في إخراج الحائض والنفساء والجنب من عنده وجه الإخراج امتناع حضور الملائكة محلاً به حائض، أو نفساء كما ورد يحضر عنده طيب
And they differed on expelling the menstruating woman, the postpartum woman, and the sexually impure person from his side. The basis of expulsion is the prevention of the presence of angels in a place that has a menstruating or postpartum woman, as it has been reported that angels attend at the death of a good person.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (or disagreement among scholars) regarding whether to remove menstruating women, postpartum women, and those in a state of major ritual impurity (junub) from the presence of the dying person. The reason given for expulsion is that angels of mercy do not enter a place where there is a menstruating or postpartum woman, and the dying person is in need of their presence. The commentary notes that some scholars argue for expulsion, while others (like al-Kaki) say it is not prohibited, especially if their presence is needed for care. The text also mentions that non-Muslims should also be removed. The underlying principle is to maintain a pure environment for the angels to attend the dying person.

Key Terms
حائض (ḥāʾiḍ): A woman in the state of menstruation.
نفساء (nafsāʾ): A woman in the postpartum period.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
وجه الإخراج (wajh al-ikhrāj): The legal basis or rationale for expulsion.
امتناع حضور الملائكة (imtināʿ ḥuḍūr al-malāʾika): The prevention of angels' presence (due to impurity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the dying person dislikes their presence.
B) Because angels avoid places with such impurity.
C) Because they are physically harmful.
D) Because it is required in all cases.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends (makruh tanzih) removing menstruating, postpartum, and impure persons from the dying to allow angels to attend, but does not require it if it causes hardship.

Immediate Post-Death Actions: Sunnah Rulings and Prohibitions
Enumeration of recommended actions after death with proofs and a prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions to be performed immediately after death and explain the prohibition of placing hands on the chest.

Core Idea
After death, tie the jaw, close eyes, cover, place iron on abdomen, hands at sides, flex joints – all sunnah except hands on chest, which is haram as imitation of Ahl al-Kitab.

When a Muslim passes away, certain recommended actions are to be performed immediately. These practices, derived from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions, ensure proper care of the deceased. This lesson details each action, its ruling, and the evidence behind it. Notably, placing hands on the chest is prohibited as it resembles the practice of the People of the Book.

Guided Path
1
Identify each action
List the actions mentioned: tying jaw, closing eyes, covering with cloth, placing iron/heavy object on abdomen, placing hands at sides, flexing joints and fingers.
There are six distinct actions plus a supplication.
2
Determine the ruling for each
Most actions are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended). Placing hands on chest is not permissible (haram) because it imitates Ahl al-Kitab.
The ruling is derived from explicit text and analogy.
3
Locate the evidence
For each action, identify the proof: closing eyes is commanded in a hadith; placing iron is from the practice of Anas and a narration from al-Sha'bi; the prohibition of hands on chest is based on the principle of avoiding imitation of disbelievers.
The hadith for closing eyes is quoted: 'When you attend your dead, close the eyes...'
4
Understand the rationale
Tying the jaw keeps mouth closed; closing eyes prevents staring; iron prevents swelling; hands at sides indicate surrender; flexing joints eases washing and shrouding.
These actions have both practical and spiritual significance.
5
Distinguish the prohibition
Hands on chest is prohibited by the text because it is the practice of Ahl al-Kitab. This is an example of avoiding tashabbuh (imitation) in funerary rites.
The Hanafi position considers this makruh tahrimi or haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا مات شد لحياه بعصابة عريضة تعمهما، وتربط فوق رأسه تحسيناً، وحفظاً لفمه وغمض عيناه للأمر به في السنة ويقول مغمضه باسم الله وعلى ملة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اللهم يسر عليه أمره وسهل عليه ما بعده وأسعده بلقائك واجعل ما خرج إليه خيراً مما خرج عنه قاله الكمال ثم يسجى بثوب ويوضع على بطنه حديدة لئلا ينتفخ وهو مروي عن الشعبي، والحديد يدفع النفخ لسر فيه وإن لم يوجد فيوضع على بطنه شيء ثقيل، وروى البيهقي أن أنساً أمر بوضع حديد على بطن مولى له مات وتوضع يداه بجنبه إشارة لتسليمه الأمر لربه ولا يجوز وضعهما على صدره لأنه صنيع أهل الكتاب وتلين مفاصله وأصابعه بأن يرد ساعده لعضده وساقه لفخذه وفخذه لبطنه ويردها مليئة ليسهل غسله وإدراجه في الكفن
When he dies, they tie his jaw with a wide bandage that covers both sides (of the jaw), and it is tied above his head for improvement and to preserve his mouth, and they close his eyes due to the command in the Sunnah. The one closing his eyes says: 'In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah, O Allah, ease his matter for him, make what follows easy for him, make him happy with meeting You, and make what he has gone out to better than what he has left behind.' Al-Kamal said this. Then he is covered with a cloth, and a piece of iron is placed on his stomach so that it does not swell, and this is narrated from al-Sha'bi. Iron repels swelling due to a secret in it. If none is found, a heavy object is placed on his stomach. al-Bayhaqi narrated that Anas ordered iron to be placed on the stomach of a freed slave of his who died. And his hands are placed at his sides to indicate his surrender of the matter to his Lord. It is not permissible to place them on his chest because that is the practice of the People of the Book. And his joints and fingers are flexed by returning his forearm to his upper arm, his shin to his thigh, and his thigh to his abdomen, and he is returned (to a natural position) to facilitate his washing and wrapping in the shroud.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage enumerates the sunan (recommended acts) to be performed immediately after death. First, the jaw is tied with a wide bandage to keep it closed, a practice done for preservation and neatness. Second, the eyes are closed, following the prophetic command, and a specific supplication is recited. Third, the body is covered with a cloth. Fourth, a piece of iron (or a heavy object) is placed on the abdomen to prevent bloating; this is based on a narration from al-Sha'bi and the practice of Anas ibn Malik. Fifth, the hands are placed at the sides, not on the chest, because placing them on the chest is a practice of the People of the Book and is therefore prohibited. Sixth, the joints are flexed to prevent rigor mortis and facilitate washing and enshrouding. Each action has its proof from the Sunnah or practice of the Companions. The text also notes that if iron is not available, any heavy object suffices.

Key Terms
الشد (لحياه) (al-shadd (liḥyayhi)): Tying the jaw of the deceased with a bandage to keep the mouth closed.
تسجية (tasjiyah): Covering the deceased with a cloth.
وضع الحديدة (waḍʿ al-ḥadīdah): Placing a piece of iron or heavy object on the abdomen to prevent swelling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on placing the hands of the deceased on the chest?
A) Sunnah muakkadah.
B) Mubah (permissible).
C) Not permissible (imitating Ahl al-Kitab).
D) Wajib (obligatory).

Key Takeaway
The immediate sunnah actions after death include tying the jaw, closing eyes, covering, placing iron on abdomen, hands at sides, and flexing joints; placing hands on chest is prohibited as it imitates Ahl al-Kitab.

Reciting Quran Near the Deceased Before Washing: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on reciting Quran near the deceased before ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Quran near the deceased before washing, explain the proof, and identify the underlying rationale.

Core Idea
Reciting Quran near the unwashed deceased is disliked (makruh tanzih) to protect the Quran from impurity, even though the dead body is not physically impure.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from Maraqi al-Falah and its hashya by al-Tahtawi: is it permissible to recite Quran in the presence of a deceased person before they have been washed? The text rules that it is disliked (makruh tanzih), and the commentary explores the reasoning based on the nature of the impurity of the dead. Understanding this ruling sheds light on how Hanafi fiqh balances respect for the Quran with the state of the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? What hukm level is assigned?
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence supports the ruling? (hadith: 'The believer does not become impure...')
3
Understand the rationale
Why is it disliked? (to protect the Quran from impurity until the body is washed)
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement within the Hanafi school or with other schools?
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon for fatwa and why?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتكره قراءة القرآن عنده حتى يغسل تنزيهاً للقرآن عن نجاسة الحدث بالموت والخبث فإنه يزول عن المسلم
And it is disliked to recite Quran near him (the deceased) until he is washed, to keep the Quran pure from the impurity of ritual impurity (hadath) caused by death and from physical impurity (khabath), for it (impurity) is removed from the Muslim.
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that reciting Quran in the presence of the deceased before washing is makruh (disliked). The reason given is to protect the Quran from being near ritual and physical impurity, as the dead body is considered impure until washed. The hashya then engages in a detailed discussion about the nature of the impurity of the dead: some scholars consider it najasat hadath (ritual impurity like janaba), while others consider it najasat khabath (physical filth). The commentator notes that the hadith 'The Muslim does not become impure, alive or dead' contradicts the idea of physical impurity. He reconciles by saying that any impurity is removed by washing. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that recitation is nevertheless disliked before washing, due to the dominant presence of impurity (even if only ritual). The text also cites a hadith that the Prophet kissed Uthman ibn Maz'un after death, indicating the dead body is not physically impure. Ultimately, the ruling is one of karahah tanzihiyyah (disliked but not sinful).

Key Terms
نجاسة الحدث (najāsat al-ḥadath): Ritual impurity that necessitates ghusl, like janaba. The dead body is considered in a state of hadath.
كراهة (karāhah): Disliked (makruh tanzih), meaning it is better to avoid but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is reciting Quran near the deceased disliked before washing according to the text?
A) Because the dead person dislikes it.
B) To keep the Quran away from impurity until the body is washed.
C) Because it is a waste of time.
D) Because the dead cannot hear it.

Key Takeaway
Reciting Quran near the deceased before washing is makruh tanzih to protect the Quran from impurity, even though the dead are not physically impure.

Hastening Funeral Preparation and Announcing Death
Rulings on announcing death and hastening janazah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hastening funeral preparation, cite the hadith evidence, and identify the exception that may delay it.

Core Idea
Hastening a Muslim's funeral is wajib, but precaution demands delay when death is uncertain.

The preparation of a deceased Muslim includes washing, shrouding, and burial. The Shariah encourages haste to avoid detaining the corpse unnecessarily. However, this haste is balanced by the need for certainty of death. This lesson explores the ruling on hastening the janazah, the prophetic evidence, and the critical refinement that may require delay in cases of apparent death from stroke.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage discusses two acts: informing people of a death (i'lam) and hastening the funeral preparation (ta'jil al-tajhiz). The first is mustahabb (recommended), the second is wajib (obligatory).
Both acts are based on the sunnah.
2
Locate the primary proof for hastening
The key evidence is a hadith: 'Hasten him, for it is not proper for a Muslim corpse to be detained among his family.' The imperative verb 'عجلوا' (hasten) is central.
The hadith is ahad, so its authority is zanni al-thubut.
3
Apply Hanafi usul: imperative implies wujub
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) without a qualifying indication (qarinah) indicates obligation (wujub). Here, the command 'عجلوا' is taken at face value, establishing wujub, not fard, because the thubut is zanni.
This is the standard Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah).
4
Identify the critical refinement: precaution for stroke
Some doctors note that death from stroke (al-saktah) may be apparent but not real; thus, immediate burial risks burying alive. The text resolves this by requiring delay until certainty (e.g., through signs of decay). This precaution (ihtiyat) overrides the general command to hasten in such cases.
The Prophet's own burial was delayed, providing a precedent.
5
Recognize the mufta bihi and exceptions
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that hastening is wajib unless there is a valid excuse, such as uncertainty of death or a beneficial delay (e.g., waiting for relatives). The ruling applies to Muslims; for non-Muslims, different rules apply.
The later Hanafi consensus adopts this nuanced position.

Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah deals with the rulings on announcing a death and hastening the funeral preparation. The author begins by confirming that it is not blameworthy but rather recommended to inform people of a Muslim's death, especially if the deceased was a righteous person, so that many may pray over him. This is supported by the Prophet's own actions in announcing the deaths of al-Najashi and the companions. However, excessive praise and pompous announcements are discouraged. The author then discusses the obligation of hastening the funeral preparation once death is certain, citing the hadith 'Hasten him, for it is not proper for a Muslim corpse to be detained among his family.' He addresses a potential conflict with the need for precaution, as some deaths (e.g., from stroke) may be apparent but not real, and thus delaying until certainty is necessary. The commentary includes a lengthy discussion on the nature of death from stroke and the recommendation to hasten five things: marriage, burial, debt repayment, repentance, and hospitality. The passage also explains the proper placement of the deceased on a bier or similar surface for washing.

Key Terms
إعلام الناس بموته (i'lam al-nas bi-mawtihi): Informing people of the death of a Muslim, especially a righteous person, to encourage participation in the funeral prayer.
يعجل بتجهيزه (yu'ajjilu bi-tajhizihi): To hasten the preparation of the deceased for burial, including washing, shrouding, and transporting to the grave.
السكتة (al-saktah): A stroke or apoplectic fit causing apparent death; a condition where death is uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on hastening the funeral preparation of a deceased Muslim?
A) It is fard.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is sunnah muakkadah.
D) It is mubah.

Key Takeaway
Hastening a Muslim's funeral is wajib based on the prophetic command, but this is qualified by the need for certainty of death; precaution requires delay in cases of apparent death from stroke, and normal delays for valid reasons are permissible.

Eulogizing the Deceased (Ritha) in Hanafi Fiqh
Clarifying the permissibility of eulogy with the condition of no exaggeration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eulogizing the deceased and identify the condition that makes it permissible or impermissible.

Core Idea
Eulogy is permissible as long as it avoids exaggeration—moderation is key.

In Hanafi fiqh, expressing praise for the deceased through poetry or other means is generally allowed. This lesson examines the ruling on ritha (eulogy) from the Hashiya, focusing on the critical condition that prevents it from becoming prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the beginning of the passage: the author says 'la ba'sa' (there is no harm). This indicates permissibility (ibahah) for eulogizing the deceased.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) as a baseline.
2
Locate the condition
The permissibility is immediately qualified by the phrase 'ma lam yufrit fi madhih' (as long as he does not exaggerate in praising him). This is the key condition.
Exaggeration (ifrat) changes the ruling.
3
Understand the ruling hierarchy
If exaggeration occurs, the ruling shifts from permissible to disliked or even prohibited, depending on the severity and content of the exaggeration.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between moderate praise and flattery.
4
Note the textual correction
The author corrects a spelling: the correct term is 'ritha' (with ra), not 'bartha' (with ba). This is a linguistic note that does not affect the ruling.
Proper terminology ensures precision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس (۱) بإرثاء الميت بشعر، أو غيره ما لم يفرط في مدحه، ولا يكره البكاء عليه بإرسال الدموع، بلا رفع صوت، ولا نياحة ولا شق ثوب، وضرب خد ونحو ذلك، وسواء في ذلك قبل الموت، وبعده على الصحيح ) النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بكى على ابنه ابراهيم فقال له عبد الرحمن بن عوف وأنت يا رسول الله تبكي فقال: يا ابن عوف إنها رحمة وقال : إن العين تدمع والقلب يحزن، ولا نقول إلا ما يرضي ربنا، وإنا بفرقاك يا إبراهيم لمحزونون» أخرجه الشيخان وفي حديث ألا تسمعون أن الله لا يعذب بدمع العين، ولا بحزن القلب، ولكن يعذب بهذا، وأشار إلى لسانه، أو يرحم رواه الشيخان أيضاً، وأما ما ورد ان الميت ليعذب ببكاء أهله عليه فأجمعوا على أنه محمول على البكاء بصوت، ونياحة ولا بمجرد الدمع وحمله عامة أهل العلم على ما إذا أوصى بذلك، (1) قوله بارثاء هكذا في الأصل وصوابه برثاء لأن فعله ثلاثي كما يعلم بمراجعة المصباح وغيره اهـ م الواحد. وأما من بكوا عليه وناحوا من غير وصية فلا لقوله تعالى : ولا تزروا زرة وزر أخرى [الأنعام / ٦] وهذا هو الصحيح من أوجه الحمل، وأوجب داود ومن تبعه الوصية بترك البكاء والنوح عليه، وقيل المراد بالعذاب أن يتأذى الميت بذلك إذ لا شك في تأذي الأرواح بما تتأذى به الأشباح قال في شرح المشكاة والحاصل أن الميت إذا كان له تسبب في هذه المعصية فالعذاب على حقيقته، ويعذب بفعل نفسه حيث تسبب في ذلك لا بفعل غيره وإلا فمحمول على تألمه سواء عند نزعه أو موته ويستوي فيه الكافر، والمؤمن وبهذا يحصل الجمع بين قوله تعالى : ولا تزروا زرة ورز أخرى وبين الأحاديث المطلقة في هذه البلية الكبرى اهـ.
And there is no harm in eulogizing the deceased with poetry or otherwise, as long as one does not exaggerate in praising him. And crying over him with tears, without raising the voice, wailing, tearing clothes, striking the cheek, and the like, is not disliked. And it is the same whether before death or after, according to the correct view. The Prophet, peace be upon him, cried over his son Ibrahim, so Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf said, 'You too, O Messenger of Allah, cry?' He said, 'O Ibn Awf, it is mercy.' And he said, 'The eye weeps and the heart grieves, and we do not say except what pleases our Lord, and indeed we are saddened by your separation, O Ibrahim.' Narrated by the two Shaykhs. And in a hadith: 'Do you not hear that Allah does not punish for the tear of the eye nor for the grief of the heart, but He punishes for this' and he pointed to his tongue, or He shows mercy. Also narrated by the two Shaykhs. And as for what has come that the deceased is punished by the crying of his family over him, they are unanimous that it is interpreted as crying with voice and wailing, not just tears. And the generality of scholars interpret it as the case when he had willed that. (1) The author's word 'baritha' is thus in the original, but correct is 'ritha' because its verb is triliteral, as known from al-Misbah and others. End. One. As for those who cry and wail over him without a will, then no [punishment], because of the saying of the Exalted: 'And no bearer of burdens shall bear the burden of another' [al-An'am:6]. And this is the correct aspect of interpretation. And Dawud and those who followed him made it obligatory to make a will to stop crying and wailing over him. And it was said that the intended meaning of punishment is that the deceased is harmed by that, for there is no doubt that souls are harmed by what affects the bodies. He said in Sharh al-Mishkat: The sum is that if the deceased had a hand in this sin, then the punishment is literal, and he is punished for his own action because he caused it, not for the action of others. Otherwise, it is interpreted as his being pained, whether at the time of his agony or his death. And it is the same for the disbeliever and the believer. And by this, reconciliation is achieved between the verse 'No bearer of burdens shall bear the burden of another' and the absolute hadiths on this great affliction. End.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya addresses the rulings on mourning for the deceased. It clarifies that eulogizing with poetry or other means is permissible as long as it does not involve excessive praise. Crying with tears, without loud wailing or harmful actions, is not disliked; this is supported by the Prophet's own crying over his son Ibrahim. The hadith explicitly states that Allah does not punish for tears but for the tongue (i.e., wailing). The controversial hadith that the deceased is punished by family's crying is interpreted by consensus to refer to wailing, not mere tears. If the deceased did not cause or will such wailing, then there is no punishment. A detailed discussion follows reconciling the verse 'No bearer of burdens...' with the hadiths, concluding that if the deceased caused the wailing (e.g., by will or practice), then punishment is for his own action; otherwise, it is mere pain.

Key Terms
إرثاء/رثاء (irtha/ritha): Eulogizing the deceased, especially with poetry, in a manner that does not involve exaggeration.
نياحة (niyahah): Loud wailing, striking cheeks, tearing clothes, and other actions of mourning that are prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the condition for permissible eulogy according to the Hashiya?
A) The deceased must have willed it.
B) It must be in Arabic.
C) It must not involve exaggeration in praise.
D) It must be done only by close relatives.

Key Takeaway
Eulogy is permissible in Hanafi fiqh provided it avoids exaggeration; this balanced approach allows expression of grief while maintaining Islamic decorum.

Crying for the Dead: Permissible Tears vs. Prohibited Wailing
Clarifying permissible crying and prohibited wailing with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between permissible crying with tears and prohibited wailing, and cite the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Tears from a grieved heart are natural and permissible; wailing with the tongue invites punishment.

The Prophet himself cried over his son Ibrahim, showing that tears of mercy are allowed. However, loud wailing and striking oneself are from the customs of ignorance. This lesson examines the hadith evidence that distinguishes between permissible grief and forbidden actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on crying
The text states 'la yukrah' (is not disliked) for crying with tears without raising the voice or engaging in wailing. This indicates it is permissible (mubah) or even slightly recommended (since it shows natural mercy).
The baseline ruling is permissibility, not prohibition.
2
List the prohibited actions
The text lists: wailing (niyahah), tearing clothes, striking cheeks, and similar acts. These are forbidden (haram) because they involve excessive grief and self-harm.
These actions are characteristic of Jahiliyyah.
3
Analyze the first hadith (Prophet's crying)
The Prophet cried over his son, teaching that tears are a mercy, not a sin. He distinguished between the eye's tears and the heart's grief (permissible) and saying things that displease Allah (impermissible).
This hadith is used as proof that crying with tears is allowed.
4
Analyze the second hadith (punishment by tongue)
The Prophet said Allah does not punish for tears or grief but for what the tongue utters. This directly supports that wailing (using the tongue) is punishable, while silent tears are not.
The pointing to the tongue emphasizes the prohibition of wailing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس (۱) بإرثاء الميت بشعر، أو غيره ما لم يفرط في مدحه، ولا يكره البكاء عليه بإرسال الدموع، بلا رفع صوت، ولا نياحة ولا شق ثوب، وضرب خد ونحو ذلك، وسواء في ذلك قبل الموت، وبعده على الصحيح ) النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بكى على ابنه ابراهيم فقال له عبد الرحمن بن عوف وأنت يا رسول الله تبكي فقال: يا ابن عوف إنها رحمة وقال : إن العين تدمع والقلب يحزن، ولا نقول إلا ما يرضي ربنا، وإنا بفرقاك يا إبراهيم لمحزونون» أخرجه الشيخان وفي حديث ألا تسمعون أن الله لا يعذب بدمع العين، ولا بحزن القلب، ولكن يعذب بهذا، وأشار إلى لسانه، أو يرحم رواه الشيخان أيضاً، وأما ما ورد ان الميت ليعذب ببكاء أهله عليه فأجمعوا على أنه محمول على البكاء بصوت، ونياحة ولا بمجرد الدمع وحمله عامة أهل العلم على ما إذا أوصى بذلك، (1) قوله بارثاء هكذا في الأصل وصوابه برثاء لأن فعله ثلاثي كما يعلم بمراجعة المصباح وغيره اهـ م الواحد. وأما من بكوا عليه وناحوا من غير وصية فلا لقوله تعالى : ولا تزروا زرة وزر أخرى [الأنعام / ٦] وهذا هو الصحيح من أوجه الحمل، وأوجب داود ومن تبعه الوصية بترك البكاء والنوح عليه، وقيل المراد بالعذاب أن يتأذى الميت بذلك إذ لا شك في تأذي الأرواح بما تتأذى به الأشباح قال في شرح المشكاة والحاصل أن الميت إذا كان له تسبب في هذه المعصية فالعذاب على حقيقته، ويعذب بفعل نفسه حيث تسبب في ذلك لا بفعل غيره وإلا فمحمول على تألمه سواء عند نزعه أو موته ويستوي فيه الكافر، والمؤمن وبهذا يحصل الجمع بين قوله تعالى : ولا تزروا زرة ورز أخرى وبين الأحاديث المطلقة في هذه البلية الكبرى اهـ.
And there is no harm in eulogizing the deceased with poetry or otherwise, as long as one does not exaggerate in praising him. And crying over him with tears, without raising the voice, wailing, tearing clothes, striking the cheek, and the like, is not disliked. And it is the same whether before death or after, according to the correct view. The Prophet, peace be upon him, cried over his son Ibrahim, so Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf said, 'You too, O Messenger of Allah, cry?' He said, 'O Ibn Awf, it is mercy.' And he said, 'The eye weeps and the heart grieves, and we do not say except what pleases our Lord, and indeed we are saddened by your separation, O Ibrahim.' Narrated by the two Shaykhs. And in a hadith: 'Do you not hear that Allah does not punish for the tear of the eye nor for the grief of the heart, but He punishes for this' and he pointed to his tongue, or He shows mercy. Also narrated by the two Shaykhs. And as for what has come that the deceased is punished by the crying of his family over him, they are unanimous that it is interpreted as crying with voice and wailing, not just tears. And the generality of scholars interpret it as the case when he had willed that. (1) The author's word 'baritha' is thus in the original, but correct is 'ritha' because its verb is triliteral, as known from al-Misbah and others. End. One. As for those who cry and wail over him without a will, then no [punishment], because of the saying of the Exalted: 'And no bearer of burdens shall bear the burden of another' [al-An'am:6]. And this is the correct aspect of interpretation. And Dawud and those who followed him made it obligatory to make a will to stop crying and wailing over him. And it was said that the intended meaning of punishment is that the deceased is harmed by that, for there is no doubt that souls are harmed by what affects the bodies. He said in Sharh al-Mishkat: The sum is that if the deceased had a hand in this sin, then the punishment is literal, and he is punished for his own action because he caused it, not for the action of others. Otherwise, it is interpreted as his being pained, whether at the time of his agony or his death. And it is the same for the disbeliever and the believer. And by this, reconciliation is achieved between the verse 'No bearer of burdens shall bear the burden of another' and the absolute hadiths on this great affliction. End.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya addresses the rulings on mourning for the deceased. It clarifies that eulogizing with poetry or other means is permissible as long as it does not involve excessive praise. Crying with tears, without loud wailing or harmful actions, is not disliked; this is supported by the Prophet's own crying over his son Ibrahim. The hadith explicitly states that Allah does not punish for tears but for the tongue (i.e., wailing). The controversial hadith that the deceased is punished by family's crying is interpreted by consensus to refer to wailing, not mere tears. If the deceased did not cause or will such wailing, then there is no punishment. A detailed discussion follows reconciling the verse 'No bearer of burdens...' with the hadiths, concluding that if the deceased caused the wailing (e.g., by will or practice), then punishment is for his own action; otherwise, it is mere pain.

Key Terms
نياحة (niyahah): Loud wailing, striking cheeks, tearing clothes, and other actions of mourning that are prohibited.
دمعة (dam'ah): Tear; permissible if without wailing or sinful actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, what does Allah punish for?
A) The tear of the eye
B) The grief of the heart
C) What the tongue utters
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Crying with tears is a natural and permissible expression of grief, while wailing with the tongue and harmful actions are prohibited.

Reconciling the Hadith on Punishment of the Deceased for Family's Crying
Critical refinement of the hadith on punishment and reconciliation with Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith 'the deceased is punished by the crying of his family' and reconcile it with the Quranic principle of individual responsibility.

Core Idea
The deceased is not punished for others' sins unless he caused it by will or practice.

A hadith states that the deceased is punished by the crying of his family. This appears to conflict with the Quranic verse that no soul bears another's burden. The Hanafi school resolves this by interpreting the crying as wailing and requiring that the deceased had a role in causing it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent conflict
The hadith seems to say the deceased suffers because of others' crying. But Quran 6:164 states no bearer of burdens bears another's burden. This is the conflict.
This conflict must be resolved for legal consistency.
2
State the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith
The Hanafis (and the majority) interpret the crying in the hadith as wailing (niyahah) with voice, not silent tears. Moreover, the punishment applies only if the deceased had willed or encouraged such wailing.
The hadith is thus restricted to specific cases.
3
Provide the Quranic evidence
The verse 'No bearer of burdens bears the burden of another' is cited as the overriding principle. If the deceased did not cause the wailing, he cannot be punished for it.
This verse is definitive (qat'i) and cannot be contradicted by a hadith that is open to interpretation.
4
Consider the alternative view (Dawud)
Dawud al-Zahiri and his followers took the hadith literally and made it obligatory for the deceased to make a will forbidding crying and wailing.
The Hanafi school does not require this.
5
Apply the reconciliation
The commentator (Sharh al-Mishkat) provides a synthesis: if the deceased caused the sin (e.g., by instructing people to wail), then the punishment is for his own action. Otherwise, the hadith refers to mere pain (ta'addhi) of the deceased, not punishment in the afterlife. This reconciles the texts.
This highlights the Hanafi methodology of harmonizing conflicting evidence.

The Ruling on Hastening Burial and the Exception for Certainty of Death
Explains the recommendation to hasten burial and the exception for sudden death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on hastening burial and identify the exceptional case where delay becomes obligatory.

Core Idea
Hasten burial is recommended, not obligatory – unless doubt of death arises, then delay is wajib.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah addresses the balance between honoring the deceased by burying quickly and the necessity of certainty of death. It presents the primary ruling based on a hadith and then introduces a crucial exception for cases of apparent death (sakta), where caution (ihtiyat) requires delay until true death is confirmed. Students will learn both the evidence and the practical application of this nuanced ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
Recognize that the default ruling is hastening burial (ta'jil). The text cites the hadith 'And hasten with him...' as evidence.
The imperative 'عجلوا' in Hanafi usul indicates recommendation, not obligation, due to a countervailing caution.
2
Understand the evidence
The hadith commands hastening, but Hanafi scholars interpret it as mustahabb (recommended) because of the need for certainty of death. The Prophet's own burial was delayed for nearly two days, showing that delay is permissible.
3
Identify the exception
The text introduces 'sakta' (sudden apparent death) where it is difficult to ascertain actual death. Medical opinion is cited that many are buried alive in such cases.
The exception applies specifically to those with the disease of sakta.
4
Apply the cautionary principle
Due to ihtiyat (caution), delay becomes obligatory (wajib) when there is doubt about death. Certainty (yaqin) must be achieved, often through visible signs of decay or expert medical confirmation.
This overrides the general recommendation of haste.
5
Observe the practical outcome
For a person who dies of sakta, burial must be delayed until death is certain. For others, hastening remains recommended. The text also notes that the Prophet's delay was due to practical reasons, not doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إكراماً له لما في الحديث، وعجلوا به فإنه لا ينبغي لجيفة مسلم أن تحبس بين ظهراني أهله، والصارف عن وجوب التعجيل الاحتياط قال بعض الأطباء أن كثيرين ممن يموت بالسكتة ظاهرًا يدفنون أحياء لأنه يعسر إدراك الموت الحقيقي بها إلا على أفضل الأطباء فيتعين التأخير فيها إلى ظهور اليقين بنحو التغير وقد مات النبي يوم الإثنين ضحوة ودفن في جوف الليل من ليلة الأربعاء (فيوضع كما مات) الكاف للمفاجأة إذا تيقن موته وأما من بكوا عليه وناحوا من غير وصية فلا لقوله تعالى : ولا تزروا زرة وزر أخرى [الأنعام / ٦] وهذا هو الصحيح من أوجه الحمل، وأوجب داود ومن تبعه الوصية بترك البكاء والنوح عليه، وقيل المراد بالعذاب أن يتأذى الميت بذلك إذ لا شك في تأذي الأرواح بما تتأذى به الأشباح قال في شرح المشكاة والحاصل أن الميت إذا كان له تسبب في هذه المعصية فالعذاب على حقيقته، ويعذب بفعل نفسه حيث تسبب في ذلك لا بفعل غيره وإلا فمحمول على تألمه سواء عند نزعه أو موته ويستوي فيه الكافر، والمؤمن وبهذا يحصل الجمع بين قوله تعالى : ولا تزروا زرة ورز أخرى وبين الأحاديث المطلقة في هذه البلية الكبرى اهـ. قوله: (بين ظهراني (أهله أي ظهر أهله قال في القاموس : وهو بين ظهرهم، وظهرانيهم، ولا تكسر النون وبين أظهرهم أي وسطهم .اهـ. قوله (الاحتياط) أي في أمر المريض فإنه يحتمل أن الذي به داء السكتة قوله : (قال بعض الأطباء أتى به دليلاً للاحتياط ولو جعل الدليل أولاً تأخر دفن النبي لكان أنسب قوله ممن يموت بالسكتة) أي يظنون أنهم موتى، وإليه أشار بقوله ظاهراً. قوله : (بها) أي بسبب السكتة فالموت لا يشتبه إلا فيمن فيه هذا الداء . قوله : ( فيتعين التأخير الخ ظاهر هذا وجوب التأخير، وهو ينافي التعجيل المطلوب إلا أن يحمل ذلك الوجوب على من به داء السكتة، وأصل هذا الداء يحدث من أكل الأوز الأبيض، والملوخية وتقليتها بدهن ويمكث هذا الداء ثمان ساعات، وظاهر كلامهم أن التأخير مطلوب مطلقاً لما رواه من الحديث، والمراد التأخير إلى تيقن الموت فإنه ربما عرض عليه هذا الداء، وقد يقال كيف يتأتى مع وجود العلامات الدالة عليه ويستحب تعجيل خمسة أشياء جمعت في هذه الأبيات وهي : وخمسة قد رأوا تعجيلها حسناً وفي سواهـا تـأتـي واسـع الـمـهـل تزويج كفء، ومــيــت هــاك ثالثها دفع الديون، وتب الله من زلل والخامس الضيف إذ يأتيك في نزل فقم له بحثيث الجد واحتفل
Out of honoring him due to the hadith, 'And hasten with him, for it is not befitting that the corpse of a Muslim be detained among his family.' And the preventer from the obligation of hastening is caution. Some doctors said that many who die of sudden death are apparently buried alive because it is difficult to ascertain true death except by the best doctors, so delay is necessary in such cases until certainty appears through something like change. The Prophet died on Monday forenoon and was buried in the middle of the night of Wednesday. (He is placed as he died) the kaf is for suddenness when his death is certain. As for those who cry and wail over him without bequest, it is not permissible due to His statement: 'And no bearer of burdens will bear the burden of another' [6:164]. This is the correct interpretation. Dawud and his followers made it obligatory to bequeath against crying and wailing. It is said that the meaning of punishment is that the deceased is harmed by that, since there is no doubt that spirits are harmed by what bodies are harmed by. The author of Sharh al-Mishkat said: The conclusion is that if the deceased had a role in this sin, then the punishment is real, and he is punished for his own action because he caused it, not for the action of another. Otherwise, it is interpreted as his pain, whether at the time of death or after death, and it applies equally to the disbeliever and the believer. By this, reconciliation is achieved between His statement 'And no bearer bears the burden of another' and the absolute hadiths regarding this great calamity. End. (His saying: 'among his family' means in their midst. He said in al-Qamus: 'He is among them (bayna zuhrihim) and bayna zuhrani him, and do not break the nun, and bayna azhurihim i.e. in their midst.' End. (His saying: 'caution') i.e. regarding the patient, for it is possible that he who has the disease of sudden death. (His saying: 'Some doctors said') He brought it as evidence for caution, and if he had made the evidence first the delay of the Prophet's burial, it would have been more appropriate. (His saying: 'those who die of sudden death') i.e., they are thought to be dead, and he alluded to that by saying 'apparently'. (His saying: 'by it') i.e., due to sudden death; death is not mistaken except in one who has this disease. (His saying: 'Then delay is necessary') This apparently indicates the obligation of delay, and it contradicts the requested hastening, unless that obligation is applied to one who has the disease of sudden death. The origin of this disease occurs from eating white goose and malukhiyya and frying it with oil, and this disease lasts eight hours. The apparent meaning of their words is that delay is requested absolutely because of what was narrated in the hadith, and the intended meaning is delay until certainty of death, for it is possible that this disease may befall him. And it may be said: How can it be possible with the presence of the signs indicating it? And it is recommended to hasten five things gathered in these verses: Five things they have seen as good to hasten, and in other matters there is ample time: Marriage of a compatible match, a deceased person, the third is repayment of debts, repentance from misdeeds, and the fifth is the guest when he comes to you in a lodging, so stand up for him with utmost seriousness and diligence.
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah deals with the ruling on hastening burial. The author begins by citing the hadith that encourages hastening the burial of a Muslim, stating that it is recommended to bury the deceased quickly. However, he then introduces an exception: if there is doubt about the actual death, such as in cases of sudden death (sakta), it is obligatory to delay burial until certainty is achieved. This is based on the cautionary principle (ihtiyat) and the medical opinion that some people who appear dead are actually still alive. The author also mentions that the Prophet (peace be upon him) died on Monday and was buried on Wednesday night, indicating that some delay is permissible. He then discusses the issue of crying and wailing over the deceased, clarifying that if the deceased did not bequeath against it, those who cry do not bear sin because of the Quranic verse that no soul bears another's burden. However, if the deceased had caused or encouraged such practices, he may be held accountable. The passage concludes with a poetic summary of five things it is recommended to hasten: marriage, burial, repayment of debts, repentance, and hospitality. The overall lesson is that while haste is recommended in burial, it must be balanced with certainty of death, and other matters like mourning practices have their own rulings.

Key Terms
السكتة (al-saktah): Sudden death or apparent death where it is difficult to ascertain actual death; a condition mentioned in the text where victims appear dead but may still be alive.
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Hastening of burial; recommended action in Hanafi fiqh.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Caution; a principle that leads to the obligation of delay when death is uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on delaying burial in a case of sudden death (sakta)?
A) Delaying is recommended but not obligatory.
B) Delaying is obligatory until death is certain.
C) Delaying is prohibited because of the hadith to hasten.
D) Delaying is only recommended if family requests it.

Key Takeaway
Hasten burial is recommended, but when death is uncertain (e.g., sudden death), delay becomes obligatory to avoid burying a living person.

Placing the Deceased for Washing: Surface, Fumigation, and Orientation
Practical rulings for placing the deceased before washing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for placing a deceased body before washing, including the recommended surface, fumigation with an odd number of incense burners, and the valid orientations.

Core Idea
The deceased may be placed in any convenient orientation for washing; fumigation with an odd number of incense burners is sunnah.

Before the sacred duty of washing the deceased, the body must be placed on a suitable surface. The Hanafi school provides practical guidance: a bier is preferred, fumigation with an odd number of incense burners honors the deceased, and orientation is flexible—any direction that facilitates washing is acceptable, though some earlier opinions suggest other placements. This lesson clarifies these rulings and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the required surface
The deceased should be placed on a bier (tacht) specifically used for washing. If unavailable, a plank or elevated stone suffices. The purpose is to allow water to flow and facilitate washing.
The surface must be raised; the ground alone is insufficient.
2
Recognize the sunnah of fumigation
Perfuming the bier with incense (sarir mujammar) is recommended to mask odors and honor the deceased. The number of incense burners must be odd: 3, 5, or 7, according to different authorities.
The odd number is a sunnah; exceeding 7 is not practiced.
3
Understand the orientation ikhtilaf
Three opinions exist: the most correct (al-ashahh) is that the body may be placed in any convenient direction. A second opinion says widthwise (like in the grave), and a third says towards the qibla. The first view is preferred for practicality.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate; all views have scholarly support.
4
Apply the ruling in practice
In a typical scenario, the body is placed on a clean, raised surface, optionally fumigated with an odd number of incense burners, and oriented in a way that eases washing—no fixed direction required.
Delaying washing due to a valid excuse is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فيوضع كمامات) لئلا تغيره نداوة الأرض، وقيده القدوري بما إذا أرادوا غسله، وهو الذي عليه العمل اليوم اهـ ولا بأس بالتأخير لعارض كما في ابن أمير حاج. قوله: (على التخت الذي يغسل عليه فإن لم يوجد فعلى لوح، أو حجر مرتفع ليمكن غسله سرير) هو الأئمة على سرير مجمر) أي مبخر إخفاء لكريه الرائحة وتعظيماً للميت ويكون (وتراً) ثلاثاً، أو خمساً ولا يزاد عليه قاله الزيلعي وفي الكافي والنهاية أو سبعاً ولا يزاد وكيفيته أن يدار بالمجمرة حول السرير (ويوضع الميت (كيف اتفق على الأصح) قاله شمس السرخسي وقيل : عرضاً وقيل : إلى القبلة
His saying: 'He is placed as he died' so that the dampness of the ground does not change him, and al-Quduri restricted it to when they intend to wash him, and that is what is practiced today. There is no harm in delaying due to a temporary excuse as in Ibn Amir Hajj. His saying: 'On the bier upon which he is washed; if not found, then on a plank or an elevated stone so that washing is possible. A bier' meaning the imams (use) a fumigated bier, i.e., perfumed to conceal bad odor and to honor the deceased, and it should be an odd number: three, five, and no more, according to al-Zayla'i, and in al-Kafi and al-Nihaya: or seven and no more. The method is to circle the censer around the bier. 'And the deceased is placed' as it may be, according to the most correct view, as stated by Shams al-Sarakhsi. It is also said: widthwise, and it is also said: towards the qibla.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage discusses the practical arrangements for placing the deceased before washing. The body should be placed on a bier (tacht) or any raised surface to facilitate washing. The bier may be perfumed with incense to mask odor and honor the deceased, and the number of incense burners should be odd (3, 5, or 7). Regarding orientation, there are three opinions: the most correct view (al-ashahh) is that the body can be placed in any direction that is convenient; another opinion says it should be placed widthwise (as in the grave); and a third says the feet should face the qibla. The commentator notes that the practice today is to place the body on a bier when intending to wash it. Delay is permissible if there is a valid excuse.

Key Terms
سرير مجمر (sarir mujammar): A fumigated bier, perfumed with incense to honor the deceased and mask odor.
وتري (watri): Odd number (3, 5, or 7) for the number of incense burners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view (al-ashahh), how should the deceased be placed before washing?
A) Only widthwise
B) Only towards the qibla
C) In any way that is convenient
D) Only on a fumigated bier

Key Takeaway
The deceased may be placed in any convenient orientation for washing; fumigation with an odd number of incense burners is a recommended sunnah.

Covering the Deceased's 'Awrah and Stripping Clothes
Ruling with proof on covering the deceased's 'awrah and stripping clothes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on covering the deceased's 'awrah and distinguish between the two views on the extent of coverage.

Core Idea
Covering the deceased's 'awrah is wajib; the easier view allows covering only the genitals since desire is absent.

When preparing a deceased body for washing, one of the first steps is to cover the private parts. The Hanafi school discusses the extent of this covering, with some scholars arguing for the full 'awrah from navel to knee, and others permitting coverage of only the genitals. This lesson examines the ruling and the rationale behind the easier view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that covering the deceased's 'awrah (private parts) is wajib (obligatory). The text states 'yustaru' (he covers) indicating a command.
Wajib here means obligatory, not merely recommended.
2
Locate the scope of 'awrah: two views
The text presents two views: one from navel to knee (the correct view in al-Nihaya) and the easier view from al-Hidayah that suffices to cover only the genitals (al-'awrah al-ghalizah).
The easier view is justified by the absence of desire from the deceased.
3
Understand the rationale for the easier view
The easier view is supported by two points: it is the apparent of the riwaya (zahir al-riwaya) and because desire is nullified (li-batlan al-shahwah).
Zahir al-riwaya refers to the most reliable transmitted position in the school.
4
Apply the ruling to stripping clothes and washing
After covering, the deceased is stripped of clothes (except for a khuntha, who is washed in his/her clothes). The 'awrah is washed with a folded cloth to avoid direct touch.
Direct touch of the 'awrah is prohibited, hence the use of a barrier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستر عورته ما بين سرته إلى ركبته قاله الزيلعي، والنهاية هو الصحيح، وفي الهداية يكتفي بستر العورة الغليظة هو الصحيح تيسراً وهو ظاهر الرواية ولبطلان الشهوة ( ثم) بعد ستر عورته بإدخال الساتر من تحت الثياب (جرد عن ثيابه) إن لم يكن خنثى، وتغسل عورته بخرقة ملفوفة تحت الساتر أو من فوقه إن لم يوجد خرقة
He covers his private parts from his navel to his knee, al-Zayla'i said so, and in al-Nihaya it is the correct view. In al-Hidayah, it suffices to cover the thicker private parts; this is the correct view for convenience, and it is the apparent of the riwaya, and because desire is nullified. Then, after covering his private parts by inserting the covering under the clothes, he is stripped of his clothes unless he is a khuntha (hermaphrodite), and his private parts are washed with a folded cloth under the covering or from above if no cloth is found.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage covers the rules for covering the deceased and stripping the clothes. The 'awrah (private area) that must be covered is from the navel to the knee according to the correct view. However, in al-Hidayah, it is considered sufficient to cover only the 'awrah ghalizah (the genitals) because there is no risk of desire from a dead body. This is the apparent of the riwaya (zahir al-riwaya). After covering, the clothes are removed so that washing can be performed. An exception is made for a khuntha (ambiguous gender), who is washed in his/her clothes. Then the private area is washed by using a folded cloth to avoid direct touch, which is prohibited. This is done either under the covering or above it if no cloth is available.

Key Terms
العورة الغليظة (al-'awrah al-ghalizah): The genitals; the thicker private parts that are obligatory to cover.
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A hermaphrodite; a person with ambiguous gender.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or most reliable transmitted position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which view is considered the zahir al-riwaya (apparent of the transmission)?
A) Covering from navel to knee.
B) Covering only the genitals.
C) Covering the entire body.
D) Covering is not required.

Key Takeaway
Covering the deceased's 'awrah is wajib; the easier view permits covering only the genitals because desire is absent, and this is the apparent riwaya.

Wudu for the Deceased and the Dispute on Istinja
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istinja for the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether istinja is performed for the deceased and identify the practical difference between the two positions.

Core Idea
Istinja for the deceased is disputed between Abu Yusuf and the two; the muscle hold argument decides.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashia details the wudu of the deceased. While the base text (Maraqi al-Falah) simply states to perform wudu, the commentator highlights a disagreement among Hanafi authorities regarding whether istinja (washing the private parts) should be done first. The dispute turns on the physical condition of the deceased and the risk of causing new impurity. Understanding this ikhtilaf is important for correct funeral rites according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act under dispute
The act is istinja for the deceased before wudu. Is it required or not?
2
State the two positions
According to the two (likely Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), istinja is performed. According to Abu Yusuf, it is not.
The text says 'according to the two' and 'according to Abu Yusuf'.
3
Examine the proofs for each
The two argue that the area is impure and must be cleaned like in life. Abu Yusuf argues that the muscle hold is gone and washing may cause more impurity to emerge.
This is a dalil aqli (rational argument) based on the state of the deceased.
4
Note the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: some Hanafis will perform istinja, others will not.
The author of al-Khulasa followed Abu Yusuf's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وبعده وضيء) لم يذكر الاستنجاء، وذكره رضي الدين في المحيط، فقال أنه يستنجي عندهما لأن موضع الاستنجاء لا يخلو عن نجاسة، فلا بد من إزالتها اعتباراً بحال الحياة، وصورته أن يلف على يده خرقة فيغسل حتى يظهر الموضع لان مس العورة حرام، وعند أبي يوسف لا يستنجي، ومشى عليه صاحب الخلاصة لأن المسكة قد زالت، وبالاستنجاء ربما يزيد الاسترخاء فتخرج نجاسة أخرى فيكتفي بوصول الماء إليه اه من التبيين ملخصاً. قوله : ( يبدأ بوجهه) لأنه لم يباشر ذلك بنفسه، فلا يحتاج لغسل يديه، أوّلاً بخلاف الحي، ولا يؤخر غسل رجليه لأنه ليس في مستنقع الماء. قوله : (فلا يوضاً) لأنه لم يكن من أهل الصلاة قاله الحلواني، وهذا يقتضي أن من بلغ مجنوناً لا يوضاً أيضاً، ولم أره لهم وإنه لا
His saying: 'And after it, wudu' – he did not mention istinja, and Radi al-Din mentioned it in al-Muhit, saying that he performs istinja according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because the place of istinja is not free from impurity, so it must be removed in consideration of his life. The form is that he wraps a cloth on his hand and washes until the area becomes visible, because touching the private parts is forbidden. According to Abu Yusuf, he does not perform istinja, and the author of al-Khulasa followed him because the hold (of the muscles) has ceased, and with istinja, relaxation may increase and another impurity may emerge, so it is sufficient that water reaches it. Summarized from al-Tabyin. His saying: 'He begins with his face' because he did not perform that himself, so he does not need to wash his hands first, unlike the living. And he does not delay washing his feet because he is not in a puddle of water. His saying: 'He is not given wudu' because he was not among the people of prayer, said by al-Halwani. This implies that one who reaches puberty while insane is not given wudu either, but I have not seen that mentioned for them, and indeed not.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashia discusses the wudu of the deceased. The matn (Maraqi al-Falah) states that after covering and stripping, the deceased is given wudu. The commentator notes that the matn did not mention istinja (washing the private parts). Radi al-Din in al-Muhit said that according to the two sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), istinja is performed because the area is impure, analogous to life. The method is to wrap a cloth around the hand to avoid touching the private parts. However, Abu Yusuf alone said that istinja is not performed because the muscle hold has gone, and washing may cause more impurity to emerge. The commentator also clarifies that the wudu begins with the face without first washing the hands, unlike the living person's wudu, because the deceased did not perform any action. Also, wudu is not performed for a child who has not reached the age of prayer. The passage ends with a note that an insane person who reached puberty may also not require wudu, though this is not explicitly stated elsewhere.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): Washing the private parts to remove impurity; for the deceased, it is disputed whether to do it.
المسكة (al-musakkah): The muscle hold or tension; in the context of the deceased, the relaxation of muscles is considered a reason not to perform istinja.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Abu Yusuf argue against performing istinja for the deceased?
A) Because the dead do not need purification.
B) Because the muscle hold has ceased and washing may cause more impurity.
C) Because it is not mentioned in any hadith.
D) Because the deceased is not considered to have had private parts.

Key Takeaway
The question of istinja for the deceased is a genuine intra-Hanafi disagreement based on rational arguments about impurity and muscle relaxation.

Washing the Deceased: Covering Private Parts and Applying Perfume
Rulings on washing the deceased and covering private parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on covering the deceased's private parts, applying hanut and kafur, and identify the exception for cotton use in orifices.

Core Idea
Covering the deceased's private parts is wajib; hanut is recommended but saffron and wars are prohibited for men.

The washing of the deceased involves several important rulings beyond the ghusl itself. This lesson examines the requirements for covering the private parts, the use of perfumes and kafur, and the controversial issue of stuffing cotton into orifices. We'll also see how the bond of marriage affects who may perform the washing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon and its hukm level. For covering private parts, it is wajib. For using hanut, it is recommended except saffron/wars for men.
Washing the deceased itself is fard kifayah.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of angels washing Adam is the primary proof. It establishes the entire procedure including ghusl, kafur, and shrouding.
The hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut, but accepted as basis for sunnah.
3
Analyze the dispute on cotton use
The apparent narration prohibits cotton; al-Zayla'i permits it except in the anus and private part. The mufta bihi is the permissive view with those exceptions.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Note prohibitions and exceptions
Cutting nails and hair is prohibited. Woman may wash husband even during iddah because the marital bond remains partially.
Contrast with Shafi'i who allow cutting nails.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: with cotton allowed, the body is better preserved; without it, water reaches all parts directly.
Al-Tahtawi follows the permissive view as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستر ما لا ينبغي إظهاره، والذي تعذر مسه يصب عليه الماء، ويغسله أقرب الناس إليه، وإلا فأهل الأمانة والورع ينبغي إظهاره، ويكره أن يكون جنباً، أو بها حيض ويندب الغسل من تغسيله وتقدم (و) بعد تنشيفه يلبس القميص، ثم تبسط الأكفان ويجعل الحنوط) وهو عطر مركب من أشياء طيبة ولا بأس بسائر أنواعه غير الزعفران والورس للرجال (على رأسه ولحيته) وسائر جسده كما في الجوهرة بعد أن يوضع على الإزار كما في القهستاني قوله : (ويجعل الكافور على مساجده) سواء فيه المحرم، وغيره فيطيب ويغطى رأسه ليطرد الدود عنها، وهي الجبهة، وأنفه ويداه وركبتاه وقدماه روي ذلك عن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه فتخص بزيادة إكرام (وليس في الغسل استعمال القطن في الروايات الظاهرة وقال الزيلعي : لا بأس بأن يجعل القطن على وجهه وأن يحشى به مخارقه كالدبر والقبل والأذنين، والأنف والفم انتهى، وفي الظهيرية واستقبح عامة المشايخ جعله في دبره أو قبله ولا يقص ظفره) أي الميت (و) لا (شعره ولا يسرح شعره أي شعر رأسه ولحيته) لأنه للزينة وقد استغنى عنها (والمرأة تغسل زوجها ولو معتدة من رجعي أو ظهار منها في الأظهر أو إلى ما لا يحل مسه، والنظر إليه ببقاء العدة فلو ولدت عقب موته وانقضت عدتها من رجعي أو كانت مبانة، أو
And he covers what should not be shown, and what cannot be touched directly, water is poured over it, and the closest relative washes him, otherwise the trustworthy and pious people should show it, and it is disliked to be in a state of janabah or for her to have menstruation, and ghusl from washing him is recommended. And after drying him, he wears the shirt, then the shrouds are spread, and the hanut (compound perfume) is placed on his head and beard. And he places kafur on his prostration points, equally for the one in ihram and others, so he perfumes and covers his head to repel worms, and they are the forehead, nose, hands, knees, feet. And there is no use of cotton in the apparent narrations in ghusl, but al-Zayla'i said: there is no harm in placing cotton on his face and stuffing his openings like the anus, front private part, ears, nose, and mouth. And his nail is not cut, nor his hair, nor is his hair combed. And the woman washes her husband even if she is in an irrevocable divorce iddah or a zihar from her, or to what is not permissible to touch and look at due to remaining iddah.
Source pages p. 570

Commentary
This passage covers multiple rulings for washing the deceased. First, it is obligatory to cover the private parts of the deceased. If direct touch is difficult, water is poured. The closest relative should wash; if not, trustworthy people do it. It is disliked for the washer to be in major ritual impurity. The use of hanut (perfume) for men is allowed except saffron and wars (a yellow dye). Kafur is placed on the seven prostration points to delay decay. The text then discusses cotton use: the apparent narration prohibits it, but al-Zayla'i permits filling orifices except the anus and private part. Cutting nails or hair is prohibited unless broken. The woman may wash her husband even during iddah, as the marital bond remains partially.

Key Terms
حنوط (hanut): A compound perfume made from various pleasant substances, used on the deceased.
مساجد (masajid): The body parts that touch the ground during prostration: forehead, nose, hands, knees, feet.
إيلاء (eela'): An oath by a husband to abstain from sexual relations with his wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on using cotton to fill the orifices of the deceased?
A) It is obligatory to use cotton.
B) The apparent narration prohibits it, but some scholars allow it except in the anus and private part.
C) It is completely prohibited.
D) It is recommended only for the face.

Key Takeaway
Covering private parts is wajib; hanut and kafur are recommended; cotton use is permissible except for anus and genitals; woman may wash husband even in iddah.
